3.3 Data analysis 
This section will describe the ways that all the different data will be analyzed and the 
reason for each analysis. The different analysis serves different purposes, with the 
quantitative analysis expected to show the current situation and why a change is needed, the 
qualitative analysis is then expected to dive deeper into why the situation is as it is and help 
in identifying areas that can be improved.  
3.3.1.1 Veitur’s warehouse inventory database  
Veitur uses a program called Tableau in order to visualize the inventory data that they have. 
In that program, it is possible to set various filters such as the type of product, the time the 
product has been in the warehouse, which department owns the product, and more.  
==PAGE:41==
 
Methodology 
Master Thesis 
30 
 
The data in Tableau will be analyzed and filtered in a variety of ways to find out, what 
products are the most problematic when it comes to the tied-up capital in the warehouse. 
The researcher will present the results of this section in visual graphs and statistics that 
show the problem that is present concerning inventory management. 
The researcher will create a sample of the product group that ends up being the most 
problematic according to the data from Tableau, and he will perform a gemba walk, with a 
quality inspector from Veitur, which is a form of analysis in lean thinking where one goes 
to the worksite and sees the problem themselves to get a better understanding of the 
problem. More details on gemba and gemba walk can be seen in Appendix D. The goal of 
that will be to see how accurate the inventory management system is in regard to the 
number of products, to see what percentage of products are actually usable and have not 
deteriorated, and how the products are stored. That percentage from the sample can then be 
used to estimate the percentage of deteriorated products for the whole inventory of the 
product type in question. 
3.3.1.2 Greenhouse gas measures 
The greenhouse gas database will be used to calculate the greenhouse gas of the products 
that will be found to be the most problematic according to the warehouse inventory 
database in order to see how much greenhouse gas waste is related to those problematic 
products. The greenhouse gas database that Veitur uses is the one released by DEFRA, but 
since the database is from 2019, the researcher first updated the constants used in the 
calculations to change along with the inflation, which has been 1,21 from 2019 to April 
2023 (Bank of England, n.d.). This was done by dividing the constant from 2019 with the 
inflation which was 1,21. Next, the author updated the constants to work with the Icelandic 
krona with the conversion rate on April 18th which stated that 1 GBP was the equivalent of 
173,18 ISK. This was done by dividing the updated 2023 GBP constant with the conversion 
rate which was 173,18. The researcher will also further analyze the products that will be 
looked at as a part of the sample in the gemba walk. The researcher will analyze how much 
greenhouse gas has been unredeemably lost due to the products in question being 
deteriorated, lost, or outdated. The percentage of the greenhouse gas that is unredeemable 
lost can then be used to estimate the total amount of unredeemable lost greenhouse gas for 
the whole inventory of the product type in question.  
==PAGE:42==
 
Methodology 
Master Thesis 
31 
 
3.3.1.3 Interviews 
It was decided by the researcher to do a thematic analysis for the Interviews. Thematic 
analysis is performed in 6 phases, the first one being familiarizing with the data collected, 
followed by, coding that data, next themes are identified from the codes, followed by a 
review of the themes identified, these themes were then lastly given relevant names, and 
lastly produced in the report (Braun & Clarke, 2006). 
In phase 1, the researcher familiarized himself with the data acquired from the interviews 
and transcribed them in order to review the data more closely. In phase 2, initial codes were 
formed and highlighted in colors depending on the code in the transcriptions. In phase 3, 
the initial themes were formed before the interview took place since the analysis is 
deductive, and the initial themes were used when conducting the interviews. In phase 4, the 
identified themes were reviewed after the interviews had been conducted, and based on the 
answers from the interviewees, new themes were identified. This process was done twice 
after the interviews. In phase 5, the themes were given reflecting names. In phase 6, the 
themes that were eventually chosen were current process, systems, improvement, and 
warehouse and inventory. The codes and themes can be seen in Appendix E along with how 
they evolved. The interviews were conducted with a deductive approach since the aim of 
the research is to see if an existing theory, that lean thinking could improve the 
warehousing/purchasing processes and inventory management at Veitur, gets rejected or 
approved in this case. The researcher decided on a deductive approach after reading that it 
was a top-down approach for identifying the themes, that is investigating whether certain 
assumptions are true or not (Braun & Clarke, 2006).   
The interviews are expected to show the need for a change in the same way as the analysis 
of the warehouse inventory database, that is the inventory has gotten too large and costly. 
The interviews are expected to give a deeper understanding of the current processes and 
help in the identification of which areas in the process have the biggest effect on the current 
problems and investigate what could be improved in those areas.  
3.4 Reliability and validation 
The research needs to be as reliable and valid as possible, so the researcher has followed 
how LeCompte and Goetz (1982) have defined reliability and validation, that is both 
==PAGE:43==
 
Methodology 
Master Thesis 
32 
 
internal validation and reliability and external validation and reliability. This section will 
discuss what that is and how it was implemented. 
Reliability refers to how easily research can be replicated and come to the same conclusion. 
External reliability refers to the degree to which the research can be replicated, this is 
difficult to determine since it is impossible to freeze the social settings and circumstances 
that were present in this research. Internal reliability refers to the question of whether other 
researchers would come to the same conclusion with the same data as the researcher of this 
paper (LeCompte & Goetz, 1982). 
Regarding external reliability, 5 things should be taken into consideration, the position of 
the researcher, informant selection, social settings and circumstances, analytical constructs, 
and data collecting and analysis methods (LeCompte & Goetz, 1982). A description of 
these 5 variables in this research will now be presented: 
• Position of researcher: Information flow is dependent on the social role held within 
the studied group and appropriate knowledge is shared based on that (LeCompte & 
Goetz, 1982). It should be kept in mind that the researcher of this paper is doing a 
master thesis with a company that he has worked in for a few years and is familiar 
with the problem in question and the relevant individuals to talk to in order to gain 
knowledge. The researcher of this paper is also trusted for closed company 
documents which he deems to be helpful for this kind of research. 
• Informant selection: The choice was to interview those in the supply chain who 
have a direct effect on the inventory at the warehouse. If this research was to be 
replicated, it is important to identify which actors in the supply chain have a direct 
effect on the inventory since it could be different from the ones in this research. 
• Social settings and circumstances: It is important to remember that what an 
interviewee feels is appropriate to reveal in one circumstance might be 
inappropriate in other circumstances (LeCompte & Goetz, 1982). All the interviews 
were conducted face to face after getting to know the interviewee, and some of 
them the researcher knew before. The interviews were all conducted in a meeting 
room at the workplace of the interviewee at a time that the interviewee chose. 
These factors were set to make sure that the interviewee gets to know the 
==PAGE:44==
 
Methodology 
Master Thesis 
33 
 
researcher and the aim of the research, as well as doing the interview in a familiar 
location at a time when they were not in a hurry.  
• Analytical constructs: Even if everything above is the same, replication might be 
difficult if constructs, definitions, and units of analysis are personal or described 
poorly (LeCompte & Goetz, 1982). The researcher does his best to explain all the 
relevant information and do it in a standard manner so that it can be understood and 
replicated. 
• Data collecting and analysis methods: Researchers should ideally present their 
methods in a clear manner that allows others to use the original report as a guide 
(LeCompte & Goetz, 1982). The researcher of this paper aims to document his 
methods and how they were completed as well as possible for others to replicate. 
Regarding internal reliability, the researcher of this paper concluded by working on the 
paper alone. Other researchers might come to different conclusions, which might even be 
more optimal than the one in this research. There is not only one correct answer in a 
research paper. This research was conducted in 2023 and sometime in the future, there 
might be some technology or methods that do not exist today that might allow the 
conclusion of the research to be concluded in a completely different way. 
Internal validity refers to the relationship between the observations that the researcher sees 
and the theoretical ideas they develop, that is, is the researcher actually observing what he 
thinks he is observing? External validity refers to whether the findings of the research can 
be generalized or applied in different social settings or industries (LeCompte & Goetz, 
1982). 
When thinking about internal validity, the research aims to analyze and improve the 
warehousing/purchasing processes and inventory management for Veitur. After researching 
the inventory database and seeing that there are a lot of goods that just sit there for a long 
time, the researcher deemed it important to interview all the actors that contribute to the 
goods ending up in the warehouse to understand better why that happens and what can be 
done better. 
When thinking about the external validity, if someone wants to replicate the research, it is 
important to be mindful that no two companies are exactly the same. The findings of this 
research might be applied to other warehouses, but one needs to be mindful of the 
==PAGE:45==
 
Methodology 
Master Thesis 
34 
 
complexity that is involved in this research, that is Veitur being a subsidiary of the 
company Reykjavík energy, that manages all purchases on behalf of Veitur, and that they 
outsource the design of the bill of materials and the warehouse management. That does not 
mean that it cannot be replicated, it just means that a researcher should be mindful of 
variables that can be different from company to company when replicating the research.  
3.5 Ethical considerations  
(Diener & Crandall, 1978) mention four ethical principles to have in mind when conducting 
research that have been interpreted by the book Bryman’s social research methods (2021). 
Those principles are the following: 
1. Avoidance of harm to participants: This principle is split into two categories, 
avoidance of harm for participants and avoidance of harm for researcher. 
a. Harm can be classified as physical harm, harm to participants professional 
development, loss of self-esteem and stress. A good way to avoid harm to 
participants is to maintain confidentiality and keep all records secure, both 
private company documents and interview recordings. It can also be helpful 
to keep all participants anonymous (Bryman, Sloan, Foster, & Clark, 2021). 
This was done by being careful not to add too much from private company 
documents to the research before asking for managers' permission if that 
would be allowed. Regarding the interviews in the research, the recordings 
of the interviews will be deleted as soon as the research has been completed 
since they will no longer serve any purpose.  
b. Avoidance of harm to the researcher can refer to any physical or emotional 
harm that the researcher might encounter (Bryman, Sloan, Foster, & Clark, 
2021). Since the researcher works at the case company, researching a 
sensitive topic could be hurtful for the researcher’s job. But the topic in 
question is not at all sensitive and he made sure to explain to all 
interviewees what the research is and that he is not looking to put the blame 
of the problem on some division within the organization, but to try to 
understand why the problem is present and how it can be minimized. When 
going to the warehouse, the researcher followed the warehouse's rules and 
made sure to wear appropriate visibility clothing and protection gear as well 
==PAGE:46==
 
Methodology 
Master Thesis 
35 
 
as being aware of his surroundings to minimize the odds of landing in an 
accident. 
2. Informed consent: This principle refers to the research participants being given as 
much information about the research as possible before deciding to participate or 
not (Bryman, Sloan, Foster, & Clark, 2021). When asking managers at the 
organization for access to data, the researcher made sure to explain what the 
research is what the data would be used for, and why it would benefit the research. 
When conducting the interviews, the researcher began the interview with an 
introduction and explained the purpose of the research and if it would be all right to 
record the interview. Every participant was also informed that if he/she/they wanted 
to be withdrawn from the research at any time, that would be possible. 
3. Privacy: The third principle refers to protecting the privacy of all participants 
(Bryman, Sloan, Foster, & Clark, 2021). All conversations that were had with 
individuals regarding the research will not be referenced by name, but rather by job 
title if they are okay with sharing that information. Regarding the interviews, 
interviewees will not be named, and names that they mention in the interviews will 
be switched out for the job title of the individual in question. Interviewees were all 
asked if they were okay with sharing their current job title or if they would like to 
skip that since that would make them easily identifiable in some cases. The 
interviewees will be addressed by their number shown in Table 3.1. 
4. No deception: The last principle relates to researchers presenting their research as 
something other than what it is (Bryman, Sloan, Foster, & Clark, 2021). The 
researcher made sure, to be honest in all his communications with individuals taking 
part in the research and be prepared to answer questions regarding the purpose and 
possible outcomes of the research. 
 
 
==PAGE:47==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
36 
 
4 Findings and analysis 
In this chapter, the researcher will present the findings of the research that has been 
conducted. It is important to understand what the problem actually is, therefore the first 2 
steps of the findings will be analyzing the inventory database and calculating the carbon 
footprint related to the products in the inventory. That was done in order to see clearly the 
problem that has been growing over the last few years. First, the researcher will discuss the 
findings of the analysis of the inventory database that Veitur has access to and the gemba 
walk that took place at the warehouse, where items were checked if they matched in 
quantity to the database and if the condition of the items were up to par. Next the results of 
the carbon footprint analysis related to the special products older than 2 years will be 
looked at, and it will be seen how much carbon footprint has been wasted due to items that 
cannot be found or items that have deteriorated and cannot be used. Lastly, the researcher 
will analyze and present the results of the interviews in order to get a better understanding 
of the process, identify areas that could be improved, and gain an understanding of the 
knowledge of lean thinking that the interviewees possess.  
4.1 Veitur’s warehouse inventory database analysis 
To get a better understanding of the products and what types of products make up most of 
the growing inventory, the researcher analyzed the internal product database that Veitur has 
access to. The aim here is to highlight the problem that is present, identify which products 
contribute the most to the problem, and showcase the corresponding cost. 
The products that Veitur uses are categorized into 3 different categories, that is: 
• Routine products: These are products that are regularly used and can be used in 
most projects, these products are ordered based on the seasonal usage of the 
previous years. 
• Spare parts: These products represent a small part of the inventory and are kept to 
be able to quickly fix machinery and other equipment that can break. 
• Special products: These are products that are specially ordered for projects, these 
products are ordered by the bill of material for a project since these are not 
commonly used items or expensive items that are purchased only when needed. 
==PAGE:48==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
37 
 
These can be custom-made items that fit the specific conditions in a certain project 
and might be unlikely to be possible to use in a different scenario. 
I order to analyze the inventory that is currently in the warehouse, the researcher got access 
to the company’s inventory database in Tableau. This was done to see the problem with the 
growing inventory and how it has gradually grown over the last few years and is not 
showing signs of slowing down. The first thing to do was to analyze the tied-up capital in 
the warehouse by the type of product in order to see if any types of products are responsible 
for most of the tied-up capital at the warehouse. Figure 4.1 shows the tied-up cost of the 
products in the warehouse from 2017 to April of 2023. The tied-up capital had remained 
quite stable for a few years but has increased from 889 million ISK (£5,133 million) to 
1.433 million ISK (£8,275 million) from April 2021 to April 2023 which is an increase of 
544 million ISK (£3,141 million) or 61,12% increase in tied up value in the warehouse 
which is alarming. Currently, the inventory status at the warehouse is the following:  
• Total inventory: 1.433 million ISK (£8,275 million) 
• Special products: 942 million ISK (£5,439 million) 
• Routine products: 481 million ISK (£2,777 million) 
• Spare parts: 10 million ISK (£57.744) 
The researcher decided to apply filters that only show products that have been in the 
warehouse for more than 2 years. The reason for choosing that filter is that products that 
have been in the warehouse for a shorter period may be there for a reason such as 
seasonality since the harsh weather in Iceland makes it so that most of the projects take 
place over the warmer months. Products that have been in storage at the warehouse for 
more than 2 years have no excuse for being there for such a long time and Figure 4.2 shows 
the tied-up capital in the warehouse for products older than 2 years. When analyzing the 
data for products older than 2 years, some concerning factors are uncovered. The first one 
Figure 4.1: Total inventory (Veitur, tableau.or.is) 
==PAGE:49==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
38 
 
is that the inventory levels remained quite stable for a few years, but when looking at the 
same time period as previously, it can be seen that the total inventory of products in storage 
that are older than 2 years increased from 106 million ISK (£612.000) in April 2021 to 274 
million ISK (£1,582 million) in April 2023. That is an increase of 168 million ISK 
(£970.000) or 158,5% over just 2 years. The second alarming part is that the bulk of the 
products that are older than 2 years are special products. The total inventory of special 
products older than 2 years has grown from 90 million ISK (£520.000) in April 2021 to 247 
million ISK (£1,426 million) in April 2023, which is an increase of 174,4%. Having special 
products as the largest contributor to the products older than 2 years is not good since these 
are products that are unlikely to be able to be used in just any project since these are often 
products that cannot be used in all situations, hence why they were specially ordered. 
Currently, the inventory status at the warehouse for products older than 2 years is the 
following: 
• Total inventory: 274 million ISK (£1,582 million) 
• Special products: 247 million ISK (£1,426 million) 
• Routine products: 20 million ISK (£115.500) 
• Spare parts: 7 million ISK (£40.500) 
As can be seen here, special products are by far most of the products older than 2 years that 
are stored in the warehouse. When analyzing the inventory even further for the period 
between April 2021 and April 2023 by taking the value for each product type and plotting 
the values in Excel, the following graph was created and studied. Figure 4.3 shows that 
Figure 4.2: Inventory older than 2 years (Veitur, tableau.or.is) 
==PAGE:50==

special products accounted for between 85% and 91% of all the products in the warehouse 
that are older than 2 years, so that are the products that should be targeted in order to reduce 
the inventory levels.

Figure 4.4 shows how the inventory of products older than 2 years has risen from 106 
million ISK (£612.000) in April 2021 to 274 million ISK (£1,582 million) in April 2023 
and how special products are by far the main contributor to that growth.

• Blue: The products marked blue are products that connect to the pipes used for 
water distribution. First, there are 2 types of valves that are connected to the end of 
pipes to open, close, and control the flow of water. Then there are 2 types of 
flanges, which are used to connect 2 pipes or a pipe to another equipment like a 
valve. Next, there is a band joint/casing joint which is a protective cylinder that can 
be placed around a pipe for extra protection. Next, there is a steel elbow and a steel 
reduction. The steel elbow is in this case a 90-degree angle to change the direction 
of the pipes connected and the steel reduction is a tool to connect pipes with a 
different diameter. Lastly, there are PEX connection fittings, which are plastic 
cylinders that are used to connect pipes. 
• Green: The products marked green are different types of pipes. The first two pipes 
are both 80 cm in diameter but one of the pipes is 6,89m while the other is 6,95m. 
The remaining pipes are all the same type but with different diameters. All the pipes 
have 2 DN numbers related to them, the first number represents the diameter of the 
pipe in millimeters while the second number represents the diameter of the pipe plus 
the insulation material. You may notice that there are 2 types of pipes with the same 
dimensions, but another metric is added at the end, that metric represents the 
material thickness in these 2 pipes. 
The tied-up capital for each product as well as the documented quantity was obtained from 
the Tableau database that Veitur uses. On the gemba walk, the researcher went to the 
warehouse and the surrounding area with the warehouse manager, and he showed the 
researcher the products in question and it was counted. The column called “material found” 
represents the results of the counts for all the products in the sample and it was noted how 
many pieces were not found or found in a deteriorated condition. The capital lost was then 
calculated by dividing the tied-up capital of the product in question by the documented 
quantity to find the tied-up capital related to one piece. Then it was multiplied by the 
number of pieces not accounted for. The formula can be seen here below: 
𝐶𝑎𝑝𝑖𝑡𝑎𝑙 𝑙𝑜𝑠𝑡= (
𝑇𝑖𝑒𝑑 𝑢𝑝 𝑐𝑎𝑝𝑖𝑡𝑎𝑙
𝐷𝑜𝑐𝑢𝑚𝑒𝑛𝑡𝑒𝑑 𝑞𝑢𝑎𝑛𝑡𝑖𝑡𝑦) ∗𝑀𝑎𝑡𝑒𝑟𝑖𝑎𝑙 𝑛𝑜𝑡 𝑓𝑜𝑢𝑛𝑑 
It can be seen that the total tied-up capital for the sample is £680.135 while the total capital 
lost due to not being found or deteriorated is £75.389 with that number increasing to 
==PAGE:53==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
42 
 
£83.021 when including products that are not used anymore. That means that from the 
sample, 12,21% of the total tied-up capital is lost.  
83.021£
680.135£ ∗100 = 12,21% 
Using the results from the sample, the researcher estimates the total tied-up capital lost for 
all the special products that are older than 2 years since that was the product that made up 
the sample. The total tied-up capital for special products older than 2 years is £1,426 
million and from the previous result, it can be estimated that 12,21% of that capital has 
been lost due to the products not being found, having deteriorated, or not being used 
anymore.  
1.426.000£ ∗0,1221 = 174.115£ 
That means that the total tied-up capital lost for special products older than 2 years old is 
£174.115 (30,15 million ISK) which is alarming and is likely to increase if the remaining 
products continue to stay in the inventory and not be used in projects. 
One might argue that the inventory has grown due to more money being spent on materials 
over the years, but the spending on materials has grown with the total spending over the 
years (Specialist at the financial department at Veitur, personal communication, May 3, 
2023), this can be seen in Appendix G. Which argues that an increase in spending on 
products is not the source of the problem. 
This subchapter summed up the inventory and found out that products older than 2 years 
that Veitur has in the warehouse, and the tied-up capital related to the inventory has risen at 
an alarming rate recently with the main contributor being special products. Another thing is 
that there seem to be a lot of special products that will never be used due to not being 
found, having deteriorated, or being outdated that take up space in the storage area. If this 
growth were to continue, Veitur would likely need to get access to a larger warehouse and 
if the percentage of capital lost remains constant, it would mean that even more capital 
would be lost as the inventory would grow larger. 
4.2 Greenhouse gas analysis 
Financial waste is not the only waste related to bad inventory management. Another waste 
is, for example, the waste in the form of greenhouse gases related to the production of 
==PAGE:54==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
43 
 
products that are ordered. The purpose here is to analyze the same sample as in the previous 
section and calculate the amount of greenhouse gas that has been unredeemable lost due to 
products not being found, having deteriorated, or being outdated.  
The researcher worked with the specialist in climate and environmental issues at Reykjavík 
Energy to assign all the special products older than 2 years that Veitur has in the warehouse 
according to the product type in order to calculate the total greenhouse gas emissions and 
the total emissions were calculated to be 1.396.069,78 kg of CO2e. The list of products that 
were categorized is over 700 products, and will therefore not be included in the appendix, 
as they will not be looked into any further, this was just to showcase the total amount of 
greenhouse gases that is tied to the inventory. 
The greenhouse gas standards from DEFRA that were used in the research have 110 
different greenhouse gas constants that are used to calculate different materials. Together 
with the specialist in climate and environmental issues, we placed all the products that 
Veitur has in the warehouse into 6 categories, the categories, and their given constants can 
be seen in Figure 4.6. 
 
Figure 4.6: DEFRA categories used 
The researcher then looked at the same sample as before and added the product category 
from DEFRA and the constants related to that product category. This can be seen in Figure 
4.7. The GHG category represents the category of the specific product that is based on the 
standards from DEFRA and the column GHG constant is the kilogram of greenhouse gas 
that is emitted for every Icelandic krona spent in that category, and total GHG represents 
the total greenhouse gas related to the product and is calculated by multiplying tied-up 
capital by the GHG constant for every product.

Figure 4.7: Sample of special products older than 2 years for GHG analysis 
The column called GHG lost is the greenhouse gas that is tied to products that were not 
found or have deteriorated. That is a greenhouse gas that is unredeemable lost since it has 
already been emitted when the product was made, but the product cannot be used. The 
column GHG lost was calculated by dividing the tied-up capital of the product in question 
by the documented quantity to find the tied-up capital related to one piece. Then it was 
multiplied by the number of pieces not accounted for and lastly multiplied by the GHG 
constant in question. The formula can be seen here below: 
𝐺𝐻𝐺 𝑙𝑜𝑠𝑡= (
𝑇𝑖𝑒𝑑 𝑢𝑝 𝑐𝑎𝑝𝑖𝑡𝑎𝑙
𝐷𝑜𝑐𝑢𝑚𝑒𝑛𝑡𝑒𝑑 𝑞𝑢𝑎𝑛𝑡𝑖𝑡𝑦) ∗𝑀𝑎𝑡𝑒𝑟𝑖𝑎𝑙 𝑛𝑜𝑡 𝑓𝑜𝑢𝑛𝑑∗𝐺𝐻𝐺 𝑐𝑜𝑛𝑠𝑡𝑎𝑛𝑡 
It can be seen that the total GHG lost is 100.554,29 kg CO2e for the sample and increases to 
104.226,29 kg CO2e when taking into account products that were found but are outdated. 
With the total GHG related to the products in the sample being 748.208,16kg CO2e, the 
percentage of greenhouse gas unredeemable lost is calculated to be 13,93%. 
104.226,29 𝑘𝑔 𝐶𝑂2e
748.208,16 𝑘𝑔 𝐶𝑂2𝑒∗100 = 13,93%

It is alarming that it is estimated that 193.155,69 kg CO2e has been released in the

something that both Veitur and Reykjavík Energy want to reduce (Reykjavík Energy, 
Sustainable development goals, n.d.) (Reykjavík Energy, E1 Greenhouse gas emissions, 
n.d.). 
This subchapter showed that it is not only financial waste that is associated with the current 
inventory that Veitur has, but there is also an environmental cost associated with the 
products. The greenhouse gas that has been released by the production of products that will 
not be used goes against both Veitur’s and Reykjavík Energy's sustainability goals. 
4.3 Interviews analysis 
Now that the problems with the current inventory and purchasing processes have been 
highlighted in the previous subchapters, it was deemed important to analyze why things are 
the way they are. The researcher interviewed individuals at various stages of the process 
that influence the products that get purchased and eventually get used or end up in the 
warehouse. The purpose of the interviews was to get an insight into the current processes 
that are followed that lead to a product ending up in the warehouse, identify areas that 
could be improved, and eventually come up with suggestions for process improvements 
that would eliminate waste. Transcriptions of all the interviews can be seen in Appendix C. 
4.3.1 Current processes 
In this subchapter, the interviews will be analyzed in order to map the current process that 
takes place in order to see the process visibly and to be able to see what areas could benefit 
the most from improving. In this subchapter, the interviews will be analyzed by the order of 
processes that take place in the real world. That is, first the external consultants, then the 
internal designers, after that the project managers, then the purchasing department, and 
lastly the warehouse supervisor. Since the warehousing/purchasing process was defined as 
the point in the process when the creation of the bill of material starts until the item leaves 
the warehouse, that will be the area that will be focused on.  
==PAGE:57==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
46 
 
4.3.1.1 External consultants 
When the external consultants were asked to go step by step through the processes involved 
in their work, they answered the following: 
Interviewee 7 mentioned that first, he starts preparing drawings and a tendering document, 
if the product goes to tender, which includes the volume of material needed for the project, 
and a project description. He then sends these documents to Veitur for review and starts 
creating the bill of material based on the feedback from Veitur. He mentioned that he bases 
the bills of materials on the product catalog from Veitur. He then sends the bill of material 
to Veitur, and they input the bill of material into the ordering system. Interviewee 8 agrees 
and adds that after he sends the bill of material to Veitur, it is reviewed and if there is 
something that needs to be changed, he goes over the bill of material again. To stay within 
the scope of the defined warehousing/purchasing processes, the focus will be placed on the 
point where the creation of the bills of material starts. 
4.3.1.2 Internal designer 
When the internal designers were asked to describe their job and go step by step through 
the processes involved in their work, they answered the following: 
Interviewee 5 mentioned that they do not design in-house, so she sometimes works on 
project assumptions with external consultants and sponsors. She mentioned that the internal 
designers follow the project during the design phase with external consultants, attend 
design meetings, review the design, and input the bills of material into DMM. Interviewee 
5 mentioned that the internal designers mainly review the documents from the external 
consultants, and make changes to the bills of materials if necessary, that is add or remove 
material. She mentioned that she reviews the bill of material and makes sure that it matches 
the drawings from the external consultants, then she enters the bill of material into DMM. 
She then mentioned that a project does not go out for tendering if necessary until the 
internal designers approve the tendering documents from the external consultants, and 
mentioned that the internal designers are involved in the designing process through design 
meetings before the review begins, meaning that all assumptions should be accurate, but 
there is always something that needs to be addressed during the review. 
==PAGE:58==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
47 
 
4.3.1.3 Project managers 
When interviewing the project managers, they were asked about their responsibilities and 
role, as well as the step-by-step process of ordering a product after receiving the bill of 
material, their answers were the following: 
Interviewee 3 mentioned that the role of the project managers is to make sure that after the 
design has been completed, the bills of material are entered into DMM and that the bill of 
material is being monitored at the right time and informing the purchasing department of 
when the material needs to be available. Interviewee 4 agrees and adds that project 
managers are responsible for getting external designers involved, negotiating with them, 
and getting them to create data for the project. She mentioned that the project managers 
manage the execution of the projects, that is oversee the projects from start to finish and 
hand it over with a final meeting. Interviewee 4 added to Interviewee 3 comment about bills 
of material being monitored, stating that the project managers are responsible for the dates 
on the bills of material are correct so that they keep being monitored.  
Interviewee 3 mentioned that the external consultants create the bill of material and that the 
internal designers review it and then enter it into DMM. The product managers then review 
the settings for the purchase request associated with the bill of material and set the status of 
the bill of material to being monitored. Interviewee 3 mentioned that it is important to make 
sure that the dates request is accurate and that 90 days before the project start date in the 
request is the time when the bill of material gets monitored automatically by the purchasing 
department if no one does it sooner. He then mentioned that the purchasing department 
handles ordering the material and getting it delivered to the warehouse. Interviewee 4 
mentioned that the whole process happens in DMM, but if the project managers do not have 
a product number, then they need to send a purchase request through email. 
4.3.1.4 Purchasing department 
When interviewing the people in the purchasing department it was important to get a better 
understanding of what each of their responsibilities were. They were first asked to describe 
their jobs and their roles in the purchasing process, and their answers were the following: 
Interviewee 1 mentioned that he oversees distributing projects to relevant individuals and 
added that he receives inquiries from Veitur. Interviewee 1 then added that he monitors the 
bills of material for all projects and prioritizes what is needed as soon as possible by the 
==PAGE:59==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
48 
 
status of the projects. Interviewee 2 mentioned that he makes sure that the entire purchasing 
department is doing what they are supposed to do, that is to service their customers. He 
mentioned the main tasks such as inventory management and making sure that the 
inventory is not too big. He added that he handles communication with suppliers, regarding 
delivery times and invoices. Lastly, he added that if people encounter any difficulties with 
certain aspects, then he can assist them. Interviewee 6 mentioned that she has a similar job 
as Interviewee 1, but that she handles Reykjavík Energy, ON Power, and CarbFix, while 
Interviewee 1 handles Veitur and Reykjavík Fibre. She added that their projects intersect 
and they assist each other but they primarily focus on their respective companies. She 
mentioned that she is mostly involved in tenders, contracts, and consulting, but that she also 
oversees procurement analysis where she reviews all the purchase activities once a year. 
These individuals in the purchasing department were also asked to describe their step-by-
step processes in ordering a product after they had received an ordering request. The focus 
here will be on the orders of special products since from the database analysis, they are the 
main contributor to the growing inventory. Their answers were the following:  
Interviewee 2 mentioned that there are 2 ways in which they receive purchase requests, that 
is either through email or through bills of material that is processed through DMM. He 
added that they also monitor the routine products themselves which Interviewee 6 also 
mentioned and added that it is based on usage in previous years. He mentioned that the 
email requests that they receive include a PDF document or just a text that says, “please 
order the following product from the following supplier”. Then he mentioned that they need 
to see if the product number exists, or create a product number and place an order with the 
supplier. He then mentioned that if it comes through a bill of material, it gets electronically 
transferred from the product managers into our accounting system(Unit4), and then a 
purchase suggestion gets generated in AGR, which is automatically sent back to Unit4 
which generates a purchase order. He mentioned that he prefers getting requests through 
bills of material since there is no manual input required for the product numbers until the 
supplier gets a PDF document, the suppliers have to enter the product numbers and the 
quantity into their system, which can result in errors. Interviewee 6 agreed on how requests 
that come through bills of material are processed and added that once they get a notification 
that the product has arrived, they inform the person who placed the order. Interviewee 6 
==PAGE:60==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
49 
 
then added that they do not track if the person who placed the order retrieves it from the 
warehouse, stating that if it is not collected, it just remains in the warehouse.  
Interviewee 1 mentioned that usually when a purchase request arrives through email, there 
is usually an offer attached, but that they are sometimes asked to look for prices. Then they 
find prices and send them to the person who sent the purchase request for approval. He then 
mentioned that if there is an offer attached to the purchase request, and order is written with 
Unit4 and sent to the supplier. He mentioned that the supplier is asked to send a 
confirmation of the order and an estimated delivery time, he then stated that they do not 
always receive these confirmations. When the product arrives, the project manager contacts 
the person who requested the product and gets a confirmation of where the product should 
be delivered. He then mentioned that when they get a confirmation that the product has 
arrived, they register it as received and sell it to the project that it is registered to. 
Interviewee 6 agrees on how requests that arrive through email are handled.   
4.3.1.5 Warehouse manager 
Lastly, the warehouse manager at Eimskip was asked what his role is in connection to 
Veitur and to go step-by-step into the processes that a product goes through at the 
warehouse. His answers were the following: 
Interviewee 9 mentioned that he handles communication between the suppliers, Eimskip, 
and the companies that they serve, stating that he is the contact person for Reykjavík 
Energy or Veitur. He then mentioned that he makes sure that every product arrives 
correctly and departs correctly, at the correct time. He mentioned that he makes sure that 
the order receipt is documented and that the arrival time and the contents that arrived get 
uploaded to a shared drive that is shared with Reykjavík Energy. He then makes sure that 
the products are counted and inspected because they only accept products in sellable 
condition. He then makes sure that the products are booked into their system and notifies 
Reykjavík Energy if there are any discrepancies or damages in the order. He then 
mentioned then mentioned that they either prepare the product for picking if it will be 
picked up right away, or that they place a pallet tag on every item to easily find them later, 
and find a storage place for them. He then mentioned that when the time comes to prepare 
the products for departure, they type it out of their system and prepare delivery documents. 
Then the product is either picked up or shipped out.  
==PAGE:61==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
50

4.3.2 Systems in use 
It can be quite confusing to understand the different systems in use, and it is important to 
get an understanding of who uses what system, and for what purpose. This subchapter will 
therefore be dedicated to explaining the different systems that the interviewees use and how 
that affects the current operations. 
4.3.2.1 Warehouse manager 
Interviewee 9 talked about how they at the warehouse use a system called MLS to manage 
their inventory. He mentioned that when they receive a product, they scan a barcode or 
input the product number to the system, they then assign it to a storage space that is marked 
with a sticker and can look up a product in MLS to see its location. He then mentioned that 
Reykjavík Energy does not have access to this system, but their system, Unit4 retrieves its 
data straight from MLS within minutes of changes and has done so for the last 5 years. 
4.3.2.2 Purchasing department 
Interviewee 2 stated that they mainly use 2 systems, that is Unit4 and AGR, Unit4 for 
procurement, and AGR for inventory management. He mentioned that all the data comes in 
through Unit4 which retrieves its data from the system used in the warehouse and then 
shares the data with the other systems in use. Interviewees 1 and 6 agreed and Interviewee 
1 talked about how AGR takes in previous years sales history of routine products in order 
to make a purchase suggestion and is the product catalog that Reykjavík Energy uses. 
Interviewee 2 mentioned that the warehouse handles tracking the inventory in their system 
and that data gets transferred to Unit4, he then mentioned that if there are any discrepancies 
between the systems, they ask the warehouse manager to investigate it. Interviewee 1 then 
mentioned that some departments use a system called DMM, which also gets its data from 
Unit4, and mentioned that Veitur creates their purchase orders there which gets sent back to 
Unit4. Interviewee 2 then mentioned that they use a system called Tableau to visualize their 
data, Tableau also gets its data from Unit4. Interviewee 1 said that the updating time for 
Unit4 and DMM is about 10 minutes, but that AGR gets updated twice a day, meaning that 
when he is working, he sees the status as it was at 6:00 that morning. 
4.3.2.3 Project managers 
Interviewee 3 mentioned that the project managers use a system called DMM for managing 
all their material orders in their projects, stating that they input the bills of materials there, 
==PAGE:64==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
53 
 
he then mentioned that DMM communicates with the systems that the purchasing 
department uses. Interviewee 4 mentioned that the purchasing department manages 
inventory management but that the project managers can see what products are available in 
DMM. Interviewee 4 then mentions that she suspects that there might be some information 
that the purchasing department can see in AGR that they cannot see in DMM. Interviewee 4 
then mentioned that DMM was not designed for the purpose that Veitur is using it for, 
meaning that purchase requests are only a small section of what is available in the system. 
4.3.2.4 Internal designer and external consultants 
Interviewee 5 mentioned that she sends the external consultants an Excel file of the product 
catalog received from DMM, which is not the same product catalog that the purchasing 
department uses. She then mentions that she inputs the bill of material into DMM after it 
has been completed by the external designers. 
Interviewee 8 mentioned that the external consultants do not have access to the product 
catalog, that is in AGR or DMM, confirming that they only get sent a copy of the product 
catalog from DMM if they request it. He then mentioned that the version that he has might 
get outdated if he does not get a new copy regularly, making it difficult to be sure that is 
always accurate.  
4.3.2.5 Summary 
Figure 4.9 then shows a visual representation of how the different systems act with each 
other.

4.3.3 Areas of improvement 
Throughout the interviews, interviewees were asked what their main challenges are, how 
they feel about current processes, what could be done better, and if there is anything that 
they do not like. They were also asked their opinions about the communications, 
transparency, and systems that are used, and what could be improved. They were then 
asked about the waste in the process, the possible causes, and the repercussions that can 
follow. This subchapter highlights the questions that were asked when the interviewees 
mentioned areas in the process that are not performed effectively and can result negatively 
in the total process. The answers from individuals will be grouped by their jobs since it is 
expected to show clearly which individuals identify which processes as problematic since 
no one is likely to point at themselves as the problem. It is worth noting that this subchapter 
is quite long and the most mentioned areas will be summarized at the end of this 
subchapter. 
4.3.3.1 External consultants 
When asked about the main challenges they face in their work, their answers were the 
following: 
They identified some challenges of their work as the point when the worksite gets dug up, 
since what they are designing is all underground, there can be some unexpected changes 
that pop up after excavating the ground. They mentioned that if there are any changes to the 
prerequisites, it is important that the new discoveries should be communicated to everyone 
involved. The bill of material is a component that should be updated if there are any 
changes in the project so that an older version of the bill of material does not get purchased, 
since it might include items that would not be useful anymore or not include items that are 
suddenly essential. Interviewee 7 identified that the product catalog would need a thorough 
review, he mentioned a fire hydrant as an example. Stating that if a fire hydrant were to be 
included on the bill of material, he would need to remember to also input all the necessary 
components that the fire hydrant needs. He mentioned that it is only possible to know all 
the components if one has experience with fire hydrants, so it would be difficult for 
someone who is not familiar with fire hydrants to precisely add all the correct additional 
components to the bill of material, and no one can be an expert in every single thing that is 
in the product catalog. He mentioned that it would be good to standardize the additional 
==PAGE:66==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
55 
 
components for larger items in the product catalog, like a fire hydrant so that when you add 
a fire hydrant to the bill of material, all the necessary components would be added as well 
under the name “1 fire hydrant”.  
When asked what in the processes could be done better, they said: 
Interviewee 7 showed me a recent bill of material that he created and mentioned that there 
were many small components that he would like to be included as a package with the larger 
items on the list if they are added to accompany that larger item as he said previously. He 
also mentioned that the product catalog is difficult to navigate and that the products do not 
have a standardized naming system. Interviewee 8 went in the direction of the reviewers at 
Veitur and mentioned that they are not always individuals who have experience working in 
the field with the items on the bill of material and as a result questioned if they have a good 
enough understanding of the items. He also mentioned that Veitur could stop acquiring 
material for the projects and leave that responsibility to the contractors that do the work. 
When asked if they always have the necessary information when creating the bills of 
material, they said: 
Interviewee 7 mentioned the product catalog again and reiterated that it needs to be 
improved and that the small necessary components should be bundled up with larger items 
to minimize the risk of wrong small components being placed on the bill of materials. 
Interviewee 8 mentioned that many variables can change after a final design is complete, 
which might make the design not as accurate as was desired. This could originate from 
workers insisting on certain methods or new discoveries after the worksite gets dug up. 
When asked their thoughts about the design having to be made with material constraints, 
that is only use material that would be standardized so that it would be easier to use in other 
projects if something went wrong, their answers were the following:  
Both interviewees claim to use standardized material where possible, with Interviewee 8 
mentioning that he likely uses more components than others in order to use mostly 
standardized material. He also mentioned that it could help Veitur utilize material that 
cannot be used in a project for whatever reason, in another project, since the material would 
be standardized. 
==PAGE:67==
 
Findings and analysis

56 
 
When asked how they rate the transparency between the external consultants and the people 
at Veitur, they said the following: 
Here, Interviewee 8 mentioned an issue with the transparency that they have. He mentioned 
that he has to request an Excel copy of the product catalog if he wants to have it, so it is not 
guaranteed that he has the latest version every time. He mentioned that the tendering 
documents are available online and wondered if the same could be done with the product 
catalog, that is had it available online so he could be sure that he is working with the latest 
version. 
When asked if it is common for them not to have sufficient data to design the bills of 
material, they said: 
Interviewee 7 mentioned the product catalog once again and said that it can be a challenge 
to find specific items in the product catalog. 
When asked if they have information about what items are available in stock when creating 
the bills of material so that they could be utilized. Their answers were the following: 
Interviewee 7 mentioned that he does not see what is currently available, but knows which 
items are regularly used, this would be the routine products. He also mentioned that there 
might be more than one product catalog, this may be due to the product catalog having 
changed in between the time when 2 individuals get the product catalog sent. Interviewee 8 
highlighted again that he might have an old version of the product catalog sent from Excel 
so he does not always know what is available and what material is preferred.  
When asked about how often the bills of material might be inaccurate and the reason why 
that could happen, they gave their responses as: 
Both interviewers are unsure how often the bills of materials are inaccurate but Interviewee 
8 mentioned that the contractors that use the material have lost material, making them need 
more for the project, and once again questioned if Veitur should transfer the responsibility 
of acquiring the material to the contractors. He also mentioned that material can get lost at 
the warehouse and said that Veitur used to have a better overview of their inventory when 
they managed their own storage area. As for why the bills of material might be incorrect, 
Interviewee 7 mentioned again that it can be due to all the small things that should 
accompany the larger items as some designers often do not work with the material in the 
==PAGE:68==

field. Interviewee 8 identified the cause as unexpected changes in the project where 
important information is not spread well enough. 
4.3.3.2 Internal designers 
When asked about the main challenges she faces in her work, her answers were the 
following: 
Here, Interviewee 5 mentioned that the product catalog can be difficult to understand and 
gave an example from her time as an external consultant that they only receive an Excel file 
of the catalog. She mentioned that an item can have 2 different names in the catalog 
depending on the size of the item. That makes it difficult to look for items in the product 
catalog efficiently since there is no standard naming system. 
When asked how they are constantly trying to improve the work processes, the answer was 
the following: 
Interviewee 5 mentioned that the internal designers want to have a better way of managing 
all the documents from the external consultants. She mentions a vague idea for a system 
where the external consultants would submit their documents for review and the internal 
designers would submit their review in the same system. That would allow them to easily 
see all the versions of the documents and not have it tied to a single individual's email. This 
could be incorporated to increase the transparency of the documents for the internal 
designers and external consultants. 
When asked if she finds it clever if the designs created by the external consultants should 
be made with constraints for using standardized material, she answered: 
Interviewee 5 mentioned she would prefer that there were standards for the materials and 
that the designs would be created using that standardized material. She said that if 
something were to happen which made some products not needed, it would be easier to fit 
them into different projects. 
When asked her opinion about the transparency between different individuals in the 
process, she answered: 
Interviewee 5 answered this from her time as an external consultant and mentioned that she 
thought that the product catalog was confusing, with a lot of random information. It can be 
==PAGE:69==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
58 
 
seen that this has not improved since the current external consultants are having similar 
problems. 
When asked if they have information about what items are available when creating the bills 
of material in order to potentially use those items, she answered the following: 
Interviewee 5 mentioned that she does not see what is available until after she submits the 
bill of material to DMM. Then she mentioned that if she looks up a specific item in DMM, 
she can see the quantity of that item that is in the warehouse, but not if those items are 
reserved for another project or not. Then she gave a long example, which can be seen in the 
transcription, about a problem that she had related to this. 
When asked about why bills of material might be incorrect and how they prevent that from 
happening, she answered: 
When asked why it happens, Interviewee 5 mentioned that when the construction ditch is 
opened, there might be something unexpected that forces them to use different items than 
originally thought. When asked how they can prevent it from happening, Interviewee 5 
mentioned that sometimes the external consultants put items on the bills of material that 
people do not want to use, or are just never used, since they do not always know if the 
current preferences or standards have changed. She will then need to replace the item with 
the appropriate item. She then questioned why the product catalog includes items that are 
not used anymore.  
4.3.3.3 Project managers 
When asked about their opinion of the current purchasing process, they answered the 
following: 
Interviewee 3 mentioned that there is room for improvement and questioned if Veitur 
should be sourcing the materials for the projects, which is something that Interviewee 8 
mentioned as well. Interviewee 4 had issues with the product catalog like some other 
interviewees, she mentioned that it would be beneficial if the products had a precise 
description about them in the product catalog.  
When asked about what in the current process could be done better, their answers were the 
following: 
==PAGE:70==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
59 
 
Interviewee 3 questioned again if it should be Veitur’s responsibility to source the materials 
for the projects and suggested transferring that responsibility to the contractors. He 
mentioned that if just one important item gets delayed, then the whole project can get 
delayed and Veitur takes the blame. Interviewee 4 mentioned that the current product 
catalog is not working as well as it should. She mentioned that it is difficult to find items in 
the catalog and suggested that it would be beneficial to see suggested items when choosing 
an item if one is needed to accompany the other, this is a similar suggestion that 
Interviewee 7 had about having item groups that go together. She also mentioned that the 
external consultants can create an incorrect bill of material due to not having good enough 
information about the items in the catalog. 
When asked if they thought that any steps in the process were unnecessary or time-
consuming, they said: 
Interviewee 3 talked about the product catalog being unorganized and gave an example of 
how difficult it can be to find something in it. Interviewee 4 agreed that the product catalog 
is confusing and questioned the roles of the purchasing department. 
When asked if they had any problems with inventory management that could be improved, 
they mentioned: 
Interviewee 3 once again questioned if Veitur should source the material and referenced a 
problem that the city might cancel a project that Veitur has already purchased products for, 
which then have to be stored. He mentioned that this can be one of the causes for the large 
inventory that Veitur has. Interviewee 4 mentioned that products sometimes arrive long 
before the project start date leaving them to need to be stored somewhere, and sometimes 
there simply is no available space. She mentioned a story from experience that can be seen 
in the transcripts, where she was asked to keep products at the worksite before she even had 
gotten a permit from the municipality to close off space for the worksite. That is something 
that the project managers do not want because, when they receive the material, they become 
responsible for it. She mentioned that it would be ideal if the product got delivered to the 
warehouse and then the contractors would pick them up when needed so that they would 
have the responsibility for the product.   
==PAGE:71==
 
Findings and analysis
