When asked if it is common for the bill of material from the external designers to be 
inaccurate, they had the following answers: 
They both agreed that bills of materials can be incorrect and Interviewee 4 mentioned that it 
could be because it had not been reviewed thoroughly or because the product catalog is not 
clear enough and includes outdated items.  
When asked about their thoughts on the transparency between different parties in the 
process and if they have had any problems with the transparency, they mentioned the 
following: 
Interviewee 3 mentions that the project managers do not see the product catalog in the same 
program as the project managers. He mentions that he only sees the amount of material 
available, but not if it is for his project or some other project. Interviewee 4 argues that 
there is not enough communication between departments. When asked about the problems 
they had, Interviewee 3 mentioned that the external consultant often does not know what to 
expect after a worksite gets dug up, so the correct items may be missing from the bills of 
material. He also mentioned that people can accidentally take items from the warehouse 
that have been assigned to another project since they do not see what project each item is 
assigned to. Interviewee 4 talked about how the warehouse sometimes does not deliver 
correct material to the contractors or even material that has gotten damaged while staying in 
the warehouse. 
When asked if they think that the database of available material is reliable, and what they 
think could be improved in that database, they said: 
Interviewees 3 and 4 both agree that the product catalog is not good, they mention that the 
catalog is unorganized, and it often uses nicknames or Icelandic translations instead of 
standardized names from the supplier. They mentioned that it would be good if it was 
possible to sort the products by supplier name and question why there are still product 
numbers for products that are no longer in use. Interviewee 3 mentioned that searching for 
an item in the database is difficult since you need to know exactly what the item is called in 
the database, he suggests utilizing leading categories for simplifying looking up items. He 
mentioned a sequence of categories as an example, that is if you are looking for a leather 
jacket in a store, you would choose “coats”, then “jackets”, and then select “leather jacket” 
==PAGE:72==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
61 
 
instead of “denim jacket”. Interviewee 4 mentioned that she would like to have more 
information about the products in the database. 
When asked if it should be standardized to check what is available in the database before 
placing an order, they said: 
They both agree that it would be beneficial, with Interviewee 4 saying that a good product 
catalog would be needed and the items would need to be properly listed for that to be 
possible. 
When asked about what they identify as the largest waste in the process, they said: 
Interviewee 3 identifies the fact that Veitur acquires materials for the projects as the biggest 
waste while Interviewee 4 identifies items being mishandled in the warehouse and not 
utilizing their inventory as the biggest waste. 
When asked what the most common reasons for products ending up at the warehouse and 
how often that happens, they had the following answers: 
Interviewee 3 mentioned the reason being that the external consultants do not always have 
accurate information, making the bills of materials incorrect, which leads to incorrect 
material being purchased. Interviewee 4 mentioned the reason is that customers sometimes 
cancel the project after items have been purchased, leading the items not to be used. They 
do not agree on how often it happens with one stating it happens often while the other 
saying it is not common.  
When asked why special products that have been in the warehouse for more than 2 years 
are not sold or disposed of, they said: 
Interviewee 3 criticizes the transparency as he states that he does not have an overview of 
how long a product has been in the warehouse, and Interviewee 4 finds it strange that there 
is no attempt to dispose of the items that have been in the warehouse for a long time. 
4.3.3.4 Purchasing department 
When asked what their challenges in the process were, they answered the following: 
Interviewee 1 mentioned that Veitur sometimes complains that products are delivered in a 
bad condition from the warehouse but argues that it can be due to products being returned 
==PAGE:73==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
62 
 
from a worksite to the warehouse where products get mishandled by the contractors instead. 
Interviewee 2 mentioned that his main challenge is the inventory levels that they have and 
mentioned that it can be due to the fact that there is not enough standardization in the 
products in use and that it would be beneficial to use more standardized products. 
Interviewee 3 mentioned that project managers sometimes forget to update the dates on the 
bills of material, which can lead to another project taking products that were originally 
ordered for the one who forgot to update the dates accordingly and cause delays in that 
project.  
When asked about what could be done better in the purchasing process, they said: 
Interviewee 1 mentioned that the systems in use could be more user-friendly and that they 
have issues related to items not being reduced from the bills of material after they make a 
purchase since currently it gets reduced once it leaves the warehouse and is registered for a 
project or if they register it manually to a project. He mentioned this being one of the 
causes for the growing inventory. Interviewees 2 and 6 mention the problems with ordering 
from email requests. The reason for those requests was mentioned being that the bill of 
material might still be worked on, but it would be good to place an order for a certain item 
early. This poses the problem of not being able to look up what project an item is tied to 
and who requested it.  
When asked if there are any steps in the process that they think are unnecessary or time-
consuming: they mentioned: 
Interviewee 1 mentioned the complications related to having many computer systems in use 
since some things can be seen in one system but not the other, which means that 
transparency is not optimal. Then he mentioned that training employees who move between 
departments is necessary, as he may not know all the processes in the new department. 
Interviewee 2 mentioned that the process of sending suppliers the ordering requests could 
be done more efficiently by having a straight connection between the ordering system and 
the suppliers. He then mentioned the problems related to emails with suppliers not being 
saved with the orders, hinting that it would be beneficial to be able to send emails through 
their ordering system that would then save the emails to that order. Interviewee 6 
mentioned that being more precise takes a longer time and she would like the project 
==PAGE:74==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
63 
 
managers to be more precise in making sure that they order the correct items, so they do not 
end up in the warehouse. 
When asked about the main bottlenecks in the process, they said the following: 
Both Interviewees 1 and 2 mentioned the lead time for items as the most time-consuming 
part of the process, stating that it can be up to a year. Interviewee 1 mentioned that they 
could schedule the projects better while Interviewee 2 just looked at this as a part of the 
process, but not as a bottleneck. 
When asked what they currently do in order to improve their work processes, they said: 
Interviewee 2 mentioned that he would like to eliminate purchase requests arriving through 
email. He would like to have a system so that when there is a reason for purchasing before 
the bill of material is completed for whatever reason, the project manager would need to fill 
out a standard request form that has all the necessary information needed in a field that 
would be mandatory to fill out. This would eliminate the process of chasing information 
after receiving a vague purchase request through email. Interviewee 6 mentioned that they 
sometimes organize training courses on purchasing and strategy. 
When asked if any problems with inventory management could be improved, they 
answered the following: 
Interviewee 1 mentioned that there can be an error between the systems in use if there is 
inaccurate input and he mentioned that Unit4 is not really user-friendly. Interviewee 2 
mentioned that they need to utilize what they have available in the warehouse better. He 
then mentioned that the problem in the warehouse lies with the special products but not the 
routine products, which is in line with the results from the database analysis in Chapter 4.1. 
He wants external consultants to have a better overview of the available items in stock, so 
they can be incorporated into the design, and that the project designs should utilize 
standardized material, so if something changes and an item will not be used, it can be used 
in a later project. Interviewee 6 mentioned that bills of material are sometimes created 
before the design is fully completed, and then changed if necessary. If an item that was on 
the original list gets removed, there is nothing that happens to notify the purchasing 
department of the changes, and the item often gets purchased since it was originally on the 
list and it will most likely end up in the warehouse. 
==PAGE:75==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
64 
 
When asked if they have encountered any communication problems with others in the 
supply chain, they said:   
Interviewee 2 mentioned three main problems. The first one is the difficulty of getting the 
project numbers from Veitur to be able to assign an item to a project. This likely happens 
when they receive purchase requests through email when adequate information does not 
follow, this would be eliminated with the standard purchase request forms that he suggested 
earlier. The second is the result of a product number or quantity being entered wrongly 
before sending to suppliers, then the purchasing department would receive an invoice that 
was not expected. Minimizing manual input would reduce the frequency of this happening. 
The last one is when they receive invoices for products that they do not see as having 
arrived, this can happen due to the product not having arrived or that it has arrived, but the 
warehouse has not recorded it as received. Interviewee 6 mentioned late responses to 
emails, which Interviewee 1 agreed to and added that emails are sometimes easy to 
misunderstand.  
When asked how communications are handled when it comes to cancellations, they said: 
All interviewees agree that reducing an order is far more difficult than increasing an order, 
the reason can be that the production of the material has already started. This can happen 
when a project gets cancelled after a purchase order has been made, or if an item had been 
requested by project managers by email or bill of material, then he realizes that he won’t 
use it but forgets to inform the purchasing department. 
When asked about their opinion of the transparency between individuals in the supply chain 
and if they have had any problems related to that, they answered the following: 
Interviewee 1 mentioned that it is important to have knowledge about the systems, what has 
been happening is that bills of materials stop being monitored due to the dates on them. He 
had an example where the number of active lists had dropped recently due to projects being 
cancelled or the project manager forgetting to update the dates, stating that the project 
managers need to keep a closer eye on this matter. Interviewee 2 stated that the process is 
not transparent enough and said that they have all the information about orders in Unit4. 
However, project managers do not have access to that system and therefore must contact 
the purchasing department for relevant information. He states that the project managers and 
==PAGE:76==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
65 
 
designers should be able to see this information. Interviewee 6 states that there is a lack of 
education about the systems in use and that new employees should get better training before 
they start so that they understand the processes better.  
When asked if they checked what is in stock before ordering products after a request is 
received, they said: 
Interviewee 1 said that the special products that are requested are usually never in stock and 
may never even have been bought before. Interviewee 2 mentioned that requests that come 
in through bills of material are checked with AGR to see if the product numbers are in 
stock, it must however be the exact same product number so if there is a similar product 
with a different product number, they won’t see that. He then mentioned that they do not 
check if items requested through email are available in stock unless they suspect that they 
are available in stock. 
When asked what they identify as the biggest waste in the process, they answered: 
All interviewees agreed that the biggest waste was related to the inventory. Interviewee 1 
mentioned that products are ordered for a project that gets put on hold. Interviewee 2 also 
mentioned products that end up in the warehouse and do not get utilized instead of buying 
new products. Interviewee 3 again mentioned items that get removed from bills of material 
that end up getting purchased and stored in the warehouse, she then talked about how a 
long storage time can be harmful to the products. 
When asked if it is common for a product to end up in the warehouse for a long time and 
why that happens, they said: 
Interviewee 1 mentioned that it is not common, but it still ends up being very costly. 
Interviewee 2 said that it is common and due to the fact that there is nothing in the process 
that notifies them that a product will not get used other than the human factor. Interviewee 
6 mentioned that they do not have any data on how often that happens as they do not know 
if a product is going to be used, she said that she only knows it when something gets 
delivered straight to the worksite and gets a message from the project manager that they 
won’t need this product. Interviewees 1 and 6 agreed that it happens due to the bills of 
material not being accurate enough and Interviewee 6 agreed with Interviewee 2 that it is a 
==PAGE:77==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
66 
 
problem that there is nothing that notifies them of changes in the bill of material. 
Interviewee 2 mentioned it is due to wrong products or too much quantity. 
When asked why special products older than 2 years are not disposed of, they mentioned: 
They all mention that the point where it stops is the fact that the one who made the 
purchase request has to take on the cost of the product when taking it from the warehouse.  
4.3.3.5 Warehouse manager 
When asked what the main challenges he faces in his job, he answered: 
Interviewee 9 mentioned the challenges of a product not being documented on arrival, as 
well as making sure that the product reaches the customer in good condition. 
When asked how he felt about the current warehousing/purchasing processes, he said: 
Interviewee 9 mentioned a headache related to the continuous orders that Reykjavík Energy 
has to the warehouse, and they are the only company that does business with Eimskip that 
is allowed to do this. This happens because Reykjavík Energy wants to have all the items 
related to the same project documented under the same order number, so they often make 
many orders to the same order number, but add a letter at the back of the order number. 
This creates a problem for the warehouse as it is difficult to have an overview of which part 
of the order has left the warehouse and which part is still there. 
When asked what could be done better in the process, he answered: 
Interviewee 9 mentioned that it would be better for them if the continuing orders would be 
made as separate orders instead, but he understands that Reykjavík Energy wants to have 
the orders for a specific project under the same number. He then mentioned that the 
workers in the warehouse are not familiar with all the products that Reykjavík Energy 
orders, so when a pallet arrives with a variety of products, it can be difficult and time-
consuming for them to be completely sure what items are connected to what names on the 
order receipt. This can pose a problem for the documentation of products in the warehouse 
and he suggested that the items could be labelled better, especially when a variety of items 
arrive on the same pallet. 
When asked if any steps in the process are unnecessary or time-consuming, he said: 
==PAGE:78==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
67 
 
He mentioned that products that are commonly used are often brought in small quantities 
arguing that it would be better to receive them fewer times in larger quantities. Here he is 
referring to routine products, which currently have not been identified as the source of the 
inventory problem. 
When asked what the main bottlenecks in the process are, he identified: 
Interviewee 9 again mentioned the many orders for routine products like previously. He 
then mentioned large orders that they receive, for a project that might take place in a year, 
leaving them to find space to store it for a year. This takes up a lot of space and slows down 
the reception of other products. 
When asked if they follow any standards in their work processes, he answered: 
They complete a condition check of the products arriving and email Reykjavík Energy if 
the invoice needs to be corrected or if there are any quantity discrepancies. For storage, 
they use a system that documents the location of pallets through the use of a pallet system, 
a sticker with the booking number of the product is placed on the rack at its designated 
storage location. This however only applies to the products that are stored in the warehouse 
and it is important not to move the pallet to a new location without updating the system and 
placing a new sticker at the new location, so the products do not get lost. 
When asked what they do today in order to improve their processes, he mentioned: 
Interviewee 9 said that they are constantly trying to improve the processes and mentioned 
that they improved their warehouse 2 years ago by replacing the rack system and repairing 
the floors which improved the utilization of the warehouse and that they upgraded the 
heating system to have it more stable. This does however only benefit the products that are 
stored inside. 
When asked what tools they use to locate products in the warehouse and how that system is 
updated he said: 
Interviewee 9 mentioned that they use a system called MLS to search where a product has 
been documented with the pallet system. He mentioned that they update it with manual 
input or barcodes, with barcodes being preferred so to minimize human error. He then 
==PAGE:79==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
68 
 
mentioned that most of the products that Reykjavík Energy brings in do not have barcodes, 
but that it would be convenient.  
When asked if the warehouse always manages to work according to FIFO(first in first out), 
he answered the following: 
Interviewee 9 mentioned that they manage to use FIFO for the products that are stored 
inside the warehouse, but it becomes more of a challenge for the products that are stored 
outside. There is not endless available space and he mentioned problems with the pipes and 
tubes being in storage, and then a similar type of pipe arrives, then they just place those 
pipes on top of the older ones. This would mean that accessing the older pipes would be 
very time-consuming and lead to very old pipes not leaving the warehouse since the first 
ones to leave would be the newer ones. The reason for this is that they do not know what 
shipment is going to arrive next or tomorrow so they cannot prepare for the reception. 
When asked if any inventory management related issues could be improved, he answered: 
Interviewee 9 mentioned that it would be possible to increase the standard orders for 
routine products, orders could be placed closer to the date the products are actually needed 
so that they will not stay in the warehouse for a long time before the project starts. He then 
mentioned that the product catalog could be made more transparent for those responsible 
for ordering, to utilize the existing stock instead. 
When asked what he thinks about the transparency between different individuals in the 
process, and if he has had any problems related to that, he mentioned: 
Interviewee 9 mentioned that the transparency is not good enough, as he does not know 
when shipments are going to arrive. He used an example that happened earlier the day of 
the interview, then he received a large shipment of pipes but had not been notified of it 
beforehand, so they just had to place them in front of the older pipes, making them the first 
ones to leave the warehouse. If he had been notified before, he could have made 
arrangements for removing the older pipes, cleaned the area, brought in the newer pipes, 
and then placed the older pipes in front. That would help them make sure that the older 
products get used before the new products, ensuring that what comes in first would be the 
first to go out. 
When asked what he identified as the biggest waste in the process, he mentioned: 
==PAGE:80==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
69 
 
Interviewee 9 mentioned the many small shipments as the biggest waste in the process. 
When asked if it is common for products to stay in the warehouse for a long time, he said: 
Interviewee 9 said that it is common for products to stay in the warehouse for a long time 
and guesses that changes in projects are the main reason for that happening. 
When asked if it is common for products to stay in the warehouse for a long time and if it 
does happen that products that get stored for a long time start to deteriorate, he answered: 
Interviewee 9 said that it is common for products to stay in the warehouse for a long time 
and guesses that changes in projects are the main reason for that happening. He then 
mentioned that it does happen that they start to deteriorate. He mentioned that he suspects 
that there are steel pipes that become impractical to use and do not meet standard 
requirements but can be repaired, but that takes time and money. He then mentioned that 
steel pipes can deteriorate on the inside if water settles inside them for a long time. He then 
mentioned products just being outdated and made an example of 3g products that are highly 
unlikely to ever be used since there are now 4g and 5g products available. 
When asked how he determines which products should be stored inside, outside, or in 
containers, he said:  
Interviewee 9 mentioned that the storage place is based on the size of the product, its 
sensitivity to the weather, and the quantity. He mentioned that large products need to be 
stored outside, which explains why large pipes are stored there. He also mentioned that if a 
product comes in large quantities, it can be stored in containers outside. Then he said that 
electrical equipment is never stored outside since it is very sensitive to the weather. 
4.3.3.6 Summary 
To summarize, the main areas for improvement from the interviews have been identified 
and later it will be attempted to apply some of the tools of lean to those areas in order to 
reduce or eliminate those problems. The main problems will now be mentioned, and some 
of the comments that individuals had related to those problems. 
The product catalog:  
The product catalog is something that the purchasing department oversees, so it was 
interesting to see that every single interviewee apart from the ones in the purchasing 
==PAGE:81==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
70 
 
department mentioned that the product catalog was something that could be improved. 
Some of the interviewees were not at all happy with how it currently is, to say the least.  
Interviewee 7 talked about how complicated and difficult to navigate the product catalog is, 
he mentioned that there are no standard names for the products in question which makes 
finding specific products in the product catalog difficult, which Interviewee 5 called a 
nightmare and stated that components can have 2 different names depending on the size of 
the component. Interviewee 4 agreed that the product catalog is chaotic and confusing and 
suggested that she should be able to click on the products to see an image of the product 
along with a short description of the product and an explanation of which situation that 
product would be suitable. Interviewee 3 agreed that the product catalog is not good in 
terms of setup and mentioned that products are often referred to by nicknames and that it 
would be much better if they were referred to by their name from the supplier, and then 
sorted by those names. Interviewee 4 agreed that using the names from the supplier would 
be much simpler and criticized the usage of Icelandic names for many of the products in the 
product catalog, stating that many external consultants might not be familiar with them.  
Interviewee 5 agrees that the product catalog is unorganized and mentioned that it is easy to 
confuse products and that sometimes there are products in it that are longer than the 
standard length, and it can accidentally be included in the bills of material since it is 
difficult to notice the difference. Interviewee 3 mentioned that searching for a product in 
the database is difficult since you need to know exactly what the item is called in the 
database, he suggests utilizing categories for simplifying looking up items. Interviewee 3 
compared the product catalog to an online store and said that it was like if you wanted to 
look for jeans, but was only shown leather jackets and gloves, and mentioned that he would 
prefer it to be set up in categories. So, if he is looking for a leather jacket, he could choose 
the category coats, then jackets, and lastly leather jackets. Interviewee 5 mentioned that the 
bills of materials are sometimes wrong due to wrong products being added by the external 
consultants and mentioned the reason being that the product catalog includes products that 
Veitur does not want to use anymore that often end up in the bill of material. Interviewee 4 
agrees that is confusing to include products that are no longer in use and questions why 
they are still included. Interviewee 5 then mentioned that the external consultant might not 
==PAGE:82==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
71 
 
be aware of these preferences and questioned why these items are still included in the 
product catalog.  
Interviewee 7 then mentioned that the external consultants can see the product number of 
each product in the product catalog, but for some reason, it is not possible for all products, 
which makes them need to contact Veitur in order to acquire the product number. 
Interviewees 7 and 8 mentioned that the external consultants do not always know what 
products are available since they only get sent an Excel file of the product catalog from 
DMM, and they could have an outdated product catalog. Interviewee 7 suspects that there is 
more than one product catalog in Veitur and Interviewee 8 suggested that since they can see 
the tendering documents online, they should be able to see the latest version of the product 
catalog online as well and mentioned that it would be helpful.  
What seemed to be the biggest issue with the product catalog in Interviewee 7's opinion, 
was that when the external consultants need to add an item to the product catalog, they also 
must remember to add all of the supporting components that are needed for that item, such 
as bolts, seals, and screws and in which sizes. Interviewee 7 mentioned that it is almost 
impossible for the external consultants unless they are very familiar with the product in 
question and said that Veitur has provided them with instructions, but that they still need to 
be worked on. Interviewee 7 therefore suggested that when the external consultants need to 
place a product on the bill of material, there should be a bundled package in the product 
catalog for that product along with all the necessary supporting components. Interviewee 7 
made the example of a fire hydrant, stating that today there are around 10-15 items that 
must be remembered to also include in the bills of material and stated that not all designers 
have practical field experience or experience with the product in question and therefore 
could choose the wrong supporting item for the fire hydrant. Interviewee 7 suggested that 
they should be able to select something called “1 fire hydrant” that would include the fire 
hydrant, along with all the necessary components. Interviewee 4 made a similar statement 
to Interviewee 7, stating that products should be grouped together if they are needed 
together, meaning that “if you order this, you must also have this”.  
Interviewee 3 said that the transparency of available products is not that great since they do 
not see the product catalog in AGR like the purchasing department, they only see it in 
DMM. Interviewee 3 said that in DMM, he can only see that there are products in the 
==PAGE:83==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
72 
 
warehouse, but he does not see if these are products that someone is planning on using or if 
it has been there for a while, making it difficult for them to decide on utilizing old products, 
while Interviewee 4 mentioned that it would be crucial to have a good product catalog in 
order to utilize the products that are in the warehouse stating that not utilizing what they 
have in stock as one of the biggest waste in the process. Interviewee 9 agreed that the 
product catalog should be made more transparent for those making the purchase requests so 
that they could see the products in the warehouse and utilize those products. Interviewee 3 
then stated that he had accidentally stolen products from another project due to this low 
transparency. Interviewee 5 added that the external consultants then only see a downloaded 
Excel of the product catalog from DMM. Interviewee 4 mentioned that the reason for the 
bills of material being inaccurate is often because they have poor information to work with 
as the product catalog is not reliable. Interviewees 3, 4, 5, 7, 8, and 9 all agreed that the 
product catalog requires a review and an update in order for it to work properly. 
The bills of material:  
Most orders for projects are done through bills of material that the external consultants 
create, the designers at Veitur review, project managers oversee the dates, and purchasing 
department purchases according to the dates. They are therefore an important component in 
the supply chain when it comes to the accumulation of inventory at the warehouse. The 
interviewees spoke a lot about the bills of material and their summarized answers can be 
seen in this section. 
Interviewee 7 mentions the importance of the bills of material being correct, Veitur can 
face significant difficulties with the project. Interviewee 7 mentioned that the bills of 
material may be incorrect due to design requirements changing after the ground has been 
excavated or due to an error by the external consultant. Interviewee 3 identifies these 
reasons to be the most common reasons as to why products end up in the warehouse for a 
long time. Interviewee 7 then mentioned that the errors made by the external consultants 
may be because the product catalog does not have enough information for the external 
consultants, for example, that necessary components are not grouped with products needing 
them and difficulty searching for items in the product catalog like mentioned before. 
Interviewee 8 agrees with Interviewee 7 and mentioned that the bills of material may be 
incorrect due to changes in the design, he then added that if that happens, it has to be 
==PAGE:84==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
73 
 
ensured that relevant information gets shared with everyone involved, otherwise, an 
important item might not get added to the bill of material which can delay the project. 
Interviewee 5 agrees that something unexpected occurs after opening a ditch leads to the 
bills of materials being incorrect, and added that it may lead to items that have been 
purchased becoming unusable for the project, which leads to them ending up in the 
warehouse. Interviewee 4 agrees that the reason for the bills of material often being 
incorrect is due to the external consultants having to work with the poor information from 
the product catalog or that they have not been reviewed well enough.  
Interviewees 7 and 8 agree that they do their best to prevent bills of material from being 
incorrect by thoroughly reviewing them after creating them, with Interviewee 8 adding that 
they get reviewed by Veitur as well after they send them over. Interviewee 5 confirms that 
they review the bills of material after receiving them from the external consultants. 
Interviewee 8 then questions if the internal designers at Veitur are the most qualified 
individuals to handle the final review of the bills of material, stating that it might be 
beneficial to have someone who has hands-on experience working with the material.  
Interviewees 7 and 8 both claim to try their best to use standardized products when creating 
the bills of material, with Interviewee 7 mentioning that sometimes he just cannot complete 
the design using only standardized material. Interviewee 8 however claims that he always 
works with standardized material which often leads to him using more components than 
needed, he then mentioned that he knows other designers who always use what they think is 
the best for each situation. Interviewee 8 then talks about how he thinks it would benefit 
Veitur if the designs had to be created with constraints to only use standardized material in 
the bills of material as it would allow them to easily find a use for the material in different 
projects something comes up and deems the material unusable in the project in question. 
Interviewee 5 agrees that they prefer when standardized material is on the bills of material, 
and mentions that if something is custom-made and changes occur, that item will likely sit 
in the warehouse and never get used. Interviewee 2 agrees that there is a lack of consistency 
and people are often just ordering what they deem best each time and mentioned that it 
would help if standardized products were more common, so we would know what we are 
buying. He recommends adapting the designs in order to use standardized material since it 
==PAGE:85==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
74 
 
would be easier to repurpose if something goes wrong and it cannot be used in the original 
project. 
Interviewees 7 and 8 both agree that they do not have clear transparency about what items 
are available in the warehouse when creating the bills of material in order to utilize the 
available items instead of suggesting items that need to be purchased, apart from the routine 
products. Interviewee 5 also does not see what items are available until she submits the bill 
of material to DMM, then she can see what is available by looking a specific item up, she 
can however only see if that item is available but not if it is reserved for another project. 
Interviewee 3 adds that he does not have any overview of what items in the warehouse are 
currently available due to their project being cancelled, but he wants it to be standard 
practice to see what is available in the warehouse before placing an order. Interviewee 2 
mentioned that when they receive the bills of material, their program AGR automatically 
checks if that item is available in the warehouse and is not assigned to an active bill of 
material, the items must however be exactly the same.  
Interviewees 1 and 6 mentioned that project managers must remember to update the dates 
on the bills of material when changes in the project schedule occur and mentioned that they 
often forget to update them. Interviewee 6 mentioned that what happens if they forget to 
update them is that the bill of material stops being monitored due to the assigned dates, 
making the products that were ordered for that project look available if the same product is 
placed on another bill of material, and someone else might accidentally take the material, 
making the original project get delayed. Interviewee 1 then showed me that he had 11 fewer 
bills of material in monitoring during the interview than the previous weekend, which 
means that those projects have been cancelled or that the dates have not been updated 
correctly. Interviewees 2  and 3 mentioned that it is the responsibility of the project 
managers to notify the purchasing department if a project gets cancelled and Interviewee 2 
added that there are not good enough trigger points in the system to let them know a project 
has been cancelled. Interviewees 3 and 4 agree that it is the responsibility of the project 
managers to make sure that the dates are correct and that the bill of material is not being 
monitored if a project gets cancelled or postponed, they do however not talk about 
informing the purchasing department about why they removed it from monitoring.  
==PAGE:86==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
75 
 
Interviewee 2 then mentioned that it would be best if everyone placed their purchase 
requests using bills of material as opposed to email. Interviewee 2 wants to eliminate email 
requests by having an ordering system that those who need to request without using bills of 
materials should use. In that system you would need to fill out the necessary information on 
the request form before sending the request, this would eliminate having to send emails 
back and forth in order to get all the relevant information. Interviewee 6 talked about how 
she gets an email stating that an item will be placed on the bill of material when it is 
complete but should be purchased now. Then the item may never be added to the bill of 
material, then it is not possible to see who requested the item and why. Interviewee 6 then 
mentioned that she gets a bill of material that is not fully complete and maybe changes 
later, this poses a problem for them since there currently is nothing in the system that 
notifies them that an item gets removed from the bill of material. It happens often that they 
order by the bill of material and then an item gets removed from the bill of material and just 
ends up staying in the warehouse with no one knowing that it is there. Interviewee 6 
mentioned this as being the biggest waste in the system as they waste a lot of money and 
storage space on items that will sit in the warehouse for a long time and maybe even start to 
deteriorate. Interviewee 2 somehow agrees and mentioned the biggest waste being 
excessive ordering and inventory, stating that the worst they can do is not utilize what they 
have, but rather order something else. 
Warehouse and inventory:  
It is important to focus on the warehouse since that is the place where the products 
eventually end up. It is important to interview the warehouse manager and get a better 
understanding of what happens in the warehouse and what their input is on the problem. 
The other interviewees then had opinions on the warehouse. Answers relating to the 
warehouse and inventory will be summarized in this section. 
Interviewee 9 talked about how Reykjavík Energy orders continuous orders to the 
warehouse under the same order number, adding a letter each time and sometimes even 
using the whole alphabet. He mentioned that makes it difficult for the employees in the 
warehouse to have a good overview of what has come in and what has gone out of the 
warehouse. Interviewee 9 mentioned that Reykjavík Energy is the only company that works 
with Eimskip that is allowed to do this, and thinks it is because Reykjavík Energy wants to 
==PAGE:87==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
76 
 
have all the products for a specific project under the same order number. Interviewee 9 
mentioned that it would be good if the commonly used items were purchased in larger 
quantities, here he is referring to the routine products, but they have been shown to not be a 
big factor in the inventory problem.  
Interviewee 9 then mentioned that they have been receiving products in large quantities that 
are for a project a year later, he said that it takes up space in the warehouse and slows down 
the reception of other items. Interviewee 9 mentioned the transparency not being as good as 
he would like, he mentioned that they have no idea about what is going to arrive later today 
or tomorrow. He wants to make sure that the products that have been there the longest get 
used before newer products of the same kind, FIFO(First In First Out), and that it works 
well with the products that are stored in the warehouse but for the products stored outside, 
it is difficult. He said that, if large pipes were to unexpectedly arrive now, they would just 
be placed on top or in front of similar pipes. He said that if he would be notified about the 
arrival beforehand they could move the older material, clean the area, bring in the new 
material, and then place the older material in front, but currently, they are not notified about 
what is arriving at the warehouse.  
Interviewee 9 mentioned that 3 variables matter when deciding on a storage place for a 
product, that is sensitivity to the weather, quantity, and the size of the product. Some 
products, such as the large steel pipes need to be stored outside, then if he gets a big 
shipment of a product, it might be stored in a container outside. But it is important that the 
product can actually be stored outside, electrical equipment is, for example always stored 
inside the warehouse. 
Interviewee 8 mentioned that contractors often take out all the products for a project from 
the warehouse at the beginning of a project and sometimes lose some of the products, he 
then questions if Veitur should even be the ones acquiring the products for the projects in 
the first place and if it would be smart to leave that responsibility with the contractors and 
mentioned that they might treat the products better if they were responsible for acquiring it. 
Interviewee 8 then mentioned a problem that he knows Veitur has, which is that products 
have been getting lost in the warehouse and that at one point Veitur used to have their own 
warehouse, questioning that it should be worth considering again as it raises the oversight 
of the inventory. Interviewee 4 agrees with Interviewee 8 that items have gone missing in 
==PAGE:88==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
77 
 
the warehouse and added that the contractors picking up the products have sometimes been 
given the wrong products, or products that are damaged or get scratched upon delivery. 
Interviewee 9 mentioned that they use a pallet system in the warehouse where a sticker is 
placed on the rack where a pallet is stored and the products on that pallet are assigned to the 
sticker through manual input or scanning barcodes. He then said that every employee can 
look up the number on the sticker to locate the pallet and this helps in preventing the 
products from getting lost, he said that this system only works for the products that are 
stored inside the warehouse. Interviewee 4 then mentioned that mishandling the products is 
the biggest waste in the process, stating that brand-new products are sometimes being lifted 
poorly with a forklift in the warehouse, damaging the products. She then mentioned 
products being stored outside as being harmful since they are exposed to all kinds of 
weather conditions, mentioning that it is not good for the exposed ends of steel pipes. 
Interviewee 1 disagrees with Interviewee 4 that products have been mishandled in the 
warehouse and claimed that products are returned to the warehouse in bad condition and 
that they had not been reviewed before being returned to the warehouse. He also states that 
the truck that picks up the products is sometimes full of gravel and that the workers even 
dump the products from the truck at the worksite. Interviewee 9 mentioned that sometimes 
products get returned to the warehouse damaged or in an unsellable state, and mentioned 
that they should be reviewed before being returned, and only accept returning products in a 
condition that they would not mind getting later. 
Interviewee 3 agrees and stated that he thinks that acquiring products for projects is the 
most prolific problem related to inventory management at Veitur and the biggest waste in 
the process. He thinks it would solve their inventory problems if they did not source 
products for all the projects, stating that it has a tremendous hidden cost involved. 
Interviewee 3 mentioned that a project can get delayed just due to one important item being 
delayed and then they are stuck with the items that were ordered. Interviewee 3 suggests 
transferring the responsibility of sourcing products to the contractors like Interviewee 8 and 
mentioned that sometimes when items have been purchased and placed in the warehouse, 
the city for example might cancel the project, leaving the items idle in the warehouse and 
stated that they can start to deteriorate after a long time in storage. He mentioned this as 
being the reason for having over a billion ISK in tied-up capital in the warehouse. 
Interviewee 9 mentioned the improvements that the warehouse has done to preserve the 
==PAGE:89==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
78 
 
products, they upgraded the entire rack system and repaired the floors, but most 
importantly, they upgraded the heating system in the warehouse to maintain a more stable 
temperature, he mentioned again that these improvements only benefit the products that are 
stored inside the warehouse. Interviewee 9 then agreed that products can start to deteriorate 
and mentioned that the pipes that are stored outside often become impractical to use after a 
long time, needing to be repaired which takes time and costs money. Interviewee 9 then 
mentioned that water can settle inside the steel pipes that are stored outside making them 
deteriorate faster, he then mentioned products simply becoming outdated and highlighted 
that there are some products in the warehouse that use 3g and will not be used since there is 
now both 4g and 5g available. Interviewee 2 then added that if you were to break down the 
warehouse, you would see that the inventory would be due to the special products, which 
further supports the findings of the inventory database analysis in Chapter 4.1. Interviewee 
4 agrees that project cancellations and delays are a big reason for products ending up in the 
warehouse, she mentioned that the one leading the project can become bankrupt or just 
abandon the project after products have been ordered for it since the lead-time for products 
can be quite long. Interviewee 2 identifies the need to utilize what they have available in 
stock better as one of the main areas to improve, Interviewee 1 agrees and said that the 
biggest waste in the process occurs in inventory due to disorganization. Interviewee 9 then 
confirmed that it is common for products to enter the warehouse and stay there for a long 
time. 
Interviewee 4 mentioned that they often do not have enough storage space for all the 
products that are ordered and stated that pipes ordered from Set are often just kept there 
until they are needed. She mentioned that there is sometimes just no available space and 
that she has often been asked to store products on the worksite, even before they have been 
given a worksite to work on and before the contractors have even set up in the worksite. 
She does not like that suggestion as she would then be responsible for any damages that 
could happen to the material.  
Interviewee 4 finds it interesting they are not trying to sell some of the products in the 
inventory that have been in storage for a really long time, with Interviewee 3 stating that 
the product managers currently do not see how long a product has been there and 
mentioned that Veitur is not in control of the warehouse, Reykjavík Energy is. Interviewee 
==PAGE:90==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
79 
 
2, who is a part of the purchasing department at Reykjavík Energy mentioned that even 
though they can see how long a product has been in the warehouse, they do not know if that 
product is going to be used or not. Interviewee 2 mentioned that the reason for old products 
not being sold or disposed of is because someone has to take on the cost of the product, the 
one who ordered the product would need to take on the cost associated with removing the 
product from the warehouse, that is where it usually stops. Interviewees 2 and 6 agree with 
Interviewee 1 on why old products are not sold or disposed of.  
Interviewee 2 mentioned that Reykjavík Energy has received invoices from suppliers for 
goods that have not been received, the reason sometimes being that the product has been 
delivered to the warehouse but it had not been recorded as being received in the warehouse. 
Interviewee 9 talked about how the workers in the warehouse are not familiar with all the 
products that are ordered and mentioned that when an order comes with a variety of items, 
they may not be 100% sure what each item is called on the receiving document, they then 
spend a long time trying to figure that out. Interviewee 9 then suggested that it would be 
helpful if the items were labelled better to make sure that everything gets recorded correctly 
in their system. Interviewee 9 then added that it would be beneficial if the products came 
with a barcode so they would be more easily identified and eliminate the chance of human 
error when receiving or typing the product numbers, he mentioned that only around 5% of 
the products from Reykjavík Energy have barcodes. 
4.3.4 Knowledge on lean 
It was then important to know how familiar the interviewees are with lean and if they are 
currently using it in some way. This will give the researcher a better insight into how it 
would be best to start implementing the tools of lean. The interviewees that were asked 
lean-related questions were the project managers and purchasing department and the reason 
why others were not asked about lean is that they either do not take a large enough part in 
the process. 
When summarizing their answers, it can be seen that all of the interviewees are somewhat 
familiar with lean but none of them have a great understanding of it, some have taken 
courses related to the subject. None of the interviewees apart from Interviewee 3 are 
currently using lean in their work, with interviewee 3 mentioning that he uses 5S. 
Interviewee 1 mentioned that the subsidiaries have implemented lean in certain areas of 
==PAGE:91==
 
Findings and analysis 
Master Thesis 
80 
 
their processes. Even though most of the interviewees do not work with lean, Interviewees 
2 and 4 mentioned some of their goals that align with lean, such as improving the efficiency 
of their processes and shortening communication paths. All interviewees agreed that 
implementing some of the tools in lean would be beneficial to them, and Interviewee 3 
mentioned that they previously had a dedicated person in these matters. Interviewee 1 
brought up the point that all the people working the jobs would need to be on board for it to 
work efficiently. Interviewee 2 mentioned that it would help them if everyone would have 
access to relevant information, suggesting that the transparency could be improved. 
Interviewee 6 talked about how improved transparency could assist her when it comes to 
ordering products and help eliminate unnecessary orders that just end up in the inventory, 
therefore contributing to a reduction of the accumulated inventory.

Recommendations: Application of lean thinking

5 Recommendations: Application of lean thinking  
From the literature review, lean thinking was mentioned to be a methodology that focuses 
on optimizing processes, reducing waste, and improving efficiency. The literature review 
mentioned the 5 principles of lean as being value, value stream, flow, pull, and perfection. 
In this chapter, the researcher will apply the principles of lean and some of the tools to the 
warehousing/purchasing processes at Veitur in order to analyze if they are likely to help in 
improving those processes. 
5.1 Value 
As mentioned in the literature review, it is important to define the value from the 
customer's standpoint. In the situation here, it is Veitur who is the customer. It is seen in the 
interviews, especially in the interview with Interviewee 2, who is the director of the 
purchasing department. Interviewee 2 mentioned Veitur many times as being the customer, 
stating that it is the job of the purchasing department to serve their customers, and that one 
of which is Veitur. His job is to make sure that their orders are fulfilled and ready on time. 
Interviewee 3 mentioned that he as a project manager needs the material to be available 
when the project starts, and Interviewee 4 agreed. Interviewees 3 and 4 mention that they 
give the purchasing department a purchasing request, which makes the value for the 
customer, which is Veitur, that the requested resources are available when needed. 
5.2 Value stream 
As mentioned in the literature review, there are 3 types of activities, value-adding activities, 
necessary non-value-adding activities, and unnecessary non-value-adding activities, which 
are called waste. The aim here is to identify all the activities in the warehousing/purchasing 
process from the interviews and identify which activities are unnecessary and non-value-
adding, that is waste. In Chapter 4.3.1 the processes were identified from the interviews and 
can again be seen in Figure 4.8. In Chapter 4.3.3 the areas for improvement were identified 
from the interviews. The areas for improvement are based on activities that are non-value-
adding for the customer and will be investigated better and ways will be identified in order 
to eliminate or reduce those non-value-adding activities that are not necessary. In the 
literature review, the 5 Why method was introduced to help with identifying root causes. 
The 5 why method was performed on the problem as to why products end up unutilized in 
==PAGE:93==
 
Recommendations: Application of lean thinking 
Master Thesis 
82 
 
the warehouse based on the interviews. The result of the root cause analysis can be seen in 
Figure 5.1, with the roots colored yellow. This was done in order to make the causes that 
lead to products ending up unutilized in the warehouse clearer and assist in identifying the 
non-value-adding activities. The identified non-value-adding activities were identified as 
the following and can be seen in Table 5.1. 
Table 5.1: Non-value-adding activities 
Non-value-adding activities 
Time spent trying to understand the product catalog and look for the correct products in it. 
- The way that the product catalog currently is set up is the source of various wastes. 
How postponements/cancellations are handled. 
- When postponements and cancellations, that information needs to be shared adequately, the transparency 
currently is not up to par, currently the bill of material is just removed from monitoring. 
How changes in bills of material are being handled. 
- Currently, there is nothing that notifies the purchasing department when a product is removed from a bill of 
material. 
Poor transparency between individuals in the supply chain.  
- The product managers do not see the same product catalog as the purchasing department. 
- The external consultants only get sent an Excel copy of the product catalog when they ask for it. 
- Then the warehouse manager has no overview of what shipments will arrive at the warehouse. 
How products are recorded in the warehouse.  
- The products are not properly labelled when arriving at the warehouse which can be time-consuming and cause 
mistakes when documenting their arrival. 
When purchase requests arrive through email. 
- Purchase requests that arrive through email are often missing necessary information that is missing. 
Products not being in usable condition. 
- Products can get lost or deteriorated. 
- Products can be outdated 
 
These are identified main activities that do not add value to the customer, and in the next 
principle, ways will be identified in order to minimize or eliminate these activities and the 
waste that follows.

Time spent trying to understand the product catalog and look for the correct products in it.
- The way that the product catalog currently is set up is the source of various wastes.
Wastes
Nr.
Overproduction - The product catalog being complicated can lead to the ordering of products that are not needed.
W1
- It takes time trying to understand the product catalog, slowing down deliveries of data to others in the supply 
chain.
W2
- Product managers not being able to see which project, if any, a product in the product catalog is associated with, 
can lead to someone taking products that were allocated for another project and delaying that project.
W3
Transportation - The external consultants needing to send emails to acquire product numbers and other information is unnecessary 
transportation of information.
W4
Inventory
- When disorganization in the product catalog leads to incorrect products being ordered, they will become 
inventory in the warehouse, not increasing the value for the customer.
W5
Motion
- Having to browse and search the product catalog due to it being confusing and unorganized is unnecessary 
motion.
W6
Defects
- Having outdated products included in the product catalog, no standardized naming system, not sufficient 
information about the products, and not focusing on standardized products can lead to incorrect products being 
purchased which is classified as a defect.
W7
Skills
- Time spent browsing and trying to understand the product catalog decreases the time that the worker could be 
doing more productive work.

non-value-
adding activity
Waiting
How postponements/cancellations are handled.
- When postponements and cancellations, it is important for that information to be shared adequately, the 
transparency currently is not up to par, currently the bill of material is just removed from monitoring.
Wastes
Nr.
Overproduction
- If project managers forgets to notify that a project has been cancelled or postponed, or if the bill of material stops 
being monitored without a notification appearing for the purchasing department, they may not notice it in time to 
cancel an order that has been placed.
W9
Waiting
- Unnecessary purchases, due to a project being cancelled or postponed, slow down the reception of other products 
in the warehouse and take up space that could be used for other products. This can happen due to a project being 
cancelled or postponed if the purchasing department is not notified.
W10
Transportation
- The purchasing department needs to send an email it order to ask if the bill of material became outdated or if it 
was removed manually if they want to know why, since they do not see the reason, is unnecessary transportation of 
information.
W11
Overprocessing - Having the supplier produce an unnecessary product that is not needed but was ordered.
W12
- If the purchasing department does not get notified soon enough, or not at all, that a bill of material is not being 
monitored anymore, it can be difficult to cancel the order.
W13
- Since the purchasing department does not know why a bill of material stopped being monitored, they cannot tag 
those products that arrived as being assigned to a cancelled project, which would make them available for other 
project managers. If the products that cannot be cancelled are not standardized, it can be difficult to use them in 
other projects.
W14
Defects
- When a purchase requests cannot be cancelled because the supplier has already started manufacturing the 
products or if purchasing department was not made aware that the project plan has changed, then unwanted 
products arrive to the warehouse.
W15
Inventory
non-value-
adding activity

Recommendations: Application of lean thinking

85 
 
 
Figure 5.4: Waste related to how changes in bills of material are handled 
 
Figure 5.5: Waste related to poor transparency in the supply chain 
How changes in bills of material are being handled.
- Currently, there is nothing that notifies the purchasing department when a product is removed from a bill of 
material.
Wastes
Nr.
Overproduction
- If a product gets removed from a bill of material, the purchasing department does not receive any notification. 
They might have exported the bill of material from the system or already placed an order, this leads to unnecessary 
products being ordered.
W16
Waiting
- Unnecessary purchases, due to a product being removed from a bill of material, slow down the reception of other 
products in the warehouse and take up space that could be used for other products. This can happen if a product 
gets removed from a bill of material without the purchasing department finding out.
W17
Overprocessing - Having the supplier produce an unnecessary product that is not needed but was ordered.
W18
Inventory
- Unnecessary product that are ordered after being removed from a bill of material will end up in inventory and it 
will be difficult to reuse unless it was standardized, and while it is not transparent which products are available in 
stock due to incorrect orders or cancellations.
W19
Defects
- When products that were removed from the bills of material end up arriving, they are identified as defects.
W20
non-value-
adding activity
Poor transparency between individuals in the supply chain. 
- The product managers do not see the same product catalog as the purchasing department.
- The external consultants only get sent an excel copy of the product catalog when they ask for it.
- Then the warehouse manager has no overview of what shipments will arrive at the warehouse.
Wastes
Nr.
Overproduction - The project managers and external consultants do not have the same overview of the product catalog as the 
purchasing department, which can leads to products being ordered instead of utilizing what is available.
W21
- The external consultants need to wait for an updated product catalog to arrive if they request it.
W22
- If the warehouse manager does not know what is going to be arriving, he cannot prepare the receiving process in 
advance.
W23
Transportation - The external consultants needing to request the product catalog if they want to see it is unnecessary transportation 
of information.
W24
- Ordering products instead of utilizing available products due to poor transparency prevents the inventory from 
shrinking.
W25
- If the warehouse does not know what is going to arrive due to poor transparency, then it can be difficult to 
prioritize older products leaving the warehouse before newer ones. The warehouse cannot prepare for an arrival of 
products so, new products get placed in front of, or on top of older products and therefore leave before the older 
ones.
W26
Defects
- Not having an optimal overview of the product catalog due to different information available for different 
individuals in the supply chain can lead to wrong products being ordered.

As seen in the figures above, there is a substantial amount of waste that needs to be 
eliminated or minimized. The next principle of lean attempts to identify tools that can be 
applied in the process in order to reduce the waste in the process.  
5.3 Flow 
As mentioned in the literature review, the flow principle aims to let information and 
products flow through the process and avoid waste. This chapter will therefore show how 
the tools of lean mentioned in the literature review could be applied to areas in the process 
How products are recorded in the warehouse. 
- The products are not properly labelled when arriving to the warehouse which can be time-consuming and cause 
mistakes when documenting their arrival.
Wastes
Nr.
Waiting
- If the receiving time is long in the warehouse, the purchasing department has to wait longer for confirmation that 
products have arrived at the warehouse.
W28
Overprocessing - The warehouse workers having to sort products that arrive in the same box and figure out what is what instead of 
having it properly labelled.
W29
Inventory
- If a product arrives to the warehouse but was documented incorrectly, it can just sit in the warehouse without 
anyone knowing.
W30
Skills
- The warehouse workers trying to figure out which product is which due to it not being labelled properly is 
unnecessary motion.
W31
Defects
- The warehouse documenting a product that arrives incorrectly is a defect and needs to be corrected.
W32
non-value-
adding activity
When purchase requests arrive through email.
- Purchase requests that arrive through email are often missing necessary information that is missing.
Wastes
Nr.
Transportation - The purchasing department having to request additional information from project managers when purchase 
requests arrive through email.
W33
Inventory
- If project number is not included in purchase requests that arrive through email, it is difficult to know who is the 
owner of the product when it arrives.
W34
Skills
- Time that the purchasing departments spends trying to get more information when they receive poor purchasing 
request through email, that time could be utilized better.
W35
non-value-
adding activity
Products not being in usable condition.
- Products can get lost or deteriorated. 
- Products can be outdated
Wastes
Nr.
Inventory
- Outdated products will most likely sit in the warehouse until being disposed of.
W36
- Products getting lost in the warehouse is classified as a defect since it needs to be ordered again if needed.
W37
- When a product has started to deteriorate, then the process of repairing it adds no value to the customer when 
comparing to its original condition.
W38
Defects
non-value-
adding activity

that are classified as waste in order to either reduce or eliminate that waste. The tools that 
will be used are standardization, 5S, Andon, Poka yoke, and DVM. 
5.3.1 Standardization 
Standards, as explained in the literature review, represent the most efficient method of 
performing a task, and are a great method of preventing discrepancies, variation, and waste. 
Therefore, the aim here is to provide recommendations for standards that could be 
implemented in the processes in order to reduce the waste previously identified.  
Standardize products: 
It is recommended that the product selection should be standardized, and Veitur should 
introduce a SOP that instructs the external contractors to always create the design based on 
the standardized products, when possible, even if it means using more components in the 
design, which is something that Interviewees 2, 5, and 8 agree that would benefit Veitur. If 
standardized products were used, it would be easier to use them in other projects if the 
project in question gets cancelled, which Interviewee 2 agrees with. If it is easier to utilize 
products that end up in the warehouse, then that would reduce the time that a product stays 
in the warehouse, which would likely result in fewer products deteriorating.  
Standardize checking the product catalog: 
It is recommended that it should then become SOP for the external consultants to check 
what is available in the product catalog when creating the bills of material and use 
standardized products unless it is impossible, this would likely result in better utilization of 
the existing inventory and result in less defects do to using standardized products.  
It is recommended that it should also be SOP for project managers to check what is 
available in the product catalog before submitting a purchase request, this would allow 
them to utilize the product catalog instead of ordering products if there are available 
products and should be an effective method after all the recommendations in this chapter 
have been implemented. Interviewee 4 mentioned that it could only be possible to do so if 
the product catalog is organized.  
Standardize storage area outside the warehouse: 
==PAGE:99==
 
Recommendations: Application of lean thinking 
Master Thesis 
88 
 
It is recommended that Veitur works together with the warehouse manager at Eimskip in 
order to create SOP for the products that are not stored in the warehouse in order to prevent 
those products from getting lost or deteriorating. As Interviewee 9 mentioned, the pallet 
system that they use and the recent improvements that have taken place in the area only 
benefit the products that are stored inside the warehouse. If an efficient and organized 
storage system was implemented for the products that are stored outside, and standards 
such as, all pipes coming with a lid to prevent water from entering the pipes, and 
standardized methods in handling and storing the products safely, there would be fewer 
products that would get lost or deteriorate in the warehouse. 
5.3.2 5S 
The literature review explained the 5S as being a tool that focuses on increasing efficiency 
and eliminating waste by utilizing the steps sort, straighten, shine, standardize, and sustain. 
The aim is to perform all the 5 steps in order to improve and standardize the product 
catalog.  
Sort: 
It is recommended that all outdated products should be removed from the product catalog. 
All the products in the product catalog that are no longer preferred, and no one wants to use 
should also be removed, as Interviewees 4 and 5 mentioned. This should eliminate the 
defect of an external consultant choosing a product that is outdated or no one wants to use.  
Straighten: 
It is recommended that better categories be introduced to the product catalog that would 
guide the user, as Interviewee 3 mentioned. Currently, there are vague categories in the 
DMM view of the product catalog that Veitur uses, but they are not detailed enough 
because the naming system is not efficient enough. It is possible to go to a category called 
steel bends, often called “steel elbow”, for example, and can be seen in Figure 5.9 which is 
an image from Veitur’s view of the product catalog in DMM.   
==PAGE:100==
 
Recommendations: Application of lean thinking 
Master Thesis 
89 
 
 
Figure 5.9: Product catalog in DMM 
The product catalog in Figure 5.9 is an image capture of DMM after the category “steel 
bends” was selected, steel bends are identified by the product number starting with 4011. 
These are all steel bends, but it is not possible to go into a subcategory within this category. 
A suggested solution would be to split the column called “product name” into more 
columns, that is, the degree of the bend would be in one column, the DN size would be in 
another, the radius would be in another column, and then the exact material code and 
standards of the products would have their own column. A suggested setup of these 
modifications, using products from the figure above, and created in Excel, can be seen in 
Figure 5.10.  
==PAGE:101==
 
Recommendations: Application of lean thinking 
Master Thesis 
90 
 
 
Figure 5.10: Suggested setup for the product catalog 
As can be seen, this setup offers a much clearer overview of the products and their 
attributes. It is recommended that all the columns be filled out, but this is how it looks 
based on how it is documented in DMM. This would however make it much easier to find 
products in the product catalog and every product would be assigned to the accurate 
category. It can however be seen that there is still not always enough information to make 
an educated decision on product selection, it is recommended that the standards and 
material column should always be filled.  
Shine: 
Even though the names are in Icelandic, it can be seen that they are referring to the same 
products, there is just no standard naming system for the products and how the names 
should be written. Obviously “Stál-suðubeygja”, “Stálsuðubeygja”, and “Suðubeygja stál”, 
refer to the same product. There is a discrepancy in how the size is written, and the angle is 
not always typed in the same manner. A suggestion would therefore be to implement a 
standardized naming system where there is an agreement on how product names and other 
information will be written. The suggested modifications can be seen in Figure 5.11.

Figure 5.11: Recommendation for a standardized naming system in the product catalog 
With this standardized naming system, it would be possible to filter the products by their 
angle, DN size, or standards. This would also allow products to be searched easier by name 
since the naming system would be standardized and not as chaotic as before, this would 
solve the problem regarding searching products that Interviewee 3 mentioned, and the 
products would have the same name regardless of the size of the product, which 
Interviewee 5 mentioned as being confusing. Then it should also be standardized that all the 
products have their product number included in a column before the name of the product. 
This would keep the workspace clean and make it easily identifiable if a new product enters 
the product catalog that is typed in an unorganized manner. This would make the product 
catalog cleaner and more understandable, which is something that Interviewees 3, 4, 5, 7, 
and 8 all had problems with before. 
Standardize: 
It is important to standardize doing the precious 3 steps regularly, the procedures of 
keeping the product catalog organized. If a new product enters circulation, it must be 
documented according to the standardized naming system and categorized correctly. If a 
product becomes outdated or gets replaced with another product, it should be removed from 
the product catalog.  
Sustain: 
It should become a habit for everyone involved to keep the product catalog organized and 
clean, so they can easily identify any abnormalities that might occur. It is recommended

that the management makes sure that every new employee working with the product

mentioned. The management should create instructions on the standardized naming system 
and make it available for employees to find out if they are unsure about anything. The 
management could also send out a questionnaire every few months to the employees that 
work with the product catalog, and find out their thoughts, what is going well, and what 
could be done better in order to get a feeling for the current situation and identify areas that 
could need improvement. 
The recommendations in 5S would give the external consultants and project managers more 
opportunities to filter the products to find what they want efficiently and likely reduce the 
time spent looking for products and reduce incorrect products chosen, due to the 
standardized naming system. This would solve some of the problems that Interviewees 3, 4, 
5, 7, and 8 mentioned. 
5.3.3 Andon 
As mentioned in the literature review, andon is a tool that is used to alert others in case of 
an abnormality. The aim here is, therefore, to apply andon cues to the abnormality of 
projects being cancelled, and a bill of material change, increasing the transparency for the 
purchasing department. 
Visual cues and notifications when changes occur: 
It is recommended that there should be created a tab on the purchase requests in DMM that 
displays the status of the project. Then when a project manager gets notified that a project 
is going to be delayed or cancelled, he should go into DMM where the purchase request for 
the project is located, and update the status to either delayed or cancelled. Delayed could be 
represented as yellow and show the date when the project is expected to resume, and 
cancelled as red. This would instantly, be visible for the purchasing department that 
monitors the bills of material for the projects by the color appearing in the tab in their 
overview of the bills of material, and with a pop-up notification. The purchasing 
department could then contact the supplier as soon as possible to make adjustments if 
needed. A simple illustration of this can be seen in Figure 5.12 where a column would 
appear in front of the project in the list that is monitored by the purchasing department. 
==PAGE:104==
 
Recommendations: Application of lean thinking 
Master Thesis 
93 
 
 
Figure 5.12: Andon alerts when the status of a project changes 
It is recommended that there should be another tab that could be called changes, then if a 
project manager makes changes to the bill of material for that project after it starts being 
monitored, the tab could become blue, and the purchasing department would also receive a 
pop-up notification, a simple illustration of this can be seen in Figure 5.13.  
 
Figure 5.13: Andon alerts when bills of material change 
Then when the purchasing department opens the bill of material, they can see what has 
changed, and contact the supplier if changes are needed, a simple illustration of how it 
could look can be seen in Figure 5.14.  
 
Figure 5.14: View of a bill of material after it is changed 
This would help with the issues of cancellations and changes in bills of material as 
Interviewees 1 and 6 mentioned. If products had already been ordered and cannot be 
cancelled, but the project has been cancelled or the product has been removed from the bill 
of material, then that product would go under the column “Available” as seen in the section

5.3.4 Poka-yoke 
As mentioned in the literature review, poka yoke is a tool that makes processes mistake-
proof and utilizes both control methods and warning methods. The aim here is to apply 
poka yoke to various points in the process to reduce defects from occurring. 
Standardized ordering system: 
Another recommendation is to add a new ordering system with mandatory standard 
information needing to be filled out to replace the orders that are sent to the purchasing 
department in emails, which would eliminate a lot of unnecessary emails like Interviewees 
1,2, and 6 mentioned. There would be mandatory fields that must be filled in so that the 
request can be sent. This ordering system could be programmed into DMM which is the 
current system where Veitur orders through bills of material. The recommended standard 
ordering form can be seen in Figure 5.15. 
 
Figure 5.15: Recommended standard ordering system 
By utilizing this standard ordering form instead of emails, it would eliminate the need for 
the purchasing department to send emails when they receive an ordering request through 
email that contains insufficient information. This would also allow them to have it 
documented, who ordered the products, and for what project, which is another thing that 
was lacking when receiving order requests through email. 
Notification when bills of material are about to run out on the date:
