It is recommended that 3 days before the dates assigned on the bill of material run out, if 
the project has not been documented as being finished, the project manager responsible for 
the project would receive an email and a notification in DMM that he should adjust the 
dates assigned if necessary. Interviewees 1 and 6 mentioned that project managers often 
forget to update the assigned dates which makes the bill of material stop being monitored 
and look available if someone else added the same products to another bill of material, 
which can delay the project that originally ordered the products. Making sure that the 
project managers receive notifications and update the assigned dates would reduce the 
occurrences of this happening. 
Barcode labels on products entering the warehouse: 
Interviewee 9 mentioned that only about 5% of the products that Reykjavík Energy orders 
to the warehouse contain barcodes, they often have problems documenting the products 
correctly due to insufficient labelling. It is recommended that the purchasing department 
starts a conversation with the most common suppliers, identified as “Set” and “Fagkaup” by 
Interviewee 6, and see if they can be convinced to use barcodes on all the products that they 
order in order to eliminate the incorrect documentation of products due to human error. If 
that is not possible, they could be asked to label the shipments better, so that the warehouse 
workers do not have to spend a long time trying to figure out what all the products are, and 
therefore reduce the likelihood of a product being documented incorrectly on arrival. 
5.3.5 Digital visual management 
As mentioned in the literature review, DVM is a tool that uses visual aids to increase the 
visibility of information in order to increase efficiency and reduce mistakes. The aim here 
is to introduce suggestions for DVM in various places in the process to improve the 
transparency of information. 
Bundles in product catalog: 
It is recommended that larger products that need many necessary accessory components, 
like an electrical cabinet or a fire hydrant, should be shown bundled together in the product 
catalog, which can be seen when clicking on accessory components. This would be 
beneficial for the external consultants and reduce the instances of them choosing an 
incorrect accessory component due to a lack of knowledge about the product in question, 
==PAGE:107==
 
Recommendations: Application of lean thinking 
Master Thesis 
96 
 
which was mentioned by Interviewee 7. The products should be standardized, as was 
mentioned in the standardization Chapter 5.3.1, and standardized bundles should be created 
for products that are needed regularly. The current status of creating a bill of material for a 
fire hydrant, for example, can be seen in Figure 5.16. 
 
Figure 5.16: Current situation for adding a fire hydrant to a bill of material 
In this current setup, it is easy for the external designers to make mistakes if they are not 
familiar with the product or if they are not sure about the preferences of Veitur regarding 
the accessory components, as was identified in the interviews, they might not know what 
sizes of accessories should be used with the product in question. A simple visualization of 
this recommendation mentioned can be seen in Figure 5.17. 
 
Figure 5.17: Adding a fire hydrant to a bill of material after implementing bundles 
In this recommended system that has the product name “Fire hydrant (bundle)”, the 
external consultant can be sure that when he adds this to the bill of material, it is all correct, 
since all the accessory components are standardized and preselected into the bundle. This 
would likely reduce the time that the external consultant has to browse the product catalog 
and reduce defects due to an incorrect item being chosen by the external consultant. 
Indication of unwanted products in the product catalog: 
In the 5S, it was mentioned that products that all products that are outdated or no longer 
preferred should be removed from the product catalog. If the purchasing department would

bills of material, as well as the project managers when they need to make a purchase 
request without the use of bills of material. This would allow them to have more of an 
understanding of the product, and its uses before ordering it, this would benefit them 
greatly if it were a product that they are not familiar with and would likely reduce the 
number of incorrect orders.

98 
 
It is recommended that there should be 2 additional columns in the product catalog, one 
called “In stock”, where the total quantity of that product in stock is visible, but project 
managers could also click that tab in order to see what projects those products are assigned 
to, how many are assigned to each project, and when they arrived at the warehouse. This 
could be automated, this information currently goes automatically from the warehouse 
system to Unit4 and then AGR, it should then be added that the assigned project and the 
arrival time to the warehouse also gets added to a drop-down list in DMM. This is 
something that Interviewees 3 and 4 mentioned was missing from their view and has 
resulted in Interviewee 3 accidentally stealing products for another project. The other 
column, called “Available”, that is recommended to add is one that shows the number of 
products that were linked to projects that got cancelled or if it was removed from a bill of 
material after being purchased, and the purchasing department was not able to cancel the 
order in time, even with the new andon system in place. This could also be automated when 
the purchasing department receives the andon notification that a project has been cancelled 
or a product was taken off the bill of material, the products could then be automatically 
added to the column “Available” when that happens. A simple visualization of this 
recommendation can be seen in Figure 5.20.  
 
Figure 5.20: View of available products and assigned projects in the product catalog 
The improved transparency would allow project managers to see if any products are 
available and they could therefore request those products if they need them fast, and in 
order to utilize the existing inventory, which is something that Interviewees 2, 3, 4, 8, and 9 
all mentioned. Then the cost associated with retrieving the product from the warehouse 
could be transferred from the project who ordered it, to the project it gets assigned to. This 
would be the most efficient after the products get standardized as was mentioned in the 
standardization section 5.3.1. 
Transparency about arrival times of shipments to the warehouse:    
The warehouse manager mentioned that he uploads reception documents to the purchasing 
department through a shared drive between them, it is therefore recommended that the 
==PAGE:110==
 
Recommendations: Application of lean thinking 
Master Thesis 
99 
 
purchasing department adds a document with the estimated delivery times that they get 
from the suppliers to that shared drive and update it if new information arrives. This would 
allow the warehouse to prepare itself better for the reception of products and make sure that 
the products that have been in the warehouse the longest, will be the first ones to depart, 
which will decrease the likelihood of products deteriorating since they would be stored for 
a shorter duration, as Interviewee 9 mentioned. 
Product catalog on a shared drive with external consultants: 
It is also recommended that the purchasing department should introduce a new shared 
drive, one that gets shared with the external consultants that design the bills of material. 
Interviewee 8 mentioned that it would be beneficial to have the newest product catalog 
always available. In the shared drive, there would be a live copy of the product catalog with 
all the recommendations previously mentioned. This would allow the external consultants 
to always have the newest version of the product catalog, improving their transparency 
greatly. This would likely result in fewer defects as the external consultants would instantly 
see when a product is not used anymore if preferences in products change, and if any new 
bundles get created.

were identified in the previous subchapter. Table 5.2 shows which tools reduce which 
wastes.

5.4 Pull 
As mentioned in the literature review, the pull principle is to have the customer pull the 
product through the processes. In this subsection, it will be shown how the customer pulls 
the product through the processes as opposed to the products being pushed through, it will 
also be recommended to think about customer relationships with regards to receiving the 
products on time. 
Regarding having the products pulled through the processes, Veitur currently does that for 
the most part. Interviewees 1, 2, and 6 all mentioned that the purchasing department only 
orders special products based on purchase requests that they receive. They all mentioned 
that the routine products are ordered based on a purchase suggestion generated in AGR to 
have them available in stock, but as was shown in the Veitur’s warehouse inventory 
database in Chapter 4.1 and later confirmed by Interviewee 2, the routine products are not 
identified as being the problem in this case. Interviewees 3 and 4 mentioned that the project 
managers only order products based on the actual calculated needs of the projects, 
suggesting that they do not order anything to have available in stock. The products 
therefore are currently pulled through the process by the customer. 
Standardization
- Standardized products
- Standardized procedures of checking the product catalog when creating the bill of material or ordering
- Standardize storage area outside the warehouse
5S
- Standardized naming system in the product catalog
- product catalog organized in a better way
Andon
- Visual cues when changes occur in bills of materials 
Poka yoke
- Standardized ordering system
- Notifications when bills of material are about to run out on the date
- Barcode lables on products entering the warehouse
Digital visual management
- Bundles in the product catalog
- Indication of unused products in the product catalog
- Additional details about the products in the product catalog
- Visibility of available products, assigned projects, and arrival dates in the product catalog
- Transparency about arrival times of shipments to the warehouse
- Product catalog on a shared drive with external consultants
==PAGE:112==
 
Recommendations: Application of lean thinking 
Master Thesis 
101 
 
5.4.1 Supplier relationship management 
As mentioned in the literature review, SRM can benefit an organization by categorizing 
suppliers and forming a relationship with them based on the categorization. The aim here is 
to recommend how the suppliers could be grouped, and mapped, and how improving the 
relationship with suppliers could improve the connection between the delivery times from 
suppliers and the time the customer needs the product. 
It is recommended that the suppliers in use be analyzed and arranged according to the 
categories seen in Table 5.3.  
Table 5.3: Supplier mapping (Momiwand & Shahin, 2012) 
  
Low-volume purchases 
High-volume purchases 
Critical product suppliers 
Bottleneck suppliers 
Strategic suppliers 
Non-critical product suppliers 
Non-critical suppliers 
Leverage suppliers 
Interviewee 6 identified “Set” and “Fagkaup” as the largest suppliers as previously stated, 
so they would be categorized in either of the high-volume purchases categories. The 
purchasing department is recommended to categorize all their suppliers and identify the 
most important suppliers. The next step was to look inwards and improve their own 
processes, this has been suggested in the previous lean principles. The purchasing 
department should next build a relationship with the most important suppliers, preferably 
the strategic suppliers and bottleneck suppliers, if in-house production is not possible. It is 
then recommended that the purchasing department present its key objectives, which are to 
decrease the instances of a product not having been manufactured and delivered when they 
are needed. The purchasing department could provide the selected suppliers with a shared 
drive as was suggested with the warehouse and external consultants in the digital visual 
management Chapter in 5.3.5. That shared drive could include the dates that a project 
manager has assigned to a project request as the start date of the project, increasing the 
transparency. This would increase the knowledge of the suppliers about the expected date 
that the project is needed and if any changes in those dates occur, which would allow them 
to then start on a different production, if they see that they were going to start had been 
cancelled or postponed. The results of the improved relationship should be measurable and 
it is suggested that the following KPIs will be used to track the performance: 
• On-time delivery: the percentage of on-time orders.  
==PAGE:113==
 
Recommendations: Application of lean thinking 
Master Thesis 
102 
 
• Late delivery frequency: number of orders that were delivered late. 
• Average delay time: the average time that an order was late. 
• Supplier incident rate: the number of delivery-related problems, such as incorrect or 
damaged products. 
It is recommended that the purchasing department starts tracking the metrics above before 
the relationship is formed with the suppliers, and every month afterward. It is 
recommended that they compare the metrics monthly and that they make adjustments if the 
outcome of the metrics is not good. 
5.5 Perfection 
As mentioned in the literature review, there is always room for more improvement as after 
implementing the recommendations mentioned above, new wastes will likely be exposed. 
The perfection principle is often referred to as continuous improvement and therefore, the 
aim of this subsection is to propose recommendations to make sure that the processes 
continuously improve. 
5.5.1 Kaizen 
Kaizen, as explained in the literature review is the Japanese word for continuous 
improvement and uses the tool PDCA in order to continuously improve processes. It is 
recommended that management at Veitur and Reykjavík Energy work together to go 
through the steps of the PDCA circle. 
Plan: The plan has been created in the previous principles, and the target is improving the 
warehousing/purchasing processes, increasing transparency within the supply chain, and 
reducing the inventory. It is recommended that KPIs be identified to track the progress of 
the changes. The recommended KPI’s are the following: 
• Inventory levels: The amount of tied-up capital in the warehouse. 
• Bill of material accuracy: The number of errors by external consultants which led to 
a bill of material being inaccurate. 
• Inventory utilization: The number of times a product that was marked “Available” 
in the product catalog gets utilized. 
• Product reception accuracy: The number of inaccuracies in the reception of products 
in the warehouse.  
==PAGE:114==
 
Recommendations: Application of lean thinking 
Master Thesis 
103 
 
Do: Managers at Veitur and Reykjavík Energy are recommended to implement the 
recommendations mentioned in this chapter. 
Check: Managers are recommended to analyze the KPIs that were created. 
Act: If the results of the KPI analysis are positive, then managers are recommended to 
standardize the changes that were made to the processes, start the PDCA cycle again and 
set new goals for improvements. If the results are not good, then the managers are 
recommended to start the PDCA cycle again and identify new methods to achieve their 
goals. 
 
 
 
 
==PAGE:115==
 
Discussion 
Master Thesis 
104 
 
6 Discussion 
In this chapter the project objectives that were formed in order to answer the research 
question and the sub-questions will be discussed, followed by the limitations of the 
research. The project objectives will be of assistance when answering the research question 
and the sub-questions in the conclusions. 
PO 1: Analyze the inventory at their warehouse and find ways to reduce it. 
PO 1 was performed in Chapters 4.1 and 4.2, where the inventory was analyzed, and it is 
alarming that the inventory levels have started to rise over the last years. It was identified 
which product type is mostly responsible for the products that have been in the warehouse 
for over 2 years. A sample of products was assembled from the product category mostly 
responsible for the inventory and was analyzed with the help of a quality inspector, and it 
was concluded that 12,21% of the products in that product category are deteriorated or have 
been lost. It was then identified that the inventory did not only contribute to the waste in the 
sense of monetary value, but also a waste of CO2e, and it was estimated that 13,93% of the 
CO2e used in producing the products in the same product category has been unredeemable 
lost due to the products having deteriorated or having been lost. Chapter 5 then 
recommended how lean thinking could be applied to the processes, which would likely 
result in a decrease in the inventory levels. 
PO 2: Analyze and map the current warehousing/purchasing processes. 
PO 2 was performed in Chapter 4.3.1 and was the result of interviews performed with 
individuals in the process who contribute to the products being purchased or stored. The 
process was then mapped in the same chapter, as seen in Figure 4.8, to get a better 
understanding of the processes and identify areas that could be improved.  
PO 3: Identify and eliminate the waste in the warehousing/purchasing process. 
PO 3 was started in Chapter 4.3.3 where the interviews were analyzed to identify areas in 
the process that could be improved, and the areas that came up the most were the product 
catalog, the bills of material, and the warehouse and inventory. A root cause analysis was 
then performed in Chapter 5.2 in order to find the roots as to why a product ends up 
unutilized in the warehouse. In Chapter 5.2, the wastes were categorized according to the 
==PAGE:116==
 
Discussion 
Master Thesis 
105 
 
categories of lean thinking as explained in Chapter 2.3, and recommendations of lean tools 
to implement in order to reduce or eliminate the wastes identified were presented in 
Chapter 5.3, and Chapter 5.3.6 highlights which tool reduced or eliminated which waste, 
and the benefits that come with each tool.  
PO 4: Improve transparency between different actors in the supply chain. 
PO 4 was first investigated in Chapter 4.3.3, where the interviews were analyzed. 
Interviewees mentioned examples where they do not have the transparency that they would 
deem necessary and could be improved. The transparency between different individuals in 
the supply chain was then improved with the suggestions of tools to implement in Chapter 
5. The purchasing department would then have better transparency regarding the bills of 
materials that fall out of monitoring. External consultants and project managers would have 
a better overview of what products complement each other, or are needed together, and they 
would have more information about each product, which would lead to fewer incorrect 
orders. External consultants would also have increased transparency over the product 
catalog by having the newest version always available on a shared drive. The project 
managers would also have better transparency of available products and which projects, the 
products in the warehouse belong to. The warehouse would have increased transparency 
about the shipments that are arriving and could therefore prepare better for the reception of 
the products. 
PO 5: Develop a plan to help Veitur improve its warehousing/purchasing processes. 
PO 5 was identified in Chapter 5, where the principles of lean were applied to the 
processes. The value was defined, followed by identifying the wastes and how they could 
be reduced or eliminated with the help of lean tools. Next, recommendations regarding 
supplier relationships were presented, followed by the importance of performing an 
analysis of recommended KPIs on a regular basis to track the performance over time. 
Lastly, it was recommended to keep analyzing the processes for further improvements. 
6.1 Limitations 
There are several limitations identified in the research and methods. As mentioned in the 
introduction, the scope of this research is limited to Veitur and other companies that are a 
part of the supply chain, so all the data collection will be limited to that supply chain.  
==PAGE:117==
 
Discussion 
Master Thesis 
106 
 
Time is another factor that must be mentioned as a limitation, which means that the study 
had to be completed in the timeframe set by the Technical University of Denmark. 
A limitation worthy of being mentioned is that this research was performed by one 
researcher, all the ideas and conclusions have therefore all come from the same researcher 
and the same research being conducted by multiple researchers might yield different 
recommendations.  
The number of interviews conducted can be considered a limitation, having more time or 
multiple researchers could result in more interviews taking place as the challenge of 
scheduling the interviews was a time-consuming task, as some of the interviewees have a 
strict schedule and not a lot of available time. 
 
 
 
 
 
 
 
==PAGE:118==
 
Conclusion 
Master Thesis 
107 
 
7 Conclusion 
This research is about the research question: Can the application of lean thinking principles 
and tools improve the warehousing/purchasing processes and reduce waste of the company 
Veitur Utilities in Reykjavík, Iceland?  
To answer this research question, the following sub-questions were formed, as well as the 
previously described project objectives. The project objectives helped in answering both the 
research question and the sub-questions. The sub-questions will be answered first, followed 
by the research question. 
SQ 1: What are the current challenges in Veitur’s warehousing/purchasing processes? 
SQ 1 was answered in Chapter 4.3.3 and with the help of PO 3 and PO 4. In Chapter 4.3.3, 
the interviews were analyzed in regard to the areas that could be improved. The main 
challenges were that the product catalog was unorganized, confusing, and with no standard 
naming system which led to incorrect orders being made. Transparency of the product 
catalog was also identified as a problem, with the product managers not having as much 
information available as the purchasing department, and the external consultants not having 
access to the newest version of the product catalog.  
The bills of material were identified as another challenge with the purchasing department 
not having transparency as to why bills of materials stop being monitored, or if a product 
gets removed from a bill of material. It was identified that it is challenging to utilize 
products that are in the warehouse since the products are not standardized, which leads to a 
variety of products being used. The project managers lacked the transparency to see what 
products in the warehouse were available, and what products belonged to which project. 
The problem of orders arriving through email was identified and the need to eliminate that 
from happening. 
The warehouse and inventory were identified as a challenge, with the warehouse not having 
information about when products will be arriving at the warehouse, and therefore cannot 
prepare for arrival. The problem of products going missing, and products being mishandled 
was aimed in 2 directions, some pointed toward the warehouse while others pointed toward 
the contractors. Storage space was another challenge that was identified, and there is not 
always available space in the warehouse. A problem with products staying in the warehouse 
==PAGE:119==
 
Conclusion 
Master Thesis 
108 
 
for a long period was then identified. It was lastly identified that it does happen that the 
products are not documented properly in the warehouse due to lack of knowledge and 
labelling.  
SQ 2: What is the waste in the process? 
SQ 2 was answered in Chapter 5.2 and PO 3 helped in answering this sub-question. A full 
list of the wastes can be seen in Figures 5.2, 5.3, 5.4, 5.5, 5.6, 6.7, and 5.8. 
SQ 3: What is the current status of the inventory? 
SQ 3 was answered with the help from PO 1 and in Chapter 4.1. It was seen in Chapter 4.1 
that the total inventory is valued at £8,275 million, inventory older than 2 years is valued at 
£1,582 million, and special products older than 2 years are valued at £1,426 million. This 
raised some alarm bells as it is not good that the bulk of the older inventory is specialized 
products which might be difficult to find use for in other projects. Another alarming 
discovery was the fact that the inventory had grown by 61,12%, or from £5,133 million to 
£8,275 million in the period of 2 years, from April 2021 to April 2023. 
SQ 4: What is the knowledge of lean thinking for the individuals in the 
warehousing/purchasing process? 
SQ 4 was answered in Chapter 4.3.4, and it was seen that they seem to recognize the 
method, but they could need to learn a bit more. Most of them do currently not use any lean 
tools but have similar goals as are mentioned in lean thinking. They all agreed that they 
think that implementation of lean thinking would be beneficial for their work and 
processes. It would therefore be recommended that a person with a good understanding of 
lean thinking, dedicated to guiding the implementation of lean be hired for the 
implementation to be as successful as possible. 
SQ 5: How can the lean thinking principles be applied to improve Veitur’s 
warehousing/purchasing processes? 
SQ 5 was answered with the help of PO 5, where a plan was developed in order to improve 
the warehousing/purchasing processes. The plan consists of implementing the 5 principles 
of lean and a recommendation of lean tools that could be applied, how they could be 
applied, and the benefit that is likely to follow, and can be seen in Chapter 5. 
==PAGE:120==
 
Conclusion 
Master Thesis 
109 
 
These objectives and sub-questions have all been leading to the research question which is 
the following: 
Can the application of lean thinking principles and tools improve the 
warehousing/purchasing processes and reduce waste of the company Veitur Utilities in 
Reykjavík, Iceland? 
The research conducted in this project suggests that the application of lean thinking 
principles and tools could improve the warehousing/purchasing processes and reduce waste 
at Veitur. 
Based on the analysis of the recommendations on how the implementation of lean should 
be implemented at Veitur, and the tools that could be used, it is safe to say that it is highly 
likely that implementing lean thinking to the warehousing/purchasing processes at Veitur 
will improve the warehousing/purchasing processes and reduce waste.  
The analysis showed that there currently is a lot of waste in the process, and it was 
identified how the implementation of lean thinking and tools would reduce or eliminate all 
the identified waste. It was shown that the reduction of inventory would not only result in a 
monetary benefit but also a reduction in CO2e released due to the production of the 
products. The analysis also highlighted that there currently is not much transparency 
between different actors in the supply chain and how the lean principles and tools would 
improve that transparency.  
The analysis introduced KPIs that can be used to monitor the performance after the 
implementation and the results of those measures will be the deciding factor in the next 
steps that should be taken.

Appendix C: Interview transcriptions 
C.1 – Interview 1 
Interview 1: Reykjavík Energy (5. April 2023) (duration: 01:17:46) 
Personal 
What job do you do? 
Service manager within the purchasing department, and I mainly deal with Veitur. 
How would you describe that job?  
Projects come in, tender projects, procurement projects, equipment purchases and price 
inquiries. Everything like that. I oversee distributing it to those who are supposed to solve 
those tasks. I also receive inquiries from Veitur and answer them. 
What role do you play in the purchasing process?  
I Monitor the bill of materials and material monitoring for all projects and prioritize what 
we need as soon as possible by project status. 
What are the main challenges you face in your work? 
It may not necessarily be the biggest projects, but the human factor. There are sometimes 
emails from Veitur that a product was damaged at the warehouse and that the warehouse 
delivered a ruined product. It's like that in the culture that it's all the warehouse‘s fault. I 
have taken many projects like this and looked at them in detail, in most cases it is not the 
warehouse that is to blame for the fact that the material is useless. Sometimes it happens 
that material is returned to the warehouse and the person who is supposed to review the 
material simply does not review it and returns ruined material that should not be returned. 
Then I am pointing to the inspector or the supervisor of the work who should review it 
before the return is made. Often, it happens that the vehicle that collects the product is just 
full of gravel and the worker still insists on getting the product. Sometimes material is also 
just dumped from a truck at a job site, I have seen projects where it has been caught on film 
where this has happened, but the blame was still tried to be placed on the warehouse. 
Process improvements 
How would you describe the current processes for ordering a product? 
There are documented procedures, but it is questionable whether they are always followed. 
If I take on a construction project, it is usually the project manager who makes the order 
and sends the receipt to the contractor who does the work. The contractor then sends 
someone from his side to pick up the material from the warehouse. 
Can you go step by step through the processes involved in ordering a product? (from 
receipt of purchase request) 
We receive a request to a specific email address, and we create a project in our system and 
assign it to a product manager. Usually when a request comes to us, there is an offer 
attached, but sometimes we are asked to look for prices, then we find the prices send it back 
to the person who sent the purchase request for approval. When an offer comes with the 
==PAGE:129==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
118 
 
request, an order is just made with the unit4 program and it is written out to the supplier. 
The supplier is asked to send back a confirmation of receipt of the order and an estimated 
delivery time, it is just a question of whether we will receive a confirmation back, but we 
remind them of this because we want the confirmation. Then it is maybe 6-12 weeks until 
the order arrives, and then the product manager contacts the person who requested the 
purchases and gets confirmation of what to do with the product, because often it is sent 
directly to the construction site and not to the warehouse. When we receive confirmation 
that the product has arrived, it is registered received and sold to the project it is registered 
to. 
How do you feel about the current processes? 
If everyone is tuned in to follow the processes, then it works really well. 
What do you think could be done better? 
The systems used can be simplified so that the interface is more user-friendly. When we are 
storing materials with 3rd parties, as we are doing today at Eimskip, there are certain 
accessibility issues that could be better because currently, the contractors must enter an area 
that is large and crowded. If they didn't have to drive through it with big containers, past 
forklifts and other things, it would definitely speed things up a lot. But what would most 
need to be improved is the overview of what goes into the bill of materials, the bill of 
materials is like shopping lists, you put something on it and there are parameters in DMM 
that state that it is being monitored by us, that is the validity period that it has not expired 
on the date, and the status of the project which shows that it is being monitored . It happens 
very often that we buy material, and it is not reduced in the bill of materials against the 
purchase so it looks like it still needs to be purchased. Because the bills of materials are 
reduced if something goes from the warehouse that is registered to a project or if we buy 
something that we register manually to a project. Naturally, this causes the inventory in the 
warehouse to continue to grow. This is one of the reasons that causes the inventory to grow 
and of course that process could be improved. 
Are there steps in the process that you feel are unnecessary and time-consuming? 
No, none of the steps that concern me. Project managers and inspectors are not too happy 
with the process because they think it takes too much time and it is unnecessary to be 
endlessly typing into the computer. It has not been long since we introduced the program 
DMM, which is the ordering system in Veitur, and it is a system that was placed on top of 
another system that is being used, which is called unit4. Having multiple computer systems 
creates complications as some things are only visible in one computer system. 
When a new employee joins us, especially if they were moved from within the company, 
they get very little information about the processes and other things because it is expected 
that an employee who has worked within the company for 10 years should know this 
already. There is someone who recently joined the inspection, he came from another 
department and a contractors asked for all the material written on the work, those of us who 
have been here a little longer know that the contractor is never going to collect all the 
material because he just doesn't have room in the area in order to store it. But when you are 
new and a contractor says this, you just write out all the material. But then the material is of 
course not all collected. 
What do you think are the main bottlenecks in the process? 
==PAGE:130==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
119 
 
I would say it is our lack of time. As of now, there are a lot of projects coming in, but the 
material that is needed may have a delivery time of 3,4 or 5 months from the suppliers. This 
affects the fact that the projects cannot continue as people want, and this is perhaps 
primarily due to the fact that we are going very late with the projects to tender, and 
deciding very late that we will carry out a project. It can be both internal or because we 
collaborate with others who are late with information. This is perhaps the main thing that 
could be improved in our process, that is to time schedule the projects better. 
Do you follow any standards in your work processes? 
There are of course forms for most of the work that the inspector or project manager has to 
fill out, but often it is the contractors who do it. It can be quite variable, and it would be 
clearer if this was filled in by those who are supposed to do it. 
are those standards always followed? 
No, this is often attributed to the fact that people don't feel they have time for it. 
What do you do today to constantly try to improve your work processes? 
When new managers enter the company, there are always some ideas about changes and 
there are always changes in processes and such. It is often one loud person in the cafeteria 
who speaks loudly and clearly, then maybe the new manager will realize that there is 
something very wrong and try to change it. It does not necessarily result in people starting 
to work in a different way, but the process was changed. It is often the case that those who 
have been here for a long time see that many things have been tried and they often go back 
to the same thing again because it is perhaps the closest thing to what people want to do. 
What tools and software do you rely on when it comes to purchasing and inventory 
management? 
AGR software is an inventory management system. It takes into account the sales history of 
materials classified as routine products. That is material that is usually ordered based on 
sales history, but the bills of materials also go to AGR, which are the special products. This 
program then sends the proposals, once the product managers have reviewed them, to unit4 
and from there the final order is placed with us. 
Unit4 is the system where AGR and DMM get their data from and AGR and DMM also 
send information to unit4. Unit4 then talks to the system at the warehouse. 
Are there any problems with inventory management that you think could be 
improved? 
It happens every now and then that there is a bug between these different systems, e.g. 
somewhere there is typed an extra space where there shouldn't be a space and then an error 
occurs. It would be good if there was better integration between the systems, but it would 
be best if there was only one system in use. I don't think unit4 is very user friendly. It is 
also being considered for the subsidiaries and Reykjavík Energy to introduce a new 
financial system, so it could very well happen that we get another one for the inventory. 
Maybe it would be nice if it happened that all the companies would start using it. 
Communication 
How are your relations with other parties in the supply chain?  
==PAGE:131==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
120 
 
Inspectors, project managers, designers, warehouse and suppliers. 
 
What communication method is used? 
Email is by far the most used, but then there are phone calls and meetings with direct 
communication. 
Have you encountered problems with communication with parties within the supply 
chain? 
Emails are such that it is easy to misunderstand what the person means. We are different in 
how we get articulate things. Such problems are usually just solved with a phone call. Of 
course, sometimes suppliers respond late and poorly to inquiries from us, but then it is best 
to just call the person in question. 
How is communication handled when it comes to order changes or cancellations? 
If the change is that you need to order more material, it's never really a problem. Often 
times when the problem is when we are canceling some products, I think it is often difficult 
for us to cancel. I don't know if it's because it's us because we'll pay the bill anyway when it 
arrives, or if it's really that far along in the process that the product is really getting ready. 
Sometimes it also happens that a bill of materials is monitored and an order is made and 
then it turns out that the project has been cancelled, maybe 2 months have passed since we 
ordered the material, then we usually find ourselves unable to cancel the order. 
What does it mean that a bill of material is monitored? 
Then it is active and sent to our system. We only order according to what is being 
monitored because we are ordering almost 200 million ISK and then it is impossible to 
review every product and wonder if someone has made a mistake. 
How do you feel about the transparency between the different parties in the process? 
It's kind of about knowing the system you're using, like with the bill of material. Something 
that happens a lot is the bill of material stops being monitored due to the assigned dates. 
Have you had any problems with the transparency? 
For example, I was seeing today that there are 11 fewer bills of material under monitoring 
than last weekend, which means that those projects have been canceled or that the date has 
expired. The project managers have to keep track of when the bills of material go for 
monitoring. 
what criteria do you use when it comes to choosing suppliers for products? 
Some products go to tender and then we are committed to buying from those who get the 
deal. What does not go to auction, it is the end user who chooses it. One example that I 
remember is, there are filters in intake racks in a house and the end user only wanted a 
certain filter that a certain party sells and then that is the one that is bought because the 
person who is handling the material only wants this. We still follow the legislation that if 
we are buying for a certain amount for a project, then we have to go to an open tender. 
Are the suppliers used mostly foreign or domestic? 
==PAGE:132==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
121 
 
Domestic. 15-20 years ago, there was a lot of trading with foreign suppliers, but it reduces 
our work considerably to use domestic ones due to customs and more. We still do a lot of 
business with foreign suppliers as well. 
What system do you use when it comes to keeping track of your inventory? 
AGR, unit4, some use DMM. We in purchasing do not use DMM, we use AGR for the 
inventory management as well as unit4. Those are the 2 systems we use by far the most. 
Is this a system managed by Eimskip and you have access to it or your system? 
They have a completely different system, these are our systems. Their system is connected 
to unit4. Unit4 is sent a DMM order that is made in Veitur and goes from there to the 
warehouse in the system at Eimskip.  
How often is that system updated? 
I dare not to confirm the time between the warehouse and unit4, I guess it is around 10 min. 
The time between DMM and unit4 is also around 10 min. But the transmission from unit4 
to AGR is only twice per day so if I go into AGR now, I'm basically seeing the status as it 
was at 6am this morning. But when an order proposal is made, it is just sent manually to 
unit4 from AGR. 
When did you start using these systems to keep track of your inventory? 
AGR was already in use when I started here and that was in 2016. Unit4 is even older than 
that. The warehouse has probably been using its own system since the establishment of the 
company, as it is practically a DOS environment. 
Do you check what is in stock before ordering material after a request is received? 
The products requested to be ordered are usually special products that are never available. 
If a purchase order comes to us, the product does not exist in stock and may even never 
have existed in stock. It is often the case that these are products that are only bought once. 
Did inventory and purchasing process improve after you started keeping track of this 
data? 
No, I can't say that, the inventory has just gotten bigger. What it has improved since I 
started working here is that now the questions often come up, “why do we have this?” And 
“why does this exist?” Then it is very easy for me to find in unit4 which project had 
requested certain materials. I can look up how much went into a project and sometimes 
none of the material was used. 
Do project managers have access to the systems to check if what they need is in stock? 
Yes, they see the entire stock. 
How long has Veitur had access to this data? 
It has always been to the best of my knowledge. 
Waste 
What do you think is the biggest waste in your process? 
==PAGE:133==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
122 
 
The biggest waste occurs in inventory due to disorganization. We start an order, and then it 
takes a long time for the material to be used because the project was put on hold. 
How long is the average lead time from ordering to receiving a product? 
Of course, it differentiates, but for larger products that we need to receive in advance, such 
as heating pipes, which are our biggest projects, it can take 3 months or more. Depending 
on the amount we are buying, this can go up to six months. 
Is it common for a product to be ordered that ends up not being used and it ends up in 
the warehouse for a long time? 
Fortunately, it is not common, if you take statistics about what is bought in and what gets 
left in the warehouse, it would be like 1, 2 or 3%. But when you add it all up, it still ends up 
being a big sum of cost. 
What is the most common reason for a product to end up in the warehouse for a long 
time? 
The wrong product is chosen in the bill of materials and is bought, and then it changes 
when people see that the product that was bought is not suitable, or that the project it was 
supposed to be used for is postponed. 
Do you only order what is needed each time or do you also order to have products 
ready? 
What is listed as a routine product is ordered based on the sales history of that product from 
the same month in the previous year in AGR. Of course, the usage of routine products can 
vary which can cause the stock to grow. But then just buy less next month, it should 
balance out. 
What is marked as a special product, it is bought exactly according to the bill of materials. 
Why are special products older than 2 years stored and not disposed of? 
Someone obviously has to pay for the product. Reykjavík Energy buys the products into the 
warehouse, and Veitur is then charged for inventory costs, and there is a cost associated 
with taking it from the warehouse, Reykjavík Energy is not going to cover the cost, but the 
person who ordered the product should do so. That is where the process usually strands. 
Which department would have to make the decision to throw a product out of stock in 
order to reduce inventory and free up space? 
The person who is marked as the owner of the product or the director of the relevant 
department of subsidiaries (at Veitur utilities). 
Could you envision savings by setting standards for discarding special products that 
have a certain age if it could result in being able to lease a smaller warehouse? 
I know that it is our desire to reduce the inventory in the warehouse and not to store special 
products for longer than about X months, but it always comes down to who is actually 
going to take on the costs of the product? People find it simpler to see maybe a million ISK 
a month in inventory costs than to have to shell out maybe 100 million ISK to pay to get the 
product out of the warehouse and thus lower the monthly inventory costs. 
==PAGE:134==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
123 
 
Does it often happen that a project is canceled or postponed an order for materials 
has been made? 
It has increased for us in the last few years. 
What are the reasons why it happens? 
That projects are postponed on our part due to lack of time and in order to stay within the 
yearly budget. 
How do you handle it when you need to change or cancel an order after the order has 
been placed? 
We try to cancel the purchase of materials, but it usually doesn't work because usually too 
much time has passed. It may have been 2 months since the material was ordered and it has 
not yet arrived when the project is delayed. 
What happens to the material that was ordered? 
It just goes into a warehouse and waits there. 
Is there a lot of cost involved? 
Yes, a lot a cost 
Does it sometimes happen that documents and equipment that need to be used cannot 
be found when they are needed? 
If it's a purchase project, it's stored under the ordering number in unit4, but then you need to 
know the ordering order number to look it up, and of course it can be a bit of a long way to 
figure things out. 
 
Why does that happen? 
Here we come back to the human factor, we are all different and some people are not as 
good as others in remembering to save data in the right places, other people feel like current 
processes slow them down, so they just don’t follow them. As a result, the files may not be 
where it should be. Then it takes even longer to find the documents. 
Implementation 
Do you know the methodology of lean thinking? 
I have heard it, but I have never worked with lean thinking. 
Do you use any lean thinking tools in your processes? 
We don't have a formal lean system in place. The subsidiaries have implemented this in 
certain locations. 
Would it be useful to use some of the tools of lean thinking in the processes? 
Sure, that would probably help, but first and foremost, it depends on if the people doing the 
work to be on the same page about how things should be done. Of course, it would be 
possible to make the process more convenient for us, e.g. by having a standard page for an 
order that one must fill in and have certain supporting documents that would then come to 
us in order to reduce the possibility that we receive a request where the information is not 
==PAGE:135==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
124 
 
sufficient and requires a lot of back and forth lots of emails to get all the necessary 
information. 
Environment 
Are you measuring the carbon footprint of the orders made? If so, can you describe 
how you do it? 
Not currently. There is some preparation for finding a carbon footprint on our products, but 
we don't have a complete view of it today. 
Are you trying to minimize your carbon footprint? If so, how? 
We are looking at this in some places in the corporate group. In tenders when we are 
bidding for construction works and other things, we are even giving points for people 
having environmentally friendly machines and other things like that. The points weigh 
them against the price, so we don't necessarily choose the cheapest option. 
 
 
==PAGE:136==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
125 
 
C.2 – Interview 2 
Interview 2: Reykjavík Energy (11. April 2023) (duration: 1:13:20) 
Personal 
What job do you do? 
I am the director of the purchasing department at Reykjavík Energy. 
How would you describe that job?  
I make sure that the entire purchasing department is doing what we are supposed to do, 
serving our customers. Our main tasks are the inventory management, that we do not have 
too much inventory. Communication with suppliers, both in relation to delivery times and 
invoices, it does happen that we receive incorrect deliveries or invoices. Then I also just run 
into most everything that is done inside the department. I take on all kinds of projects 
where needed. 
What role do you play in the purchasing process?  
In the purchasing process, I can take on several roles. If needed, I can participate in 
procurement activities such as tendering, ordering, and communicating with suppliers and 
customers. Additionally, if people encounter difficulties with certain aspects, I can assist 
with those as well. 
What are the main challenges you face in your work? 
It really depends on where I am positioned in the process, what challenges I face. When I 
take a step back, the main challenges today are the inventory levels, which have become 
too high. But when you dig deeper into the process, the challenges are the interactions with 
suppliers and the fact that there are not many standards in this market. There is a lack of 
consistency because we are not always working with the same product numbers from 
suppliers. People are buying different products based on what they think might work each 
time, there is no structure around what can be used, anything goes. There are so many non-
standardized products that we use. It would be more convenient for the purchasing 
department to work with more standards, so that we know what we are getting when we 
purchase a product. However, I understand that people are always trying to find the best 
solutions and the best products, which leads to us ending up with all sorts of products and 
such. 
Process improvements 
How would you describe the current processes for ordering a product? 
There are currently 2 ways in which we receive requests to order products, either through 
email or through a bill of materials. These are the requests that we receive, but we also 
monitor the routine products ourselves. 
In the email, we receive a PDF document or just text that says, "please order the following 
product from the following supplier". Then we simply need to find the supplier, check if the 
product number exists, or create one if it doesn't exist, submit a bid, place an order, and 
send it. 
==PAGE:137==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
126 
 
If it comes through a bill of materials, it is electronically transferred from project managers 
into our accounting system (Unit4) and then we review it (in AGR). For example, if you 
requested 100 units and there are 50 units in stock, then the system will suggest purchasing 
50 units. The system takes into account what is available and if this is a regular usage that 
occurs, the system may say that there are 50 units in stock, you need 100 units, and you use 
100 units in half a year, so you might order 75 units. Then you have the project 
requirements plus daily or regular usage. 
Can you go step by step through the processes involved in ordering a product? (from 
receipt of purchase request) 
There are mainly these 2 ways that requests come to us, email or bill of materials that are 
processed in DMM. The advantage of using a bill of materials is that as soon as a product is 
added to the bill of materials, there is no manual input required for the product number until 
the supplier gets the PDF document. All that process is digital between our systems. It goes 
from DMM to our accounting system (unit4), then a suggestion is generated in our backend 
system AGR, which is automatically sent back to unit4 when a purchase suggestion is 
generated, and then a purchase order is created without manual input on product numbers 
and quantities. However, we can still modify the quantity on the purchase suggestion, but 
we usually don't do that when we see that there is a bill of materials behind the suggestion. 
I have mentioned that the ideal scenario would be if the information could be transmitted 
digitally to the supplier. Now we send them the PDF and the supplier has to enter the 
product number and quantity in their system, which can result in input errors. It can happen 
that we intend to order 10 meters, but the supplier accidentally inputs one extra zero and it 
becomes 100 meters. Then I would say that I only ordered 10 meters and then we go 
through a correction process and we regularly return material to the suppliers. I think it 
happens every week that we notify the suppliers that we received materials that we did not 
order. This is the main weakness of the process not being fully digital between systems, if 
all systems would communicate with each other, it would at least reduce these human 
errors that can occur. 
How do you feel about the current processes? 
Working with a bill of materials is very good, as it is purely digital and requires minimal 
manual input. But requests that come in emails, that's all-manual input. Someone may need 
to input it somewhere, then the question is just where you want the manual input to take 
place in the process. 
What do you think could be done better? 
The current procurement process can definitely be improved, especially when it comes to 
communication with suppliers. Its best to have as much digital communication where no 
manual input is required. It would be most convenient if everyone worked with bill of 
materials, so that if someone would have a project and say, "I need this material". The 
email communication is more related to specialized products like computer equipment, 
software licenses, and there are all sorts of things that come in emails. 
Are there steps in the process that you feel are unnecessary and time-consuming? 
Yes, the process of sending orders to suppliers works like this: You create the order, 
generate a PDF document within Unit4, retrieve the PDF file there, create an email, attach 
the file, and send it to the supplier. We are aware that it would be best to be able to send the 
==PAGE:138==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
127 
 
email directly from the system (Unit4) to the supplier. It just hasn't been a priority to 
develop the system that way. Even better would be if I could send digital data to the 
supplier, so that in their sales system, it would simply display "Reykjavík energy wants 
these items in this quantity", because we have the supplier's item numbers in our data, as 
well as the quantity. Then they would just need to input the unit price and process the order. 
We're not quite there yet, but that would be the dream. As someone told me, "we can land 
on the moon, but we can't send digital orders." 
All communication with suppliers is done through emails, and we always save them, so that 
behind each order, there is a record of all communication. We try to save all 
communication we have with the supplier, so that we can trace back if there are any issues 
with permits or if someone is on leave, then someone else can take over. These are time-
consuming steps, but necessary to ensure that someone can take over if there are any 
changes. In our system, it should be possible to see all communication, but it relies on the 
fact that the party involved in the communication drags the files into the system and saves 
them. Sometimes things can be forgotten, that's the human factor. 
What do you think are the main bottlenecks in the process? 
I would maybe not call it bottleneck, it's just lead time. It's just variable, lead time for 
products can range from a day to up to a year. Whether it's bottleneck or not, I don't know. 
It's just part of the process. If you need something and you know there's a 6-month lead 
time, then you just have to place your order earlier. We did that last year, then the lead time 
started to extend a bit in delivery time. What used to be 8 weeks had gone up to 12 to 16 
weeks in lead time just due to shortage of raw materials. Then we sent messages to the 
project managers, “these items from these suppliers have been extended in lead time, you 
need to be proactive if you're planning to request them for projects”. That at least gives 
them a chance to react. I find it difficult to interpret it as bottleneck, because it's just how 
the process is, but that's mostly where we wait, this lead time for items. 
Do you follow any standards in your work processes? 
Yes, purchase orders are always generated in the same way and communication with 
suppliers is almost always the same. The purchase order is taken out of the system (unit4) 
and sent as an attachment in an email. Those processes are fairly standardized, these steps 
are pretty much always done the same way. You create the purchase order, you get it 
approved, you generate a digital document in the accounting system (unit4), retrieve this 
document and send it to the supplier. So, how it's done is quite standardized. 
are those standards always followed? 
You can't skip any steps there, because then the supplier naturally wouldn't receive 
anything and the item wouldn't be delivered. The main thing that gets forgotten is to save 
the communication with the suppliers within the purchase order. Under the purchase order, 
there can be a document library that stores the communication with the suppliers, it can be 
overlooked, it's human to forget to transfer emails into the accounting system (unit4) to 
save it under the purchase order. That sometimes gets forgotten. 
What do you do today to constantly try to improve your work processes? 
Well, there is one thing we are currently considering but it is at an initial stage. Instead of 
receiving emails, I want to create a request system where you would simply fill out a 
==PAGE:139==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
128 
 
request form stating what you want to purchase, attaching any offers from suppliers, and 
submit the request. This would generate a task list for us to work from. Instead of receiving 
requests via email that we need to input into the system and create task lists, we would 
allow the customer to input directly into the system what they want to purchase. This would 
eliminate the need for email requests and standardize the request form. There would be 
standardized information, such as who is requesting it, for whom, for what project, and 
these would be mandatory fields to fill out in order to submit the request. These would be 
called conditional fields. If you send me an email today saying, “Can you order this product 
from this suppliers”, but do not provide any project details, it would still go through to us. 
We would like to avoid chasing after additional information and make it mandatory to have 
certain fields filled out. 
What tools and software do you rely on when it comes to purchasing and inventory 
management? 
We use Unit4 for procurement and AGR for inventory management. All the basic data used 
by our systems comes from Unit4. Unit4 receives its information from the system used in 
the warehouse, which records receipts and deliveries and feeds information into Unit4. 
Are there any problems with inventory management that you think could be 
improved? 
Utilize what we have in stock better, as it often accumulates in the warehouse, products are 
ordered that end up not being used. If you break down the warehouse, you'll see that the 
problem is not related to routine products but rather these special products that are obtained 
through specific requests. That's mainly what needs to be improved in order to keep the 
value tied to the inventory as low as possible. 
Also, providing designers with a better overview of what we have in stock would be 
helpful. They could then design based on that. 
Standards would also be beneficial. For example, if you are going to do some angles and 
you need pipes of a certain size, there would be standardized angles and you wouldn't just 
be able to design whatever. We have received pipes with an 11.5 degree angle, it would be 
good if this came in specific angles and you would just work with that. It would be great to 
have maybe 5 options for which angles are used instead of saying, for example, “I need a 
pipe with a 7.3 degrees angle here”. Then we would adapt our path a bit and use the 
standardized angle instead. I believe that these standards would help us, so that we are 
always working with similar products. Then it would be much easier to use the material in 
another project if something doesn't work out in one project, because we would always be 
using the same products. 
Communication 
How are your relations with other parties in the supply chain?  
There are primarily 4 parties that we have the most communication with. That is the 
customer (Veitur), suppliers, and the warehouse, with whom we have daily communication, 
especially in terms of receiving goods and being informed if there are any discrepancies in 
quantity or which products are arriving. We also have good communication with the 
accounting department regarding payment of invoices, where we ensure that suppliers are 
paid when everything is received, or we put invoices on hold if goods are not yet received. 
==PAGE:140==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
129 
 
What communication method is used? 
The communication methods used are primarily email and phone calls with the customer, 
suppliers, and warehouse. The accounting department is located in the same building as us, 
so we usually communicate directly with them. 
Have you encountered problems with communication with parties within the supply 
chain?  
It often happens that responses are received late. The most convenient communications are 
with the warehouse and the accounting department, as we always get fast responses from 
them. Sometimes it can be difficult to get responses from the customer (Veitur). For 
example, we may be missing a project number for a project, and despite purchasing the 
material, we never received a response. In that case, we simply take a general project 
number for the department that the customer works with and record the material there. It is 
then up to them to figure out if it is not recorded correctly, and they need to make 
corrections. 
There are also occasional communication issues with suppliers, which can go back to what 
we previously discussed, as there may be errors in entering product numbers and quantities 
when the supplier is receiving an order, resulting in mistakes on their invoices. The supplier 
then sends an invoice based on what they believe they have sold, which can cause 
discrepancies on their part due to incorrect product numbers or quantities entered. This then 
causes issues with the invoices on our end. 
Sometimes, it also happens that we receive invoices for goods that have not been received, 
and the supplier is not satisfied because they have not been paid, while we are not satisfied 
because we have not received any goods. This occurs when there has been a failure in 
giving us a particular product or if the product has been received in the warehouse but not 
recorded as being received. These are some of the communication challenges that can arise. 
How is communication handled when it comes to order changes or cancellations? 
This is usually done through email or phone calls. We simply ask what can be done. We 
have encountered situations where we have ordered a large quantity of materials and 
realized that there is no need for them, and then we have conversations and sometimes they 
agree to cancel or not proceed with production. Sometimes the materials are already in 
production and we have to accept them. It's only our obligation if we have formally placed 
orders, or we only accept the part that has already been produced. Changes and 
cancellations are rare, fortunately. 
How do you feel about the transparency between the different parties in the process? 
It's not transparent enough. Our communication with suppliers is mainly through email, and 
we keep the information in our accounting system (Unit4), where we input estimated 
delivery times from the suppliers on product numbers, but that information is not visible to 
the customers who are waiting for the product. 
Have you had any problems with the transparency? 
Not directly, but project managers don't have visibility. Project managers and designers 
should be able to see this information, but I don't think the system is set up that way 
currently. They often have to contact us to inquire about delivery times, but if they had the 
==PAGE:141==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
130 
 
same view that we have on all orders, they would be able to see the estimated delivery 
times for everything. 
what criteria do you use when it comes to choosing suppliers for products? 
The customer (Veitur) chooses which supplier to trade with to some extent. 
The bill of material lists are usually for products that are similar to products that have been 
ordered before, and then suppliers are registered there. There are contracts with specific 
suppliers for specific products. Then there are other products that we purchase from 
suppliers on the market. 
Usually, for special products, if the amount is over 18.5 million ISK, it goes to tender, but 
if it falls below that, we trade directly with the supplier. However, we have requirements 
for suppliers regarding ethical rules. We check if payments are made by transparent entities 
before trading with them, we are careful not to trade with bad suppliers. Most of these 
companies that we are trading with, around 20 companies that have the majority of the 
products, are well-established companies. The companies are asked to confirm that they 
have accepted our ethical rules and work accordingly. 
Are the suppliers used mostly foreign or domestic? 
Most of our suppliers are domestic, I would say that we trade with fewer than 10 foreign 
suppliers. Recently, we counted 146 domestic suppliers that we traded with last year, of 
course, the volume varies for each supplier. Some suppliers have larger volumes, while 
others have occasional purchases that need to be sourced elsewhere. 
What system do you use when it comes to keeping track of your inventory? 
We use both Tableau reports for visualizing the data and AGR. Unit4 provides data to both 
Tableau and AGR. 
Is this a system managed by Eimskip and you have access to it or your system? 
These are all our systems. They handle receiving and tracking our inventory in their 
systems as well. We reconcile the systems, and if there are any discrepancies between ours 
and theirs, we ask them to investigate the cause. 
How often is that system updated? 
I'm not sure how often Unit4 is updated, but I do know that when I place an order, the data 
is entered into their system on the same day as it is the base system. 
AGR, I believe, is run every day, so if there is any usage happening currently, I won't see it 
until the next day. 
I think Tableau is also updated once a day. 
When did you start using these systems to keep track of your inventory? 
That was before I started working here. 
Do you check what is in stock before ordering material after a request is received? 
==PAGE:142==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
131 
 
Requests that come through the bill of material are automatically checked by AGR to see 
what is available. It must however be the exact same product number and must be in stock, 
it cannot be something similar, but precisely the same. 
However, for requests that come through email, we probably won't check unless we suspect 
that it's available at the moment. 
The only way to know if something is available is if the person requests something with the 
same product number as something that is recorded in stock. For example, if someone 
requests pipes with an 11.8-degree bend, we wouldn't see that there are tubes with a 12-
degree bend in stock because the product numbers are not the same. 
Did inventory and purchasing process improve after you started keeping track of this 
data? 
I believe people are much more aware of inventory management, people can see the 
development of the inventory visually. I think there have been improvements as a result of 
that. 
Do project managers have access to the systems to check if what they need is in stock? 
I do not know what access they have. 
How long has Veitur had access to this data? 
I do not know if they have access. 
Waste 
What do you think is the biggest waste in your process? 
I believe that the biggest waste is excessive ordering and inventory. Because what has been 
produced and purchased remains in the warehouse and creates waste. The worst thing we 
do is not utilizing it, but rather ordering something else. I think that is our biggest waste. 
How long is the average lead time from ordering to receiving a product? 
As soon as you place an order, a timestamp is generated, and when the product is received, 
another timestamp is added, so this information is available. However, we are not currently 
keeping track of this. We track the percentage of items delivered on defined delivery times. 
This percentage fluctuates between 60% to 90% on a monthly basis. 
Is it common for a product to be ordered that ends up not being used and it ends up in 
the warehouse for a long time? 
Yes, because our system does not have a mechanism for alerting us when a product is not 
going to be used, apart from the human factor. If no one communicates that the product is 
not going to be used, the system does nothing, and the product arrives in the warehouse and 
sits there without any action. If there are changes in the bill of materials or specific 
requests, there is nothing in the system that triggers the notification that the product is not 
going to be used. It would be good to know if something in the warehouse is not going to 
be used and is then available. 
What is the most common reason for a product to end up in the warehouse for a long 
time? 
==PAGE:143==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
132 
 
The reasons can vary, it could be excessive ordering, or ordering the wrong product. That 
are the main reasons. 
Do you only order what is needed each time or do you also order to have products 
ready? 
Routine products are ordered to have them ready in stock. 
Special products are only ordered for specific projects. 
Why are special products older than 2 years stored and not disposed of? 
Because if a customer requests a special product, and it needs to be returned, the customer 
has to bear all the costs. So, that is why some prefer to just store the product. 
Which department would have to make the decision to throw a product out of stock in 
order to reduce inventory and free up space? 
We would make a suggestion on which product should be disposed of, and the customer 
who ordered the product needs to approve bearing the associated costs. 
Could you envision savings by setting standards for discarding special products that 
have a certain age if it could result in being able to lease a smaller warehouse? 
Yes, there would definitely be an opportunity for savings. Ideally, we would want to use 
these products that we have to avoid waste, and it would need to be tried to use them before 
deciding to dispose of them. 
Does it often happen that a project is canceled or postponed after an order for 
materials has been made? 
It does happen, but not frequently. The main issue is what happens when a decision is made 
to cancel a project. Because there are not enough good trigger points in the system for 
information to flow to everyone who needs to know. The project manager knows that the 
project has been canceled because it is removed from the projects plan, but the information 
has not reached everyone. Then the project manager needs to let us know. 
What are the reasons why it happens? 
Collaboration with municipalities, government, and other entities. 
How do you handle it when you need to change or cancel an order after the order has 
been placed? 
It is usually just a call or send an email to the supplier. 
What happens to the material that was ordered? 
It ends up in our warehouse if we cannot return the product. 
Is there a lot of cost involved? 
Yes, it incurs both financial commitment and monthly storage costs. 
Does it sometimes happen that documents and equipment that need to be used cannot 
be found when they are needed? 
==PAGE:144==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
133 
 
It can happen, but there are not many cases that I remember. 
 
Why does that happen? 
Not answered. 
Implementation 
Do you know the methodology of lean thinking? 
I'm not using lean methodology, but I have taken several courses in process engineering, 
especially related to production and shortening communication paths. This lean thinking 
approach in the process, I'm just a little bit familiar with it. 
Do you use any lean thinking tools in your processes? 
The AGR inventory management system helps with purchasing the right amount at the 
right time. I work with the mindset of wanting to shortening communication paths and 
make things more efficient, but we're not specifically using lean thinking to do that, we're 
just tackling specific parts of the process and trying to shorten them. 
Would it be useful to use some of the tools of lean thinking in the processes? 
It would help if the party that needs information has access to the information, they need to 
streamline the supply chains. 
Environment 
Are you measuring the carbon footprint of the orders made? If so, can you describe 
how you do it? 
Our environmental department assesses the carbon footprint of products using a formula to 
calculate it based on the products. The department receives a list of everything that is 
purchased, which is categorized, and specific categories have designated carbon footprints. 
Is this some data that I could get access to? 
Yes 
Are you trying to minimize your carbon footprint? If so, how? 
We consider the environmental friendliness of products in our calculations during the 
tenders. We assign points to it in relation to the price of the product. If environmentally 
friendly machines are used, points are also assigned. This contributes to minimizing our 
carbon footprint at the same time. This way, a supplier might win the tendering process 
even if they don't necessarily have the lowest price.

Master Thesis
