C.3 – Interview 3 
Interview 3: Project manager Veitur (21. April) (duration: 1:05:11) 
Personal 
What job do you do? 
Project Manager. 
How would you describe that job?  
The job essentially revolves around overseeing the projects, ensuring that bills of materials 
are available, and that resources are ready for the projects. It involves a lot of stakeholder 
management for Veitur, and we are at the forefront of these investment projects, directly in 
contact with contractors and other suppliers. It also involves cost control, keeping data 
updated, and ensuring that work is based on accurate information. 
What role do you play in the purchasing process?  
My role is, once the project has been designed, there is a bill of material that follows the 
project or design. As project managers, we request it and are responsible for ensuring that 
the bill of material is entered into DMM and monitored, that it is monitored at the right 
time, and informing the purchasing department when the item needs to be available. Often, 
we may have a bill of material for a project that spans several years, so we inform the 
purchasing department that these may be large orders that can be moved between years. We 
act as intermediaries for information. 
What are the main challenges you face in your work? 
I would say the main challenges are overseeing the service providers who work for us and 
ensuring they deliver. There are quite a few people working for me, such as internal 
designers, consultants at engineering firms, and others. I'm requesting a lot of information 
from them, such as designs, bills of material, cost estimates, and various things, and it's 
difficult to keep track of what I have requested from each of them. It can take several days 
to receive a response. The main challenge is waiting a long time after sending an email and 
requesting something, sometimes it takes weeks to get a response to that. 
Process improvements 
Can you go step by step through the processes involved in ordering a product? (from 
getting the bill of material) 
The external consultant creates the bill of material, then we take the bill of material and 
submit it to designers for their review. They examine the drawings and bill of material to 
ensure that the correct materials are included, materials that we will be using. Once they 
enter the bill of material into DMM, we review the settings for the request that the bill of 
material is associated with. We place the work order in the correct status, and then the list 
goes into monitoring. We also need to ensure that the dates are set correctly, 90 days before 
the estimated project start date is the time when the bill of material gets automatically 
monitored for the purchasing department. They handle ordering the materials from 
suppliers and getting them delivered to the warehouse. So when the contractor starts the 
project, the materials should already be available in the warehouse. The contractor requests 
==PAGE:146==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
135 
 
the materials for the project, contacts Veitur's quality supervisor or project manager, who 
goes into DMM and writes out the order the contractor requested, and the contractor picks 
up the materials. That's the detailed step-by-step process. 
How do you feel about the current processes? 
It's like a Band-Aid solution. There's definitely room for improvement in various aspects. 
It's just so messy that we're putting ourselves in a position where we're sourcing materials 
for all the projects. 
What do you think could be done better? 
I believe that the problem would be solved if we weren't sourcing materials for the projects. 
It would then be the contractor's responsibility to source materials for the project. There is a 
tremendous hidden cost and waste involved in this setup. It's as absurd as if the government 
were stockpiling concrete for future projects. In just one project, there can be 100-200 
product numbers, and just one of these products can delay the project, and then we're stuck 
with the material. Then the project may have started, and there's something that goes wrong 
in the supply chain, like a shortage of steel or additives, or something with the 
manufacturer or supplier that results in the materials not being available for the project. We, 
as procurement, are blamed for not having the materials in the project. 
Are there steps in the process that you feel are unnecessary and time-consuming? 
The process itself is quite good. We have the bills of material, a procurement system that 
works well, good communication with the purchasing department, but our product catalog 
(AGR) is not good. The purchasing department has not updated it as we have repeatedly 
requested in recent years. The product catalog is like if you were shopping online and 
looking for jeans but only got leather jackets and gloves. The product catalog is somewhat 
chaotic and quite unreasonable in many ways. It has not improved despite our efforts to 
have the purchasing department fix it. 
What do you think are the main bottlenecks in the process? 
The review of material lists. It takes a long time to review the bills of material, and it's one 
of those emails I mentioned earlier that takes a long time. It can sometimes be challenging 
to keep track of what I have requested and follow up on it. It applies to both internal and 
external parties, the review process. Sometimes, something may not have been reviewed 
when needed, and then it needs to be pushed. It's a bottleneck if something is not available, 
if the purchasing department has not sourced the materials when needed. It can happen, and 
it does happen regularly that we don't get the materials we need. There may be delays with 
suppliers or other issues. There's so much material that we order on an annual basis, and 
there are so many projects. We're taking on a lot. There's a great deal of responsibility that 
comes with it. But I would say the review process is the main bottleneck, and of course, 
that the deliveries are on time. 
Do you follow any standards in your work processes? 
Yes, we have bills of material for each project. The standardized workflow itself is not 
complicated. Those responsible for material issuance from the warehouse have a predefined 
list and are supposed to only take out the materials that are on the bills of material. 
However, there are so many product numbers, and it's easy to make mistakes. In such cases, 
==PAGE:147==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
136 
 
they just need to check the catalog and see what is available and whether they can resolve 
the issues if something has been missed from the material lists. 
Are those standards always followed? 
I wouldn't say followed in the strictest sense, but they are followed, although exceptions are 
made when necessary. People try to be flexible. 
What do you do today to constantly try to improve your work processes? 
We are in constant development, and there have been significant organizational changes in 
the company in recent years, so we have had to constantly review and examine our work 
processes. For example, it is currently planned for the quality supervisors, which is 
responsible for material deliveries for the projects, to move between departments, shifting 
from the project department to the central units. The heat supply inspector will then be 
under the heat utility company, not us. So there will be some changes for us, we are in 
constant development. 
What tools and software do you rely on when it comes to creating a purchase request? 
We use DMM, which manages all our materials and orders in the projects. DMM 
communicates with the AGR system of the purchasing department. 
Are there any problems with inventory management that you think could be 
improved? 
Number one would be to stop sourcing materials for the projects and transfer the 
responsibility to the contractor to procure the materials, so that we wouldn't have these 
inventories, just get rid of this problem. Also, we have noticed over time that there are 
projects that are supposed to start, the bill of material list is being monitored, materials are 
being ordered to the warehouse, and then the city, for example, may cancel the project. So 
there is a significant waste there, that's the reason why we have over a billion ISK in 
inventory at the warehouse and those materials can start to deteriorate if they sit there for a 
long time. 
Communication 
How are your relations with other parties in the supply chain?  
We have extensive communication with designers, and once their work is completed, we 
need to communicate with the purchasing department. We also have communication with 
the quality supervisors, which handle material issuances from the warehouse. These are the 
main internal stakeholders we interact with. 
What communication method is used? 
With the purchasing department, we mostly communicate through our computer systems to 
convey information to them. However, if there are any deviations, we receive messages 
from them. Otherwise, we consistently use email. 
Have you encountered problems with communication with parties within the supply 
chain?  
==PAGE:148==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
137 
 
Yes, of course, it happens. People have different workloads, and sometimes we receive 
very delayed responses to emails and messages. 
Is there is often a long time between when a purchase request is made and 
when the purchasing department approves or rejects the request? 
It's not really a matter of receiving approval or rejection or any specific responses from 
them because it happens automatically. So, I don't experience any delays. I simply submit 
the bill of material list and don't think much about it unless I need to ensure that the 
materials are available in the warehouse for the project. I don't actually have an overview of 
whether my requested materials have been ordered or if they are already in stock. For 
example, I may have some DN200 pipes, and I may have multiple projects requiring the 
same size of pipes, totaling 300 pipes, with 100 pipes per project. So, I may see 100 pipes 
in the warehouse, but I don't know which project they belong to. I only see the overall 
status in the warehouse. 
How are communications conducted when it comes to changes in orders, 
cancellations, or errors in the bill of materials? 
We fix the bill of materials if it is incorrect, and often we receive comments from the 
purchasing department. 
 
Is it common for bill of materials provided by external designers to be 
inaccurate? 
Yes. 
How do you feel about the transparency between the different parties in the process? 
I don't think it's particularly great. For example, we don't see what the purchasing 
department is doing. We don't see any materials in AGR, we only see them in DMM. And I 
might see that there are pipes available, but I don't know if those are the pipes ordered for 
my project or for another project. So, my overview of that part is nonexistent. Our visibility 
into what others are doing is very limited, except maybe towards the designers because we 
send them everything they need to see. 
Have you had any problems with the transparency? 
Oh yes, I have accidentally stolen materials. The designer may have completed the design, 
but maybe something still needs to be dug up at the construction site, so the designer 
doesn't see which item are best for connections, so that item might be missing from the bill 
of materials. It has also often happened that we need certain materials now, and they might 
be available in the warehouse, but because they were not on our bill of materials, they were 
not ordered for us. However, they might be listed for another project. It can happen that the 
other project hasn't started, and the materials intended for that project are mistakenly used 
by workers in our project. We have no overview of available materials that were ordered 
for a project that has been canceled. 
What system do you use when it comes to keeping track of your inventory? 
We have DMM, but the purchasing department uses AGR. 
How often is that system updated?

I don't think there's much of a delay. We send orders, and they go simultaneously through

Do project managers have access to check whether what they need is available 
in stock? 
Yes, we can see in DMM if it's in stock, but it depends on the accuracy of the inventory

How long have you had access to this data?

Not answered. 
Do you check what is available in stock before ordering materials? 
Yes, we do. 
Do you find the database of available materials to be reliable? 
The quantity is probably accurate mainly due to the inventory counting processes at the 
warehouse, which is fairly good. However, the product catalog is not good in terms of 
setup, arrangement of the product catalog, and product names. Often, some products are 
referred to by nicknames, which have been attempted to be standardized by using supplier 
product names. It would be good if the list could be sorted by supplier product names, but 
that's not possible yet. The product catalog contains all item numbers in the warehouse. 
What do you think could be improved in the database? 
A thorough review and organization of the database and arrangement of materials are 
needed. The structure of the database needs to be changed. Currently, the products are 
arranged according to product numbers, a specific numbering system. However, no one 
except the purchasing department uses that, regular users are not concerned with item 
numbers but with product names. It's difficult for the purchasing department to change the 
product numbers because they want to maintain the sales history associated with those 
numbers. We would prefer to have it organized by product names. It is possible to search 
by product names, but you need to know exactly what the product is called by the 
manufacturer or suppliers. Therefore, the product catalog needs to be better organized, 
somewhat intuitive. For example, if you're looking for a leather jacket in an online store, 
you would choose the category "coats," then "jackets," and then select "leather jacket" 
rather than "denim jacket." So, the catalog needs to be a bit more user-friendly. There are 
many opportunities to improve this database, we just need to decide on the structure and 
organization. 
Do you find it clever to standardize checking the list before placing an order? 
Yes, it should be.

Do you keep track of when bill of materials are sent for monitoring and notify the

If something happens, and a project needs to be discontinued, then we remove the bill of

it should still be monitored. If a project is discontinued, we receive that information and 
remove the bill of materials from monitoring. 
Waste

The biggest waste in the process is continuing to acquire materials for the projects.

Through DMM or email if there are any specific comments.

They don't order the wrong materials, if there is a wrong material in the order, it's because

Is it common for a product to be ordered that ends up not being used and it ends up in

Yes.

It may simply be because we didn't have the correct information, such as incorrect

It happens regularly. There are so many product numbers and pieces that it occurs

Do you only order what is needed each time or do you also order to have

C.4 – Interview 4 
Interview 4: Project manager Veitur (24. April) (duration: 1:17:28) 
Personal 
What job do you do? 
Project Manager in construction projects 
How would you describe that job?  
We take over a formulated project from the sponsor. Or formulated, it depends how 
formulated it is, but it should be formulated, meaning it should be ready. It varies, but the 
goal is to have the project framed. We take care of getting external designers involved, 
negotiating with them, and getting them to create data for the project. We then manage the 
execution of the project, essentially overseeing the project from start to finish, until 
everything is ready, and then we hand it over with a final meeting. 
What role do you play in the purchasing process?  
Sometimes it's necessary to take timely measures regarding materials, such as when 
purchasing for a pump station and similar cases, then we need to go through a tendering 
process, which can have a long processing time, especially for large pipes, valves, or other 
significant items that are not in stock. We need to take timely action on that. Additionally, 
it is essential to monitor the design process so that the bill of materials is submitted into 
DMM for material ordering to begin. We are responsible for ensuring that material is 
always available, even though others are involved as well. We need to ensure that all dates 
are in order and keep track of material availability. If there is any material that is not 
available, which happens sometimes, we need to address the issue and try to resolve it with 
the purchasing department. Sometimes there are materials that we are waiting for, which 
haven't arrived on time, in that case, we just push the purchasing department and follow up 
accordingly. 
What are the main challenges you face in your work? 
It's all kinds. It can be either to hire a designer or to get precisely from the sponsor exactly 
what needs to be done and discuss it because sometimes the reasons for undertaking this 
project are not always clear, and those of us who have been working here a little longer 
may be questioning whether it is all necessary, just drawing attention to the fact that 
everything has surely been examined. Then, of course, designers have different levels of 
proficiency, and it's important to keep them engaged and ensure that everything is delivered 
on time, which doesn't always go well. There's just a lot to do in terms of consultancy, 
many large projects that take a long time, and it's often challenging to get hold of designers, 
they're not always readily available. Then we naturally need to invite tenders, and that's 
where the contractor comes in, who gets the job. They can vary in terms of convenience, 
both in terms of quality and communication. We just have to handle that. We also need to 
appoint a supervisor for the project, usually when the tendering process is underway, they 
have become quite scarce. They are intermediaries between contractors and us. They 
oversee the site, communicate with various stakeholders, and take care of security issues on 
site. When the supervisor is competent, the project goes much smoother than when they 
lack the appropriate knowledge. 
==PAGE:154==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
143 
 
Process improvements 
Can you go step by step through the processes involved in ordering a product? (from 
getting the bill of material) 
It actually all goes through DMM. However, it's been a while since I ordered special 
products, like larger pipes and such. But if you don't have a product number, then it goes 
through email as well, through phone calls and other means. But the system that manages 
material procurement is DMM. You specify the materials you need and set the time when 
the material needs to be available, then it's up to the purchasing department to decide when 
to purchase the item. Because, of course, we don't want to be stuck with some materials for 
months. 
How do you feel about the current processes? 
Sometimes it's just fine, for something very basic, like commonly used materials that are 
always available, it goes smoothly. It's not everything that goes wrong, but there are too 
many deviations. Then there's also the description of the materials in the product catalog, 
you should be able to right-click and get attachments with information, sometimes it's there, 
but sometimes it's not, and sometimes the description is just a single image or some useless 
information. It needs to precisely explain which materials are suitable for each situation. 
What do you think could be done better? 
The product catalog (AGR), it has been talked about since I started working here, almost 20 
years ago. There was a workshop held about it probably 10 years ago, talking about a new 
product catalog, our current product catalog is not serving its purpose, not at all. It's just 
very chaotic, making it difficult for those who don't know the materials precisely to find 
anything in it. The layout is often illogical, and materials are not necessarily grouped 
together in a way that "if you order this, you must have this". Both meters and piece counts 
are used depending on the product, and people have made all sorts of mistakes because of 
that, accidentally purchasing materials for several million ISK when it should have been 
only around 100 thousand ISK. I'm not an expert in the product catalogs, but it's not 
functioning well. So, you get the product catalog for the designer out in the field, and they 
choose materials based on the information in the product catalog, but it can be wrong. 
That's why the bills of materials are often faulty because the designer only has poor 
information to work with. The system is just poor, which means it's difficult to work with, 
for all parties involved, whether it's you or external parties who also need to work with it. 
Are there steps in the process that you feel are unnecessary and time-consuming? 
Actually, there's nothing complicated about entering bills of materials into DMM, it's been 
reasonably streamlined. But the system itself, the product catalog, it's just unclear. It's often 
unclear what you have at any given time. And then there's the question about roles, what is 
the role of the purchasing department? Is it just to sit, get some product numbers, and place 
orders without any thought? What's the purpose, for example, of attending product 
exhibitions? I've often wondered about that. We don't attend product exhibitions, I think we 
rather belong there. 
What do you think are the main bottlenecks in the process? 
==PAGE:155==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
144 
 
Some things just go wrong, that's just how it is, I don't know why. I'm only speaking for 
myself, but there are often many suppliers who can provide the same product. Why are we 
dealing with a supplier who claims to deliver something in October 2022, and it's now 
April 2023 and only part of the order has arrived? Why are we doing business with this 
supplier, for what purpose? I never get proper answers There are all sorts of things that we 
have no control over, and we have often pointed out that there are others selling similar 
products or items. How about talking to them? Is this something we are doing wrong, do 
we need to define in detail what we want? There is no specific discussion within our group. 
I believe the purchasing department should be an expert in procurement, at least, that's how

whether we should be the ones purchasing all these materials ourselves at all, that's another

Do you follow any standards in your work processes? 
We don't have many standards, but we always enter the bills of materials into DMM. 
Are those standards always followed? 
Not answered. 
What do you do today to constantly try to improve your work processes? 
There hasn't really been much focus on it lately. People here are constantly changing, and 
so much experience and knowledge are lost. Often, individuals are trying to reinvent the 
wheel, starting anew because they simply don't know better. There used to be productive 
discussions between Veitur and the purchasing department, with someone from the 
department regularly present at meetings to address issues, improve coordination, and be 
close to us. At one point, we had made good progress, and there were weekly meetings 
between representatives of the purchasing department and Veitur, where things were being 
reviewed and refined. But with the arrival of new people, somewhere along the line, this 
fell apart. I can't exactly tell you when it happened, but at least there is nothing formal 
going on right now. This is important to ensure that everyone is not shouting from different 
corners. We have also lost valuable employees on the other side and brought in new people 
who may be just starting out and may not have received information from those who left. 
It's difficult for people to come into such circumstances. 
What tools and software do you rely on when it comes to creating a purchase request? 
We use DMM, email, and phone calls as well. If there is a complex request, it can also be 
discussed in a meeting. 
Are there any problems with inventory management that you think could be 
improved? 
Plenty of them. Not all materials go into the warehouse, often, large pipes are ordered from 
“Set” and just stored there. We often need to store pipes somewhere, and at one point, the 
purchasing department started pushing us to see if it was possible to take the materials 
directly to the worksite, even when we were still in the process of applying for permits 
from the municipality and didn't have a worksite yet. Sometimes, there is simply no space 
available to store these huge pipes. We encountered this issue before, and it still happens, 
where we receive materials months before we need them. Once we receive them, we

become responsible for them, even though the contractor may not have arrived on the site.

Communication 
How are your relations with other parties in the supply chain?  
Naturally, the purchasing department at Reykjavik Energy handles the purchasing, while 
the designers are responsible for designing the materials and checking if they meet the 
requirements. Then there is the sponsor. 
What communication method is used? 
We submit procurement requests through DMM, but we also frequently use email or make 
phone calls. 
Have you encountered problems with communication with parties within the supply 
chain?  
Yes, that has definitely happened. 
Is there is often a long time between when a purchase request is made and when the 
purchasing department approves or rejects the request? 
If it goes through DMM, it's not something you track. You just need to enter the correct 
date. We input the date for when we want the material to arrive and another date for when 
we plan on being done using it. Sometimes delays occur, and you end up using the material 
later. If you don't update the date and it has expired, it may appear as if there is available 
material in the warehouse that someone else sees and takes for another project. Then two 
parties end up reserving the same material. 
How are communications conducted when it comes to changes in orders, 
cancellations, or errors in the bill of materials? 
In such cases, you simply need to update the bill of materials if you know what needs to be 
corrected. 
 
Is it common for bill of materials provided by external designers to be 
inaccurate? 
Yes, it happens sometimes. They may not have been thoroughly reviewed. It also occurs 
because the product catalog is not reliable. It's difficult for the designers to interpret the 
information. The product descriptions are often misleading, and there may be product 
numbers in the catalog for materials that are outdated and no longer in use. If you don't 
want a certain material to be used, why is it still in the product catalog? 
How do you feel about the transparency between the different parties in the process? 
I feel that there isn't enough communication between the parties in the process, and it's not 
clear enough what is expected from each individual. I, for instance, sometimes just feel like 
picking up the phone and buying the material myself, and some people have actually done 
that. However, it's not within our workflow to purchase materials directly, we can only 
make requests, and it naturally goes through the purchasing department.

Have you had any problems with the transparency?

No, maybe it's just ignorance sometimes, but the old system was heavily patched, and many

ordering an item and it doesn't have a product number, you simply have to request it,

Do you check what is available in stock before ordering materials?

C.5 – Interview 5 
Interview 5: Internal designer Veitur (2. May 2023) (duration: 00:33:16) 
Personal 
What job do you do? 
I have been a designer for a year and a half, but I am transitioning to the project 
management team. Before that, I worked in an engineering office and often served as a 
external consultant for Veitur. 
How would you describe that job?  
We are not designing in-house as it currently stands, so sometimes we work on project 
assumptions with sponsors and external consultants. We then follow the project during the 
design phase with external consultants, attend design meetings, and review the design. We 
review all tendering documents, drawings, and bill of materials, and input the bill of 
materials into DMM. 
What are the main challenges you face in your work? 
There are various challenges. I often find it difficult to understand the product catalog. 
External consultants only receive an Excel file from DMM, which is often unorganized and 
can be quite messy. It is set up in a way that makes it easy to confuse items. Sometimes 
there is a piece that is longer than the standard length, and it is accidentally entered and it 
can be difficult to notice it. Sometimes I end up with a piece that cannot be used, and it just 
ends up in the warehouse. The main challenge is the product catalog, that's where the 
biggest challenge lies. Additionally, there are instances where material needs to be 
replaced, and searching for it can be quite a nightmare. There may be a component that can 
have two different names if it comes in two different sizes, so the product catalog needs to 
be worked on to ensure that orders will be accurate. 
Process improvements 
What is the process for reviewing the bill of materials? 
We mainly review the bill of materials, go through them, make changes if necessary, add 
and remove materials. 
Can you go step by step through the process involved in your work? 
It's not a direct process, we simply receive the bill of materials and go through them. I 
check if the list matches the drawings I have reviewed. Then I enter the bill of materials 
into DMM. 
If we receive a tender package, it usually includes the tender description, drawings, bill of 
materials, and likely everything in the package. Sometimes there is a lot to do, and it has to 
wait, but we allocate around 2 weeks to review everything. We give ourselves that time. 
A project doesn't go out for tendering until we have approved the tendering drawings. We 
have been involved in the design process, attending design meetings until the review 
begins. So, all assumptions and everything should be included, but there is always 
something that needs to be addressed during the review. 
==PAGE:163==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
152 
 
Is there anything in the process that could be done better? 
Not answered. 
Are there steps in the process that you feel are unnecessary and time-consuming? 
Email communication takes up a lot of time, you need to keep track of all email 
communications. 
What do you think are the main bottlenecks in the process? 
There are not so many bottlenecks. It's just challenging to keep track of all the inputs from 
everyone involved in the design. 
Do external consultants always have the necessary information required for 
designing? If not, why not? 
Based on the design meetings we attend with them, they should have all the information, 
but they also often call and ask about something that is unclear. It's just part of our job, they 
have access to us if there is something missing. 
Do you follow any standards in your work processes? 
Naturally, we have design guidelines that we want to be followed, both in appearance, 
materials, and drawing layout. 
Are those standards always followed? 
Yes, this is the standard way we want things to be done. Consultants need to calculate and 
design, they need to decide on size for pipes and other things. but we have the methodology 
in the design guidelines that they follow. 
What do you do today to constantly try to improve your work processes? 
We have been working on improving the review process, aiming to better manage all the 
documents. We have a vague idea for a software where the consultant could submit the 
tendering package, and we would review it within the system. The consultant would receive 
notifications about comments that they could address or update. This way, we would have a 
history of all versions of the review. Everything would be within the same system, which is 
something we would like to use for reviewing projects. It would reduce the need to rely on 
email or MS teams communication, and it would be beneficial to have all comments in one 
place. It would also make it easier for other designers to take over a project in case of 
absence, as the communication history would not be confined to a specific person's email. 
How do you ensure the accuracy of the bill of materials? 
We rely on design meetings to go over the assumptions for the design, ensuring they are on 
the right track and identifying any necessary changes. This way, we can see the status 
before the package comes in for review and make sure everything is in order. Ideally, we 
prefer not to create the bill of materials until the entire process is completed. The 
consultants would then create the bill of materials based on the latest valid design, so the 
designers wouldn't have to constantly update them if any assumptions change. We always 
want to receive the final version. 
==PAGE:164==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
153 
 
Do you find it clever if the design had to be done within certain material constraints to 
only use standardized materials that would be easier to recycle if something went 
wrong? 
We would prefer that. We would like to use standard units in bends, for example. We prefer 
not to have extensive customization because it often happens that you have something 
custom-made, and then something changes, and you no longer need it, but you still have it 
in stock until it's discarded or repurposed. That's why we would rather use standard bends 
because if you don't use them, you can easily use them in another project. 
Communication 
How are your relations with other parties in the supply chain?  
We have extensive communication with consultants, and we work alongside project 
managers. We also communicate with the purchasing department when we submit the bill 
of materials, and sometimes there are missing product numbers, so new product numbers 
need to be created. 
What communication method is used? 
Usually emails. 
Have you encountered problems with communication with parties within the supply 
chain?  
That does not happen often. However, we used to send emails directly to individuals in the 
purchasing department, and suddenly we received information that there was an email 
address for the entire purchasing department. It could easily get lost if you sent the email 
directly to a specific person. I experienced this when I needed a specific product number, 
and I never received a response because the email got lost in someone's mailbox. But if I 
had sent it to the purchasing department's email, it would have been treated as a task and 
resolved sooner. 
How do you feel about the transparency between the different parties in the process? 
When I worked as an external consultant, we always had access to project managers and 
designers whom we needed to collaborate with. I found the product catalog to be a 
complete disaster when I first received it. As an external consultant, when I was about to 
create a bill of materials, I received the catalog, and I looked at it thinking, "What on earth 
is this?" It was just a bunch of random information, and it took me a long time to figure out 
how to navigate through it. 
Is it common for you to not have sufficient data to design the bill of materials? 
No, we usually had enough data. There was a man who used to work with Veitur, who has 
now quit. He knew all the production sites really well and I could always call him if I had 
any questions. 
Do you have information about which items are available in stock when creating the 
bill of materials in order to potentially reuse those materials? 
Well, I don't see that until I submit the bill of materials. Then I can see what is in stock. But 
I can see it in DMM if I look the specific product up, then I can see the quantity in stock of 
==PAGE:165==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
154 
 
the product that is on the bill of material. But I can't see if the item is available or not. The 
other day, I submitted a bill of materials for a project on February 7th, and another project 
manager had an active bill of materials with the same item, but he didn't pay attention to the 
date on the bill and his bill expired on February 1st. Then it looked like there were two 
valves available for my project, so there was no need to order them because they seemed to 
be in stock. So, they weren't ordered because they looked like they were available. Then on 
February 28th, someone took out the valves for the other project, and the following week, 
someone looked at it and realized that my materials were never ordered and were no longer 
available. It caused a delay in my project, and I needed them urgently. I need them 
connected by next Thursday. 
 
How long have you had that information? 
I don't know, I've only been working here for a year and a half. 
Do you think it's a good idea to check what is available in stock in order to be able to 
use those items in the design? 
It might not be a bad idea, but then it must be easy to see what's available. 
Waste 
How often does it happen that the bill of materials is incorrect? 
It definitely happens, but it probably would not be so different to what was actually used. 
 
Why does it happen? 
Naturally, during the construction phase when the ditch is opened up, there might be 
something there that you didn't anticipate. Then you might need to use different fittings and 
connections to work around it. Then you can end up with unused material and different 
material needs to be ordered. 
 
How do you try to prevent it from happening? 
It's through a review. For example, there's are some items that consultants often don't input 
correctly. The product catalog can be a bit confusing, and there are fittings included in the 
catalog that we don't want to use, but they often end up on the bill of materials. So, one 
needs to be awake, If I notice it, I simply remove them from the bill and add the appropriate 
fittings instead. These are fittings from one company, but the ones working on the project 
prefer to use fittings from another company. No one wants to use these fittings. The 
consultant, for example, may not be aware of this and doesn't distinguish between the 
fittings, which is why the wrong ones often end up on the bill of materials. I would prefer 
to have those fittings removed from the product catalog.

C.6 – Interview 6 
Interview 6: Reykjavík Energy (12. May 2023) (duration: 00:57:40) 
Personal 
What job do you do? 
I am a service manager for purchasing. 
How would you describe that job?  
My colleague and I divide the responsibilities between us. I handle the parent company, ON 
Power and CarbFix, while the other one takes care of Veitur and Reykjavík Fibre. Although 
our projects intersect to some extent and we try to assist each other, but we primarily focus 
on our respective companies. 
What role do you play in the purchasing process?  
I am more involved in tenders, contracts, and consulting. I also oversee procurement 
analysis, where I review all the company's procurement activities once a year. I examine 
the proportion of tenders, direct purchases, and if there's anything unusual, I investigate it. I 
discuss this with the chief operations manager, go over the objectives, propose 
improvements, and eventually present it to the management. 
Process improvements 
Can you go step by step through the processes involved in ordering a product? (from 
receipt of purchase request) 
It can happen that an email is sent regarding the purchase of a product, which we would call 
an incidental purchase. In such cases, a project is established, and we allocate the project 
based on which subsidiary the request came from, incorporating it into the purchasing 
process. If it's a straightforward incidental purchase where only an order needs to be placed, 
we allocate the order to the department responsible for the request. That department 
receives an email describing what is needed and places the order accordingly. Then, they 
make arrangements based on whether the item should be delivered to the warehouse or 
directly to the worksite. If it's to be sent to the warehouse, the person overseeing it ensures 
the item arrives and is received at the warehouse. Once that is done, they close the project. 
If the delivery is to be made directly to the worksite, it usually goes through the reception at 
Veitur, and the recipient confirms the receipt and informs where the item should go. 
For routine products, a purchasing proposal is generated through the AGR system, based on 
the usage in previous years and what is recorded on the bill of materials. If the proposal 
suggests ordering a large quantity or if the items are expensive, we still review the proposal 
and assess whether the period targeted by AGR aligns with a period of unusually high 
usage of the item being ordered. In such cases. These items are usually sent to the 
warehouse. 
Special products are usually ordered based on bills of material, and they are either delivered 
to the warehouse or the worksite. Once we receive notification that the item has been 
received, we inform the person who placed the order that it has arrived. We do not track 
whether the person who placed the order retrieves it from the warehouse. If it's not 
==PAGE:167==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
156 
 
collected, it remains in the warehouse, and when the material list is removed from 
monitoring, the item becomes available for others to use in different projects. One problem 
with the bills of material is that project managers are not diligent enough in updating the 
dates on the lists according to the actual scheduling of the project. Therefore, there may be 
instances where certain items were ordered for a specific project, and then a new bill of 
material is issued by another project manager requesting the same item. The system 
indicates that the item is in stock and available. The other project manager may retrieve the 
item, making it no longer available for the original requester, which delays the project. This 
is the issue we're currently facing, and it's quite unfortunate. 
How do you feel about the current processes? 
The purchasing processes are quite good, but there are areas that could definitely be 
improved. 
What do you think could be done better? 
For example, it would be beneficial for people to be well informed about what needs to be 
done and how they should participate in the purchasing process. Sometimes, we engage in 
large purchases, and it is stated that a requested item will be included in the bill of material 
list when it is ready, but then that item may never actually be added to the list. In such 
cases, we cannot see why the item was requested and who requested it. That is why it 
should be recorded in the bill of material list. 
Are there steps in the process that you feel are unnecessary and time-consuming? 
I don't know for sure, but generally, the more precise everything is, the better, even though 
it usually takes more time. So, I would say that things could be made even more precise, 
and project managers should adhere to those processes to ensure that the ordered items are 
actually requested and collected from the warehouse, thereby avoiding the accumulation of 
special products in the warehouse. 
What do you do today to constantly try to improve your work processes? 
We try to organize training courses related to the purchasing strategy and purchasing rules. 
We also go through the purchasing process to some extent, where I address the process in 
terms of when the need for purchases arises and what the next steps should be based on the 
characteristics of the order. We often receive inquiries regarding the DMM system, even 
though we don't use it extensively. People often turn to us if they encounter difficulties with 
DMM instead of contacting the technical service. 
What tools and software do you rely on when it comes to purchasing and inventory 
management? 
We use AGR and then there's Unit4, which is the inventory, purchasing, and financial 
system. Unit4 is a centralized system, and all other systems retrieve data from it. 
Are there any problems with inventory management that you think could be 
improved? 
One thing that happens is that bills of material are created before the design is fully 
completed, and then something changes, and they modify the bills of material. This means 
that an item that was initially deemed necessary and ordered may no longer be needed. We 
==PAGE:168==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
157 
 
don't receive any notification when bills of material are changed. For example, if an item is 
removed from the bill of material, there's nothing in the system to inform us that it has 
occurred, and that item might still be ordered. So that item arrives at the warehouse, and it 
becomes evident that no one is expecting it, and it has been ordered for no reason. This 
happens very often. This may be more of an issue with special products because, with 
routine products, we know they will eventually be used. However, with special products, 
which are sometimes custom made, it's rarely possible to return them. One example is a 
large project where isolated pipes were ordered for 20 million ISK, and then there was a 
change in the project to use wider pipes, and the material list was modified, but the 
purchasing department was not notified. Then the material arrived, and we informed the 
project manager, only to find out that they had were not going to use that size. This is a 
very uncomfortable situation, and we have to store the pipes at the warehouse, hoping that 
someone will need that size later on. It would be very helpful if there was a system that 
notified us when changes are made to the material lists. It would greatly assist when items 
are being removed from the lists, but it's not a big issue when items are added to the lists 
since they will be considered in the next order. 
Communication 
How are your relations with other parties in the supply chain?  
There are many of them. Of course, there's the warehouse. Then there are suppliers, with 
various contacts there. Within the subsidiaries, it's mostly project managers, especially 
when it comes to purchasing goods or project execution, and it varies depending on who is 
involved in each project. Otherwise, there are many others who have interactions with the 
purchasing department. 
What communication method is used? 
A lot of communication happens through email, especially when it comes to ordering 
goods, requests come through email. Or requests for tenders, those are also via email. This 
then goes into our system, where a project is created, and it's either allocated or we handle 
the work ourselves. 
Have you encountered problems with communication with parties within the supply 
chain? 
Yes, sometimes people take a long time to respond to emails. It depends on the season, 
there's often a lot going on for everyone in spring when all the construction projects are 
being planned. Then everyone takes longer to respond, including myself, of course. 
How is communication handled when it comes to order changes or cancellations? 
If there's a need to change an order, it can involve additions or reductions in materials.  
Additions are usually easier in the sense that suppliers rarely say no if we want to order 
more from them, but it might affect the delivery time, depending on the nature of the item.  
Cancellations can be more difficult, especially if it's a special product that has already 
entered production. Then it's often not possible to cancel. The riskiest situation is when a 
project manager realizes they have ordered something they don't anticipate using, and they 
forget to inform the purchasing department so that we could cancel it. We have often 
==PAGE:169==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
158 
 
encountered situations where they let us know, but it's already late, so we have to accept the 
item. 
How do you feel about the transparency between the different parties in the process? 
It can vary greatly. I feel that there is a lack of education about the system and how people 
should conduct themselves. I often find that when new employees join the company, they 
are thrown into the deep end and expected to figure things out on their own. Someone 
might say, "Just contact the purchasing department," without showing them how the system 
works and what the process should be. I believe it would simplify things for many if new 
employees went through training courses before they started doing anything else. 
What criteria do you use when it comes to choosing suppliers for products? 
It depends on what we're buying, whether we have a contract with the supplier or not, and 
the cost of the products. If the value of the goods exceeds certain financial limits, we must 
go through a tendering process. Then we decide what we're going to purchase and 
announce how we're going to select the supplier. It could be based on price alone, or price 
and delivery time, carbon footprint, and various other factors. There are different factors 
that determine how we choose a supplier for a particular product. 
Are the suppliers used mostly foreign or domestic? 
Our largest suppliers are domestic. "Set" and "Fagkaup" are our largest suppliers. They 
have the widest range of products and, as a result, they have become the biggest suppliers. 
Set handles pipe materials, while Fagkaup deals with cables, voltage, and electrical junction 
boxes. 
Waste 
What do you think is the biggest waste in your process? 
Regarding time, there can be all kinds of waste, everything takes time. For example, if 
someone requests something to be ordered and we place the order, then it can happen that 
the invoice is sent to one of the subsidiary companies within the group. This can happen 
when the person in contact with the supplier is, for example, an employee of Veitur 
explaining what they want, and the supplier enters the order under Veitur, but we at 
Reykjavík Energy are the ones purchasing the product, yet the invoice is sent to Veitur. If 
the invoice is then approved, then everything needs to be reversed in the system to ensure 
things go the right way. This happens quite often. 
Regarding material purchases, waste occurs when we have bought a material that was on 
the bill of material list but later removed from the list without notifying us. This results in 
us wasting a lot of money on a product that may never be used or will sit unused for many 
years or even indefinitely. The material can then end up deteriorating due to long storage 
times. 
Is it common for a product to be ordered that ends up not being used and it ends up in 
the warehouse for a long time? 
We don't really have statistics on that, but what we have noticed is mostly when products 
that don't go to the warehouse directly but go straight to the workshop. Then the project 
manager might say they don't need the material when it arrives. But if it's a product that is 
==PAGE:170==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
159 
 
supposed to go to the warehouse, it just goes there and sits there, and nobody knows about 
it. 
What is the most common reason for a product to end up in the warehouse for a long 
time? 
When the project manager makes changes to the bills of material without informing the 
purchasing department because there is no system in place to notify us when it happens. 
There needs to be something in the system to notify us, so that it is not just based on human 
factors, especially when it comes to special products. 
Why are special products older than 2 years stored and not disposed of? 
Products are assigned to owners of the product, and when products are purchased, 
regardless of the type of product, the respective owner needs to pay for it. Often, that's 
where it stops. When we have had a product for a long time and inquire about what to do 
with it, we often receive responses that we can dispose of it. But when we ask for a project 
number to assign the cost, we often don't receive any response or are told to keep it. They 
don't prioritize disposal because it can be expensive. I think that's where it gets stuck. 
Which department would have to make the decision to throw a product out of stock in 
order to reduce inventory and free up space? 
The decision would have to be made by the person assigned as the owner of the product. 
Implementation 
Do you know the methodology of lean thinking? 
To some extent. 
Do you use any lean thinking tools in your processes? 
No, not as far as I know. 
Would it be useful to use some of the tools of lean thinking in the processes? 
Possibly, I think it would be worth exploring. It would be good to have visibility when 
something is removed from the bills of material and track the changes. The system captures 
it when something is added to the inventory list and generates a purchase suggestion, but it 
doesn't capture when a product is removed from the list. I believe it would help eliminate 
unnecessary orders and greatly contribute to reducing inventory accumulation. 
Environment 
Are you measuring the carbon footprint of the orders made? If so, can you describe 
how you do it? 
No, we haven't reached that point yet. 
Are you trying to minimize your carbon footprint? If so, how? 
We request carbon footprint information from suppliers, but most suppliers haven't made 
significant progress in this area. We don't have all the necessary information. It hasn't 
become widespread for manufacturers to be advanced in these matters. We aim to keep our 
carbon footprint low, it's actually part of our strategic initiative to reduce it.

C.7 – Interview 7 
Interview 7: Mannvit (15. May 2023) (duration: 0:43:17) 
Personal 
What job do you do? 
I am a consultant for Veitur here at "Mannvit". 
How would you describe that job?  
I work on various projects related to Veitur, mainly focusing on the district heating, 
wastewater, and water supply systems. I don't work much on the electricity distribution side 
of things. 
What role do you play in Veitur’s projects?  
I am an external consultant, and sometimes I act as the project manager for projects that we 
either won through bidding or under a framework agreement. Sometimes I work as a 
subcontractor under other project managers, it is a mixed role. I mostly have my own 
projects but also work with others on theirs. 
What are the main challenges you face in your work? 
There are many things that are good, but there are some things that might be done better. 
Veitur has project managers who manage projects in quite different ways. I have been 
fortunate to work with very good project managers from Veitur, but I have also worked 
with project managers who are less organized and attentive to their projects than the ones I 
work with the most. Communication is generally good, and a few years ago, there was a 
significant improvement when Veitur provided design guidelines for us external 
consultants. That happened about five years ago, and it has been excellent since those 
guidelines were established. Of course, there are always things that can be criticized, but 
overall, it has been a great development. It simplifies the work for all parties involved, both 
external consultants and Veitur's staff. Material issues are always difficult, as they affect 
many aspects. For example, there was a major street repair project downtown five years 
ago, and everyone was frustrated because the project was delayed. The main reason for the 
project delay was due to material-related issues, there was a shortage of materials. So, 
material management is a significant part of Veitur's projects. It is crucial to determine the 
required materials and order them on time. 
Another challenge is lead time. I am currently working on a project where we want to use 
DN800 ductile pipes (80 cm diameter), and the lead time for those pipes can be several 
months. If the bill of material list is not correct, for example, if the consultant doesn't 
provide an accurate bill of material or if the design requirements change after the ground 
has been excavated, Veitur can face significant difficulties with the project. I have been 
involved in projects where large materials needed to be ordered from abroad, and it can cost 
millions to import two large pieces. Assuming they are available from a supplier, and if not, 
then they need to be custom made. So, these material issues are crucial in the larger 
context. 
The bills of material are also quite complex, and some designers sitting in their offices with 
limited practical experience sometimes struggle to determine which materials need to be 
==PAGE:172==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
161 
 
included when other materials are ordered. We receive a product catalog from Reykjavik 
Energy, and it requires thorough review. Let's just say I'm being very polite here. 
Additionally, if you want to include a fire hydrant in the material list, there might be around 
10-15 items that need to be remembered to add as well. It includes bolts, loose flanges, 
flange gaskets, and all sorts of items that are almost impossible to know unless you are 
either very familiar with them or Veitur has provided us with instructions. However, there 
is still some work to be done to finalize those instructions. But when it comes to fire 
hydrants, there should simply be one item in the product catalog called "fire hydrant, 1 
piece." Then all the accompanying parts needed for one fire hydrant would be included in 
the order. That's something that is lacking. 
Process improvements 
Can you go step by step through the process involved in your work? 
If we are going to design a utility system, after a contract has been established based on the 
framework agreement or after a public tender, we receive data from Veitur and go out to 
measure the site using GPS if necessary. Then we begin the design process. Among other 
things, we prepare drawings and a tendering document, which is a file with the volume 
needed and is not the same as the bill of materials, along with a project description. Once 
we have completed these three components, we submit them to Veitur for review. In the 
subsequent phase, we refine the bill of materials based on feedback from Veitur. We 
establish the necessary prerequisites and identify any changes that need to be made, and 
then we finalize the bill of materials. We accomplish this in two ways, we create a bill of 
material list in Excel based on Veitur's product catalog, and we also incorporate the bill of 
materials into the drawings. We then submit this to Veitur, and they input the bill of 
materials into their system and order materials accordingly. This is essentially the process 
in a nutshell. 
 
Is there anything in the process that could be done better? 
In many respects, the process is quite clear in terms of what we need to do. However, not 
long ago, Veitur started requesting the bill of materials to be included directly on the 
drawings in addition to the Excel file. 
Here he shows me a bill of material for a project that he has. 
You can see the product number from Veitur's product catalog, but not all items have a 
product number. So, we often must inquire about them and obtain the product number. 
Additionally, you can see here that the bill of materials includes gaskets, bolts, and 
washers. It specifies which bolts to use and their sizes. This should all be similar to what I 
mentioned earlier regarding the fire hydrant. There should simply be a designated item, 
such as "fire hydrant," and all the small components it requires would be included in the 
order. I can't imagine Veitur receiving a bill of materials that is 100% accurate, but I can 
imagine that Veitur often receives bill of materials from external consultants that are 
significantly incorrect. 
Then there's the issue of the product catalog itself, which requires an update because there 
are no standardized names for the products. It's incredibly challenging to navigate. 
Do you always have the necessary information when creating an bill of material? If 
not, why not? 
==PAGE:173==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
162 
 
Not always. That could be improved. As I mentioned earlier, the product catalog needs to 
be thoroughly reviewed and not everyone can correctly decide on which bolts and seals 
should be used for all products. Therefore, I believe this should be packaged together as 
some sort of kit rather than individual bolts, seals, and screws that need to be selected for 
each product. It should be bundled together so that external consultants don't always have 
to remember which sizes of bolts and gaskets are associated with a particular product. 
Do you follow any standards in your work processes? 
We follow design guidelines provided by Veitur. 
Are those standards always followed? 
They are always followed. 
How do you ensure the accuracy of the bill of materials? 
We follow design standards from Veitur and review the design and bill of materials. 
How long does it take on average to create the bills of material? 
Creating the bill of materials typically takes around half a day to 2 days. 
Do you find it clever if the design had to be done within certain material constraints to 
only use standardized materials that would be easier to recycle if something went 
wrong? 
That's something we try to achieve. I aim to use standardized materials wherever possible. 
However, in reality, I sometimes come across situations where we need to make changes. 
The general rule is to use commonly used fittings and connections. For example, if I have 
two pipes with a slight angle difference of 12 degrees, I wouldn't use a 45-degree bend. I 
always strive to adhere to these standardized components whenever feasible, but it's not 
always possible. 
Communication 
How are your relations with other parties in the supply chain?  
We have the most communication with the project manager, but we have extensive 
communication with the designers at Veitur, especially regarding aspects like the bill of 
materials. Generally, this goes very well. 
What communication method is used? 
It varies, but in many projects, we have regular design meetings, which is always better. It 
is often decided to have kickoff meetings so that everyone can see each other. We also use 
phone calls and emails. 
Have you encountered problems with communication with parties within the supply 
chain?  
Communication is generally good. 
How do you feel about the transparency between you and people at Veitur? 
==PAGE:174==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
163 
 
Generally, it goes very well. However, when there are new individuals on the other side 
who are learning, guidance is needed. 
Is it common for you to not have sufficient data to design the bill of materials? 
No, usually not. However, finding specific items in the product catalog can be a different 
matter. 
Do you have information about which items are available in stock when creating the 
bill of materials in order to potentially reuse those materials? 
No, but we have a general idea of which standard items are commonly used and likely to be 
available. 
I have a strong sense that there are more than one product catalogs in use at Veitur. I first 
became aware of the product catalog when I was creating the bill of materials around the 
year 2000. 
Do you think it's a good idea to check what is available in stock in order to be able to 
use those items in the design? 
To some extent, we try to use standards, for example, not using a 53-degree bend unless 
absolutely necessary. It's challenging, but it's smart to consider the product catalog when 
designing. However, it's not possible to design solely based on what is available in stock. 
Waste 
How often does it happen that the bill of materials is incorrect? 
Yes, it happens sometimes. We don't always find out about it, but I just can't imagine 
anything else. 
 
Why does it happen? 
It's difficult to piece together items, as I mentioned earlier with the fire hydrant, for 
example with a designer not having practical field experience. They may not know which 
bolts, brackets, or pipes should accompany the design. The person who creates the bill of 
materials needs to be very conscientious and precise, otherwise it won't be accurate. 
 
How do you try to prevent it from happening? 
By having the right people who create the bill of materials and by thoroughly reviewing 
them.
