C.8 – Interview 8 
Interview 8: Efla (15. May 2023) (duration: 0:40:35) 
Personal 
What job do you do? 
I work as a water supply and geotechnical designer at Efla. 
How would you describe that job?  
I work with ideas that have been developed to varying degrees, where a conventional 
definition of the project might be a new neighborhood that should be connected to water. 
That includes hot water, cold water, and wastewater. I go through a process of needs 
analysis to determine the best locations for the pipes, how to best link them, and the impact 
it has on the surrounding neighborhoods. I follow these projects from the initial stages all 
the way to the tendering process, where I hand it over. As part of that process, I create bills 
of materials for both hot and cold water, which is not typically done for wastewater as the 
contractor usually handles the materials. 
What role do you play in Veitur’s projects?  
I am responsible for creating the design and bills of materials for Veitur's projects. 
What are the main challenges you face in your work? 
The main challenges are essentially the needs analysis since the infrastructure layout can 
change while I'm designing, which affects the prerequisites. Challenges can also arise in 
material matters when there are changes in the sizes of buildings that are being built. The 
prerequisites can change in relation to the size and complexity of the pipes. 
Another challenge is ensuring that when changes occur, relevant information is 
communicated to all involved parties. This has happened to some extent, where people 
have made changes to drawings and forgotten to update the bills of materials, which can 
have serious consequences. Materials may have been ordered and if, for example, a specific 
bend is missing, which Veitur doesn't have in stock, it can delay the project once it reaches 
the execution phase. 
Process improvements 
Can you go step by step through the process involved in your work? 
I start with the model once I have established all the prerequisites regarding the selection of 
sizes for the pipes. Then I draw up the model with all the units that should be present and 
present it to the people who manage the system to confirm how they want the entire system 
to be. Once the nail-down design is complete, I create a bill of materials based on the 
design, which is shown on drawings or on an Excel file that is sent to the project manager. 
It is reviewed, and if the review indicates that something needs to be changed, I go over the 
bill of materials again. These lists are then uploaded into the DMM system for purchasing 
and material allocation. The tendering documents are then sent to the project manager, who 
takes it from there. 
Is there anything in the process that could be done better? 
==PAGE:176==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
165 
 
I believe there should be someone who is well-versed in the materials, with good 
knowledge of the material aspects, who receives the drawings and bills of materials for 
review at Veitur. I know that as designers, we have varying levels of knowledge about 
materials, so there should be someone who knows the material well and reviews the lists. 
Of course, people should do things correctly, but the fact is that individuals have different 
levels of knowledge in this area. Not all reviewers are the most qualified people to review 
bills of materials, and it would be beneficial to have someone with hands-on experience in 
working with the materials being used. Few reviewers have experience working with the 
materials in the field, and as a result, there are various aspects that individuals may not fully 
understand when ordering materials. 
Another option would be if Veitur stopped acquiring material for the projects and 
transferred that responsibility to the contractors. In that case, only the drawings would be 
provided, and they would work from there. 
Do you always have the necessary information when creating an bill of material? If 
not, why not? 
Yes and no. It actually depends on the department within Veitur. If we are dealing with the 
district heating system, it is generally much simpler than when dealing with the cold-water 
supply system. The cold-water supply system requires detailed specifications for bolts and 
fittings, and there are significantly more components involved in cold water projects 
compared to hot water projects that need to be taken into account. Additionally, there may 
be multiple material options that essentially serve the same purpose. In general, the district 
heating system commonly uses the same steel fittings, and there are less options in material 
selection. 
Once the design is complete, there are many variables that can change. Some individuals 
may be insistent on using specific materials, and naturally, we are designing something that 
goes underground, where not everything is visible. There could be archaeological findings 
or obstacles that need to be bypassed, potentially causing changes after the projects start 
date. It may happen that suddenly additional bends are required that were not initially 
ordered, which can cause complications and delays. We try to anticipate things as best as 
we can, but unexpected factors can arise. 
Do you follow any standards in your work processes? 
The design guidelines provided by Veitur serve as the starting point for how we should 
deliver the data, how it should appear, how the drawings should look, and so on. However, 
the design itself is defined by European standards, which include certain aspects that we 
need to consider and design according to. They are requirements for our design. For the 
sewer system, we need to know what is required to maintain self-cleaning of the pipes. For 
the district heating system, we need to ensure proper insulation. And for the cold-water 
system, we need to consider pressure requirements. 
Are those standards always followed? 
Yes, always. 
How do you ensure the accuracy of the bill of materials? 
==PAGE:177==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
166 
 
It is primarily done through review. We always review our own work and cross-reference it 
with the drawings. Then there is usually another internal review in most cases before the 
data is finally approved for release to the customer, which is Veitur. Within Veitur, there is 
a third level of review. However, despite all of this, some mistakes can still slip through. I 
believe it's simply because we overlook certain details or changes that occur, and in some 
cases, it's just due to lack of knowledge. 
How long does it take on average to create the bills of material? 
It depends on the size of the project. It takes less time to create it for a hot water project 
compared to a cold-water project because there are generally more components involved in 
cold-water projects. If we take a simple street as an example, it would take around 2 to 4 
hours. 
Do you find it clever if the design had to be done within certain material constraints to 
only use standardized materials that would be easier to recycle if something went 
wrong? 
This varies depending on the designers and how they approach it. I always work according 
to standards and thus likely have to use more components to ensure compliance with the 
standards. However, I know others who prefer to choose what they think is best each time, 
which creates inconsistency among designers. So, yes, perhaps emphasizing that Veitur 
only uses standardized components and making it clear would be clever. It would be natural 
for Veitur to have such requirements. Non-standard materials sometimes cannot be reused 
between projects, if they don't fit in one project, it becomes difficult to utilize them in 
another project. So, it would definitely help if you did that. It has not been a problem for 
me since I worked for Veitur before and struggled with using non-standard materials, and I 
know the complexity that can follow if non-standardized material is used. The fact is that 
you never know for sure if you can use a specific bend at a certain location until the 
excavation is done. 
Communication 
How are your relations with other parties in the supply chain?  
Usually, I am in direct contact with the project manager, and I also take care of monitoring 
during the execution time and visiting the worksite. So, sometimes communicate with the 
contractors as well. 
What communication method is used? 
Most often, it's through emails or simply meeting at the worksite. 
Have you encountered problems with communication with parties within the supply 
chain? 
That doesn't happen to me, but it might be because I have direct phone numbers for many 
people at Veitur since I previously worked there. So, I can quickly get responses. However, 
I can imagine that for those who are not familiar with all the people, there could be delays. 
How do you feel about the transparency between you and people at Veitur? 
The product catalog could definitely be better because currently it's an Excel file that we 
have to request, and I don't think it's accessible anywhere online as it currently stands. So, 
==PAGE:178==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
167 
 
it's not guaranteed that all designers have the latest version of the product catalog, which 
poses a certain risk. It could be simpler and better. We can see tendering documents on 
Veitur's website, so it would be possible to have the latest version of the product catalog 
there as well, but just remove the prices so that it's not visible. It would be very helpful to 
have this centralized and accessible. 
Is it common for you to not have sufficient data to design the bill of materials? 
It's actually part of the design process regarding information gathering because you don't 
start creating the bill of materials until the design is complete. Information regarding design 
assumptions is often unclear, but it's the designer's job to inquire and gather the necessary 
details to finalize the design. Additionally, it helps a lot to visit the worksite, talk to 
contractors, and interact with property owners if there is any work that needs to go through 
someone’s property. Information is not always perfect when starting a project, and 
sometimes you need to spend time searching for it, but I think it's just natural in such 
dynamic work. 
Do you have information about which items are available in stock when creating the 
bill of materials in order to potentially reuse those materials? 
We receive the product catalog as an Excel list, which can be outdated, so you don't know 
if some of the items in there are no longer available. So, no, I don't really have a good 
overview of what is in stock in terms of using old material. It can also change what type of 
material is desired, and then it can be difficult to use old materials that may not meet new 
standards. 
Do you think it's a good idea to check what is available in stock in order to be able to 
use those items in the design? 
I'm not sure. Projects are numerous and varied, with specific assumptions on how, for 
example, bends are used, where joints are placed, and so on. But yes, it would certainly be 
good to see what is available in order to make slight changes to the design and be able to 
use existing materials. However, I doubt that designers would realistically approach the 
product catalog in that way. I believe that usually only what is needed is recorded unless 
there are clear instructions from Veitur for something else. 
Waste 
How often does it happen that the bill of materials is incorrect? 
I'm not fully aware of that because I usually finish my involvement in the projects on the 
tendering day, but I do occasionally follow up on projects as well. I can't say from my own 
work experience that it has been a problem. It may have been more of an issue that 
something was missing rather than a great surplus that had been ordered. However, it's 
worth mentioning that I have never completed a project and never seen exactly how much 
material has been returned after the project is finished. But I know that contractors, for 
example, have taken all the materials from the warehouse at the beginning of the project 
and even lost some materials on site. It's something to consider, and it comes back to the 
question of whether it would be wise for the responsibility of acquiring the materials to lie 
with the contractor, and they would have to manage it. They might handle it better that 
way. Another aspect to look into is something I know has been problematic at Veitur, 
==PAGE:179==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
168 
 
which is the loss of materials in the warehouse. At some point, Veitur had its own storage, 
so that might be something to consider for better oversight. 
 
Why does it happen? 
There are various factors involved. It can be due to changes in the project that where 
information is not adequately spread, changes in the site that the external designer is 
unaware of even though they should always inquire about it. It can also be simply due to 
lack of knowledge on the part of those creating the bill of materials and those reviewing it. 
Additionally, there may be poor oversight despite the relevant expertise being present. 
 
How do you try to prevent it from happening? 
It's through review. What we have done is reviewing the bill of materials and try to identify 
any discrepancies based on the design. This process involves at least two, and in reality, 
three different parties conducting the review. The designer should review their own work, 
then there is secondary review from colleagues, and finally, there is the third review at 
Veitur. 
 
 
==PAGE:180==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
169 
 
C.9 – Interview 9 
Interview 9: Eimskip (26. May 2023) (duration: 00:51:16) 
Personal 
What job do you do? 
I am a service manager at Eimskip. I serve Reykjavík Energy, Shell, and Olís. 
How would you describe that job?  
I am responsible for communication between the suppliers, Eimskip, and the companies we 
serve. I ensure that everything runs smoothly, that every product arrives correctly and 
departs correctly, at the correct time.  
What role do you play in Veitur’s projects?  
I am Eimskip’s contact person with Veitur and make sure that every product arrives 
correctly and departs correctly, at the correct time. 
What are the main challenges you face in your work? 
The challenges are that a product might not be documented, even though it has arrived to 
the warehouse, ensuring that products are prepared for departure on time, and that a product 
gets delivered to the customer in a good condition. 
Process improvements 
Can you go step by step through the process that a product goes through at your 
company?  
Purchase order: 
First, a purchase order is created by Reykjavík Energy. The order is prepared by the 
suppliers, then it is sent to us. We receive the order, sign a receipt sheet that the product is 
received with a signature and a stamp. We take a photo of the receipt and upload it to a 
shared drive so that Reykjavík Energy's inventory management can see the receipt, both the 
time it arrived and the contents that arrived. 
Receiving: 
After that, we proceed with the conventional receiving process, where we divide, count, 
and carefully inspect the goods because we only accept products in a saleable condition. 
Then we book the respective products into our system, send notifications of any 
discrepancies or damage if necessary. Otherwise, we move on from the booking stage, and 
it is considered complete. At this point, the goods are ready, and Reykjavík Energy can pay 
the supplier, and only then can we release them for pickup, but not before. 
Storage: 
We place pallet tags on each individual item and store them in our system, either in a 
designated storage space or in a designated picking area, then we can track where the 
product is in our system and the product has received its storage space or is ready for 
picking. 
==PAGE:181==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
170 
 
Order: 
Then an order is created, and we gather the items, type it out of our system, then the 
product gets removed from our inventory and gets placed on the order. We print a shipping 
label and delivery note, which accompany the product. The product is either picked up by 
the customer or shipped out. Most often, it is picked up from our location. 
How do you feel about the current processes? 
It is good in many ways, but they regularly create follow-up orders. Sometimes there is an 
ongoing project, and we receive a receipt sheet that may be called 13031515, and then it's 
just order numbers A, B, C, D. Sometimes we have completed the entire alphabet because 
they keep ordering for a specific project. It's a real headache for us. Then we might be 
asked, "How many screws have you taken out of this order?" We have no idea which part 
of the order they are referring to and need to ask what day it was supposed to have arrived 
and look it up in the computer system. We then check and may see that it's order B that 
arrived in March, but they say that the order in March was accurate, and the missing item 
was supposed to arrive in August. These are all items for the same project that have been 
ordered at different times, so it's often difficult to keep track of exactly what has been 
delivered and what is still pending. This is the only company that works with Eimskip 
where this is allowed because usually companies create new orders each time, but these 
orders just have an endless lifespan. It becomes incredibly difficult to keep track of what 
has been delivered and what hasn't. Maybe one time we are expecting 10 items, but only 5 
arrive, and then the next month we expect 10 items but 15 arrive, so we need to be able to 
differentiate between all of this. 
What do you think could be done better? 
They at Reykjavík Energy don't think it would be better to have all the orders made as 
separate orders, even though it would greatly help us. But we also understand that they 
want all the orders for a specific project in the same location. However, it doesn't change 
the fact that we are just a warehouse. Here, goods are only ordered in and later ordered out. 
Another thing that I have commented on since I started here, and I've been here for almost 
5 years. Some contractor submits a plan of what is needed for the project. Let's say they 
need 2 bends, so we receive an order for 2 bends. Then the next one comes, and they also 
need 2 bends, so we receive another order for 2 bends. The supplier then receives orders for 
2 pieces, 2 pieces, 2 pieces, and the same product can go through the warehouse many 
times a week, in small quantities. We understand the need for some bends with a specific 
degree, but when it comes to just 1 box of clamps, those are routine products, and the 
minimum order should be a full pallet. These products should be available in stock, and 
there shouldn't be a need to constantly place small orders. What could be done better is not 
solely relying on the estimated need for a product calculated by a computer program but 
having better inventory management for these routine products. 
Also, we are not plumbers, we are just warehouse employees. Sometimes a pallet arrives 
with a variety of items, and we may not be entirely sure what they are. We then spend 
several hours sorting and figuring out what is what. It would be helpful if the items were 
better labeled for us, so that it would be easier to ensure that everything is correctly 
recorded in the system. 
Are there steps in the process that you feel are unnecessary and time-consuming? 
==PAGE:182==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
171 
 
Commonly used products could be ordered in larger quantities. Currently It's as if you were 
going to the grocery store three times a day and were always buying only what you feel like 
having at that exact moment. 
What do you think are the main bottlenecks in your processes? 
The bottle necks are perhaps all the small orders that are made instead of combining them 
and reducing into fewer bigger orders. Then we have been receiving goods that will be used 
in a project after a year later, so a product arrives in enormous quantities, and we need to 
store it for a whole year. That fills up the space inside and slows down the reception of 
other items. 
Do you follow any standards in your work processes? 
In the reception process, there is a receipt upon reception. We activate a reception 
supervision where we check the condition of the product and send an email to Reykjavík 
Energy if the invoice needs to be corrected or if there is a significant quantity discrepancy. 
For everything falling under storage, it's just standard in our computer system. We use the 
carrier system (pallet system) to locate the products in the warehouse. We move the pallets 
with carrier so that the product is always in its designated place. Each pallet has a carrier 
sticker, which displays the booking number of the product. Here, it is important to ensure 
that the product is not moved from the area where the label has been documented to prevent 
it from getting lost. 
Then comes the ordering process, where standardized information is required, such as the 
quantity, who picks up the product  or the delivery location. 
Finally, there is the picking process, a product is picked be standard picking paths, it is 
standardized how we prepare the products, we always wrap them in plastic or place them in 
a box. 
Are those standards always followed? 
Yes, always. 
What do you do today to constantly try to improve your work processes? 
We are constantly improving our work processes. For example, two years ago, we made 
significant investments, we replaced the entire rack system, repaired all the floors to 
improve utilization and accessibility to products in the aisles. We also upgraded the heating 
system in the warehouse to maintain a more stable temperature. However, these changes 
primarily affect the products stored inside the warehouse and not those stored outside. 
What tools and software do you rely on when it comes to inventory management? 
We have our warehousing system called MLS, and there are computers throughout the 
entire facility, including computers and scanners on all the forklifts. All employees are 
connected a computer through the warehousing system. This system is somewhat old-
fashioned but still works well due to its simplicity. You simply scan the numbers, and it's 
easy to learn. 
 
How is that system updated? 
==PAGE:183==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
172 
 
Both manual input and barcode scanners are used. We can scan the products that arrive 
with barcodes. We don’t do that with the products from Reykjavík Energy because only 
about 5% of the products for them have barcodes. It would, of course, be much more 
convenient to have barcodes on all the products. 
In your service agreement, it states that FIFO(First in first out) is the standard unless 
otherwise requested. Do you always manage to implement FIFO or are there any 
obstacles regarding accessibility or the arrangement of items that hinder its usage? 
This is actually a two-part answer. Inside the warehouse, it works very well to use FIFO, as 
the computer system guides you. However, we encounter difficulties with the pipes and 
tubes stored outside. Often, there are pipes on the ground, and when a new order arrives 
with similar pipes, they are placed on top of the existing ones to keep them in the same 
location. Additionally, there is limited space available. This means that to access the oldest 
pipes, one would have to remove all the newer ones, which can be time-consuming and 
none of the people coming to pick up the products have the patience to wait that long. 
Moreover, if the next shipment of pipes arrives tomorrow, what can we do? We simply add 
them to the pile. Unfortunately, we are unable to fully comply with FIFO for the pipes and 
tubes stored outside. 
Are there any inventory management issues that you believe could be improved? 
It could be possible to increase the standard order quantity for routine products. 
Additionally, there might be cases where orders are placed too early for projects that will 
take place many months later. 
Furthermore, the product catalog could be made more visible to those responsible for 
ordering, in order to utilize the existing inventory of older items that are available. 
communication 
How are your relations with other parties in the supply chain at Veitur or Reykjavík 
Energy?  
We are in the closest communication with the purchasing department, almost exclusively. 
We only interact with others if something has gone wrong and needs to be addressed. 
 
What communication method is used? 
We use email a lot but we also just use the phone. 
Have you encountered problems with communication with parties within the supply 
chain? 
Not really, of course, there are instances where it takes a while to get responses, and 
sometimes I have to send reminders, but I do that myself, so I'm not sure if it's worth 
mentioning. It's just human nature, it happens occasionally. 
How do you feel about the transparency between the different parties in the process? 
It is not good enough, we have for example no knowledge of what's coming into the 
warehouse, it's just a surprise when some products arrive. I don't even know what's going to 
arrive later today. 
==PAGE:184==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
173 
 
Have you had any problems with the transparency? 
Yes, repeatedly. Earlier, for example, we received a large batch of 6-meter pipes. It's good 
that there was a large order at once like I mentioned before, but it would have also been 
nice to receive an email this morning or yesterday, letting us know that we should expect a 
huge shipment of pipes. Then, perhaps, we would have moved the older inventory this 
morning, cleaned the area, brought in the new material, placed it at the back, and put the 
older items in the front so they would be used first. But we received no notification, so the 
new items were simply placed in front of the older ones, preventing us from using FIFO. 
There should be more information flow about what's coming into our warehouse, especially 
when there are large quantities of big items. That way, we could prepare the storage space 
and ensure that FIFO is followed. 
What system do you use to manage the inventory? 
Our program called MLS. 
Is this a program that the purchasing department at Reykjavík Energy/Veitur 
has access to and can view before they place orders for materials? 
They don't have access to our program, but their Unit4 program retrieves data from us. So, 
everything we do is reflected in their program after a few minutes. 
How long has Reykjavík Energy had access to this data? 
I'm not sure, I've been working here for 5 years, and it has always been like that. 
Waste 
What do you think is the biggest waste in your process? (Overproduction, waiting 
time, transportation, overprocessing, inventory, motion, defects or underutilized 
skills). 
The biggest waste is actually many small packages that arrive with the same products again 
and again instead of a whole pallet arriving. 
Is it common for products to arrive at the warehouse and sit there for a long time? 
Yes, I believe the main reason for that is changes in projects. 
What is the average time for products to stay in the warehouse? 
I would estimate around 8 months. Some items stay for a longer period while others for a 
shorter one. 
Does it sometimes happen that products that have been stored for a long time start to 
deteriorate? 
Yes, it does happen. There are also many products that simply become outdated, especially 
electronic products. There's a lot of products here that I know have become outdated 
because it's 3G, but now there's 4G and even 5G. Then there are the pipes stored outside, 
and I suspect that often these pipes that have been sitting with us for a long time are 
impractical to use. But if they don't meet certain standards due to minor damage to the 
==PAGE:185==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
174 
 
insulation, they can often be repaired. It just costs money and takes time. However, when 
water settles inside the steel pipes, the metal can start to deteriorate. 
Are products often disposed of 
It rarely happens, but it should definitely happen more often. 
How is the organization in the warehouse? 
The organization is such that we store products based on their picking path, weight of the 
product, and how frequently they are picked up. Different sizes of pallets get stored in 
different sized racks and we have shelves at different heights to maximize space utilization. 
We ensure that each product fits optimally. When a shipment arrives, we try to combine the 
products on the available shelves. I don't have 30 shelves with only a few items on each 
one, we try to combine products on each shelf. 
Has clutter hindered access to materials that needed to be accessed? 
Yes, it has happened, in such cases it's either relocated or the person has to wait for a few 
days while we sort it out. But it's not clutter per se, rather it's products that arrived 
unexpectedly and we were unaware of their arrival. In such cases, they may be temporarily 
placed somewhere until we find a proper space for them. 
How do you determine which products are stored inside, outside, or in containers? 
It mainly depends on the sensitivity of the products and whether they can be stored outside. 
It also depends on the size of the product. Unfortunately, many products are too large to be 
stored inside the warehouse, so we must store them outside. The quantity also plays a role, 
if we have a substantial amount of a product, I sometimes have to store it in containers 
outside. However, the bottom line is that these products can be stored outside. For example, 
electrical products are not stored outside. 
Appendix D: Gemba 
All business organizations operate around three main activities to earn a profit, these 
activities are development, production, and sales. A company cannot exist without these 
activities and gemba therefore represents the sites of these three activities. The Japanese 
word gemba can be translated to “the actual place” and it refers to the place where value is 
created, where the work is done, and where problems are both identified and solved. The 
gemba philosophy focuses on the importance of going to see the actual problem rather than 
relying on assumptions and passed-on information. Managers practicing gemba therefore 
go to the place where a problem is to see it for themselves to gain a better understanding of 
the problem. This process is called a gemba walk, the manager visits the workplace and 
both observes and interacts with the workers, this allows managers to identify where 
opportunities for improvements might be, something that they would likely not see if they 
had not performed the gemba walk (Imai, 2012).  
==PAGE:186==
 
Appendix 
Master Thesis 
175 
 
The gemba house is a representation of how an organization can look after adopting lean 
thinking to its operations. The gemba house has two main objectives, the first is 
maintenance and the second one is continuous improvement. Maintenance refers to 
following existing standards and maintaining the current situation and continuous 
improvement refers to continuously finding ways to improve those standards. Gemba 
managers usually focus on one of those objectives in order to improve the organization's 
quality, cost, and delivery (Imai, 2012).  
Figure XX shows how the gemba house looks and how organizations can keep their 
customers happy by providing a product or service to their customers on time and for a 
reasonable price.  
 
Figure 0.2: Gemba house (Imai, 2012)
